# Deferred-Anchor Registry

> The canonical source of truth for every `D-*` anchor cited in `src/` but
> deferred to a future cycle. The leading underscore sorts this file before
> the numbered plans in directory listings — call this out as the registry,
> not a plan. Per-plan §3.1 rows are still the preferred home for anchors
> whose feature area maps cleanly onto a plan; this file catches the orphans
> + cross-cutting anchors that don't belong to any single plan.
>
> **CI/pre-commit guard** (`tools/check-anchor-registry.{sh,ps1}`): every
> `D-*` identifier appearing in `src/` MUST resolve to a row in this file
> OR a citation in any `.plans/*.md`. Pre-fix this recurred TWICE
> (memory: "the same gap silent-failure caught for MULTI-PAGE-GOT").
> The guard makes the system enforce the discipline — same shape as the
> agnosticism veto + the `CallConv` static_assert.
>
> **V2-4.X / full-C ownership (2026-06-10):** the C-language-feature deferral
> CLUSTER — modulo codegen (`D-CSUBSET-MOD-OP-CODEGEN`, …), primitive widths
> (`D-LANG-PLATFORM-DEPENDENT-PRIMITIVE-WIDTH`), linkage/visibility syntax
> (`D-CSUBSET-LINKAGE-VISIBILITY-SYNTAX`, `D-DECL-PREFIX-STRIP-SHARED-HELPER`),
> rodata aggregates (`D-LK4-RODATA-PRODUCER-NONSTRING-ARRAY`), non-main implicit
> return (`D-LK10-ENTRY-MAIN-IMPLICIT-RETURN` — the OPEN non-main successor row,
> cross-ref `D-CSUBSET-ENTRY-NAME-SPLIT`), variadic FFI
> (`D-FFI-DESCRIPTOR-VARIADIC-SIGNATURE`), the apple-arm64 ABI divergence
> (`D-FF3-APPLE-ARM64-ABI-DIVERGENCE`), and peers — is now OWNED by **stepper
> V2-4.X / [`23-full-c-plan`](./23-full-c-plan%20-%20tbd.md)** (c-subset → full
> C23). Each closes inside the relevant FC phase (see the plan §3.1).
>
> **NOT in this cluster — already shipped, do NOT re-claim as new FC work**
> (caught by the 2026-06-10 plan-lock accuracy review). Two genuinely-CLOSED
> anchors: `D-CSUBSET-DIVISION-OP-CODEGEN` (✅ 2026-06-04 — signed division shipped;
> the modulo successor `D-CSUBSET-MOD-OP-CODEGEN` ✅ since closed too — FC1 cycle 1, 2026-06-10, above) and `D-FFI-EXTERN-CALL-DISPATCH`
> (✅ 2026-06-08 — direct-plt/indirect-slot dispatch shipped; the OPEN variadic concern
> is `D-FFI-DESCRIPTOR-VARIADIC-SIGNATURE`, above). PLUS one closed FEATURE with no
> anchor row: the `main` implicit-return-0 (shipped 2026-06-02, live in
> `c-subset.lang.json`, config-only) — the anchor `D-LK10-ENTRY-MAIN-IMPLICIT-RETURN`
> itself remains the still-OPEN non-main successor (above), NOT a closed item. The
> full-C arc supersedes each predecessor with its named successor, never by reopening it.
>
> New full-C exotic-tail exclusions land as `D-FULLC-*` rows as clusters ship.
> Individual rows are NOT rewritten here yet (the plan is the live map until a
> cycle actually closes the anchor).
>
> **Schema (one row per anchor)**:
> ```
> | Anchor | Trigger | Closing work | Cross-refs |
> ```
>
> When an anchor closes, replace its row's status with `✅ CLOSED <date>`
> and cite the commit/SymbolId. Don't delete the row — the audit trail is
> load-bearing for future regressions.
>
> **Authorization log — robustness sweep (2026-06-24, branch `feature/0-0-2-p14`):**
> the user authorized a "robustness sweep," which FIRED the trigger for three
> trigger-gated anchors and CLOSED them in one sweep (393/393 ctest, MSVC
> Release + MinGW): `D-CSUBSET-BLOCK-SCOPE-PROTOTYPE`,
> `D-CSUBSET-EXTERN-DEFINITION-MERGE`, and
> `D-SEMANTIC-ASSIGN-STMT-ASSIGNABILITY-BYPASS` (see their rows below). The
> sweep surfaced one new backlog row, `D-CSUBSET-TENTATIVE-DEFINITION-MERGE`
> (C 6.9.2 tentative definitions — still fail-loud, trigger-gated). [That backlog
> row was later ✅ CLOSED 2026-06-28 (p19 Cluster G c33) when the sqlite3.c
> re-probe fired its trigger — see its row below.]

## Anchor Index

| Anchor | Trigger | Closing work | Cross-refs |
|---|---|---|---|
| `D-PARSE-EXPR-DEPTH-GUARD` | ✅ **GUARD DELIVERED 2026-06-20 (FC13 hardening cycle); CAP RAISED 16→256 on 2026-06-20 (FC13 cycle 2) once both cap-raise blockers (`D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK` + `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC`) closed — the cap is now a real SEMANTIC limit, not a host-stack artifact (parse is O(N) + the frontend's deep recursion [CU build + `analyze`] runs on a 64 MiB worker stack via `core/substrate/large_stack_call`). The "lowered to 16" note below is HISTORICAL.** The Pratt-walker expression-depth guard (`ParserConfig::maxExpressionDepth`, enforced at the single chokepoint `parseExpressionAt` in `src/analysis/syntactic/parser.cpp`) was a `fatal()`/`std::abort()` on overflow, and its cap (256) was ~10x too high for the host C++ stack: the heaviest path (the paren atom re-entry `parsePrimary->parseUntilFrameDepth->stepOnce->walkExpression->parseExpressionAt`) overflows a Windows ~1 MB Debug stack at depth ~25 — BEFORE the guard could fire — so deeply-nested input RAW-crashed (rc 127) or hung. **DELIVERED:** (1) the `fatal()` is now a POSITIONED `P_ExpressionTooDeep` (0x0018) at the offending token + graceful RECOVERY (`recoverExpressionTooDeep_`: emit-once + Error leaf via `panicRecover` + unwind), never an abort/overflow; (2) the default cap lowered 256→16 so the guard fires with comfortable margin below the Debug paren overflow (~25) while still admitting realistic hand-written C nesting (≤15 deep). STEP-1 empirical finding: (B) on-path (NOT a bypass) — `expressionDepth` DOES grow per nesting level; the cap was simply unreachable before the stack blew. **CAP-RAISE follow-up → `D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK`:** EXPLORED this cycle and found INSUFFICIENT — a parser-only large-stack worker thread does NOT enable a higher cap, because stage markers localized the ~25-level overflow DOWNSTREAM of the parser (semantic `analyze` / HIR-MIR lowering recurse over the expr tree on the host's MAIN ~1 MB stack); raising the cap needs the downstream stages deep-safe (`D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK`) AND the speculative cost bounded (`D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC`). **SECOND follow-up (distinct, pre-existing) — c-subset speculative-operand O(N²):** the depth guard eliminates the CRASH, but on PATHOLOGICALLY deep parens the c-subset full parse is SLOW (CLI @ cap=16: depth 100 ~2s, 150-200 ~12s, 250+ >25s) because the `operand` rule is `speculative:true` (compoundLiteral/cast/paren disambiguation, lookahead 64 = 1024-token probe budget): each of the cap-many paren levels re-probes the deep tail, and nested speculation (`maxSpeculationDepth=8`) rollback-re-parses it. This is INDEPENDENT of the cap (cap=8 still times out @ depth 1000) and of THIS fix (pre-fix the deep parens crashed in Pratt recursion before the speculation finished; the fix EXPOSES the speculation cost, it does not cause it). A NON-speculative grammar (`kParenSchema`) parses 1000 parens in ~10ms — the headline unit test pins exactly that (the GUARD mechanism, isolated from c-subset speculation). The fix is a speculation-engine / grammar concern (memoize probe results, or bound speculation by expression depth), NOT the depth guard. Note: only manifests on ALREADY-INVALID input (depth > cap); valid C nests ≤4 in the entire corpus. Tests: `PrattWalker.{ExceedingMaxExpressionDepthDiagnosesAndRecovers (lowered-cap structural pin), DeeplyNestedParensDiagnoseAtDefaultCapWithoutCrashing (1000 parens @ default cap → positioned diag, no rc-127), DeepPrefixChainDiagnosesAndRecovers, DeepTernaryChainDiagnosesAndRecovers}` (test_pratt_walker.cpp) PLUS the c-subset end-to-end golden pin `tests/corpus/diagnostics/c-subset/expression_too_deeply_nested.c` (real frontend → `P_ExpressionTooDeep 1:41-1:42` golden, the exact code+position at the 17th paren where cap=16 trips). | (guard delivered; cap-raise → the 2 dedicated anchors) | plan 05 (PA2 walker); `D-PP-FATAL-HALTS-PARSE` (sibling); `D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK` + `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC` |
| `D-PP-FATAL-HALTS-PARSE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-20 (FC13 hardening cycle).** The compilation-unit PP branch (`compilation_unit.cpp` `parseAndAdd_`) parsed UNCONDITIONALLY even when a FATAL preprocessor backstop had TRUNCATED the synthesized stream (the >256 macro-expansion-nesting guard or the include-nesting guard), feeding the truncated tokens to the parser — producing an inscrutable secondary cascade / hang on top of the real PP cause. **CLOSED:** added `PreprocessResult::fatal` (set ONLY by the two stream-TRUNCATING backstops: `MacroExpander::truncated_` at the >256 guard, `SynthBuilder::fatal` ref-threaded through the recursive include builders at the include-depth guard); the CU gate now keys on `pp.fatal` and, when true, feeds the parser an EOF-ONLY stream — yielding a minimal well-formed tree that STILL carries the (remapped) PP diagnostics, halting the parse before the cascade. Crucially the gate is NARROW: a RECOVERABLE PP error (missing `#include` file, malformed directive, redefinition) or a folded LEXER error leaves the stream INTACT and the parser STILL runs (an earlier `diagnostics->hasErrors()` gate was too broad — it swallowed the rest of a file on an unresolved `#include`; caught by `HirLoweringCSubset.IncludeDirectiveIsSkippedNotFailed` + the FFI ingest tests). Tests: `CompilationUnitPPGate.{FatalMacroNestingTruncationGatesParser, OrdinaryMacroCompileIsNotGated, UnresolvedIncludeStillParsesRestOfFile}` (test_compilation_unit.cpp). | (closed) | `D-PARSE-EXPR-DEPTH-GUARD` (sibling); plan 05; FC13 |
| `D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-20 (FC13 cycle 2 — deep-expression-nesting end-to-end).** Built the standard compiler facility for deep recursion: `src/core/substrate/large_stack_call.{hpp,cpp}` — `runOnLargeStack(stackBytes, fn)` runs `fn` on a dedicated worker thread with a `stackBytes`-RESERVE stack, JOINs (synchronous — no concurrency), and re-throws any exception `fn` threw (captured into `std::exception_ptr` on the worker, rethrown on the joiner; never escapes the entry → no `std::terminate`); value-returning convenience `callOnLargeStack`; `kDeepRecursionStackBytes = 64 MiB` (cap 256 × ~40 KB/level ≈ 10 MB, lazily-committed reserve costs ~nothing). FAIL-LOUD (`std::abort` + stderr) on every thread-API failure AND caller bug (empty `fn`, `stackBytes==0`, Windows `stackBytes > UINT_MAX` — reject, never truncate the 32-bit `_beginthreadex` arg). Windows arm = `_beginthreadex` + `STACK_SIZE_PARAM_IS_A_RESERVATION` + `WaitForSingleObject`/`CloseHandle`; POSIX arm = `pthread_attr_setstacksize`/`pthread_create`/`pthread_join` (CI-verified — no `find_package(Threads)`, raw symbols resolve as `std::thread`'s do). AGNOSTIC: pure host/OS utility, names no language/CPU/format; the `_WIN32`/POSIX `#ifdef` is host-portability. Self-test `tests/core/substrate/test_large_stack_call.cpp` (RunsTheCallable; RethrowsEscapedException value-preserving; ProvidesStackForDeepRecursion = ~1000 frames × `volatile char[8192]` ≈ 8 MB that the default stack can't hold). **KEY EMPIRICAL CORRECTION of the localization below:** wrapping JUST `analyze` was INSUFFICIENT — stage markers in the full c-subset→PE-exec pipeline showed the analyze-wrap lifted the DOWNSTREAM ceiling well past 25 (n=100..180 compile + run clean), but at the raised cap (256) a NEW overflow appeared UPSTREAM: the **CU build (parse / preprocess / type-name oracle)** in `Program::compileFiles`/`compileUnits` (`UnitBuilder::addFile`→`finish`) recurses building the expression tree and overflows the host main stack at ~n=185 (Debug-MSVC) — the low cap (16) had MASKED it (the guard fired at 16, no deep tree was ever built). So the CU build, `analyze`, AND the BUILD-half `buildCuMir` (HIR + MIR) are ALL wrapped on the 64 MiB stack: `analyze` via a file-static `analyzeImpl` + a thin public `analyze` (`callOnLargeStack(kDeepRecursionStackBytes, …)`); the two CU-build sites in `program.cpp` via `callOnLargeStack` returning the `CompilationUnit`. The BUILD half `buildCuMir` (= analyze + CST->HIR + HIR->MIR) is wrapped via a file-static `buildCuMirImpl` + a thin `buildCuMir` (`compile_pipeline.cpp`). **THIRD incompleteness, independent-audit-caught (this cycle's dss-audit):** wrapping JUST parse + analyze was STILL insufficient — CST->HIR (`cst_to_hir.cpp` `lowerExpr`/`lowerOperand`) and HIR->MIR (`hir_to_mir.cpp` `lowerExpr`) ALSO recurse one host-stack frame per nesting level, running inline on the MAIN thread inside `buildCuMir` AFTER `analyze`'s worker has joined; so a valid 41..256-deep expression that parsed + analyzed could still overflow downstream (it HAPPENED to fit at n<=250 on Debug-MSVC, but that is host/frame-size luck, NOT a guarantee — exactly the uncontrolled-margin the wrap removes). FIXED by the `buildCuMir` wrap (analyze nests as a benign inner worker; peak live-deep stack ~10 MB << 64 MiB). Only the LOWER half (MIR->LIR->codegen->link, `lowerMirModuleToAssembly`) genuinely needs no wrap — it iterates a FLAT SSA arena (`mir.hpp`), NOT a tree, so it is non-recursive in nesting depth (audit-confirmed). Cap raised 16→**256** (`parser.hpp`); now a real SEMANTIC limit (parse O(N) via `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC`'s LL(k) prune + analyze/parse on the big stack), so deep-but-legal C compiles end-to-end and only pathological nesting past 256 trips the positioned `P_ExpressionTooDeep` guard. **Verified:** n=100/200/250 c-subset compile (rc 0, ~0.2s) + run (exit 0); n=300 fails LOUD fast (`P0018`, no hang/crash). Test harnesses that build deep CUs unwrapped were also routed onto the facility (the corpus harness `test_diagnostic_corpus.cpp` for the >256-paren fixture; the headline `PrattWalker.DeeplyNestedParensDiagnoseAtDefaultCapWithoutCrashing` 1000-paren pin at the raised default cap) and the duplicate local `runOnLargeStack` in `test_parser_speculation.cpp` was CONSOLIDATED onto the substrate facility (Win32 `CreateThread` trampoline deleted). Re-added + DEEPENED the runnable witness `examples/c-subset/deeply_nested_expression` (200 nested parens → exit 7; PE-windows + ELF-linux) — a VALID deep expression that compiles AND runs through the WHOLE BUILD+LOWER pipeline at 200 nesting levels (closes the audit's M2: the prior 40-paren example + the guard-tripping fixtures never lowered a valid deep tree past HIR). Corpus fixture `expression_too_deeply_nested.c` regenerated to 300 parens (golden `P_ExpressionTooDeep 1:281-1:282` + `P_UnexpectedToken 1:582-1:583`). 335 ctest green. — *Original localization (audit trail):* Frontend stages DOWNSTREAM of the parser (semantic `analyze`, HIR/MIR lowering) recurse over the expression tree on the host's MAIN ~1 MB stack (Windows) and OVERFLOW at ~25 nested levels (rc-127, NO diagnostic), independent of the parser (which handles deeper). This is what caps `ParserConfig::maxExpressionDepth` at 16. Localized empirically via stage markers in `program.cpp` `runCusToTargets` (parse completes; the crash is inside `compileOneTarget`→`analyze`). A parser-only large-stack worker thread was EXPLORED this cycle and does NOT help (the crash is downstream). [SUPERSEDED: the crash was ALSO upstream in the CU build once the cap allowed a deep tree — see the close note above.] | (closed — `large_stack_call` substrate; CU build + `analyze` + BUILD-half `buildCuMir` [HIR/MIR] on a 64 MiB worker stack; cap 16→256) | `D-PARSE-EXPR-DEPTH-GUARD`; `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC`; `parser.hpp` maxExpressionDepth; `core/substrate/large_stack_call.hpp` |
| `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-20 — fixed by a config-driven LL(k) predictive prune (the `Correct direction (b)` below, IMPLEMENTED): `computePredictivePrefixes` (grammar_schema_json.cpp) precomputes a per-rule FIRST_k `predictivePrefix` at schema-load (the leading single-token run + the first variable element's FIRST set, STOPPING before a NULLABLE stop element so each recorded offset is an EXACT admissible-token set ⇒ a SOUND over-approximation); `predictivePrefixPrunes` (parser.cpp) prunes a speculative candidate when an OBSERVED next-token is outside its prefix; a lone unguarded survivor DESCENDS DIRECTLY (no probe). `((` → castExpr/compoundLiteral pruned (token[+1]=`(` ∉ FIRST(castTypeRef)) ⇒ O(N); n=300 154s→0.17s (~1100×); the lone-`(Identifier)` ambiguity still speculates (binder triage unchanged). Agnostic (walks FIRST sets + the position table, names NO token) + config-driven (FIRST + the rule's `lookahead`); independent review-folded — nullable-stop soundness guard + contextual-keyword precondition → `D-PARSE-PREDICTIVE-PRUNE-CONTEXTUAL-KEYWORD` + synthetic RED-on-disable tests (`ParserSpeculation.{DeepNestCastVsParenIsLinear, PrunesFirstBranchAtOffsetOneAndDirectDescends, NullableStopElementDoesNotOverPrune}`); 333 ctest. A RESIDUAL mild wall-clock super-linearity in the deep parse itself was CHARACTERIZED 2026-06-22 and promoted to its own row `D-PARSE-DEEP-NEST-RECURSION-MEMORY` — a controlled flat-chain-vs-nested experiment PROVED the parse WORK is O(N) (the "TreeBuilder/arena bookkeeping" guess first sketched here is REFUTED: a flat `0+0+…+0` chain of equal node count parses with FLAT per-element cost), so the residual [measured ~exp 1.7, not the ~exp 1.2 first estimated] is a constant-factor cost of the N-deep HOST recursion (inferred BY ELIMINATION to be memory-hierarchy behavior — not directly cache-instrumented), bounded/moot under the 256 depth cap — LOW-priority / trigger-gated. — Original characterization (audit trail):** The c-subset `operand` rule is `speculative:true` (compoundLiteral/cast/paren cast-vs-paren disambiguation; lookahead 64 = 1024-token probe budget). Deeply-nested input parses SUPER-LINEARLY (O(N²)+) in depth — measured @ cap=16: depth 20 ~0s, 100 ~3s, 300 TIMES OUT (>40s) — so deep input HANGS before the depth guard can fail loud, even at a LOW cap (the speculation descends the deep tail at the early levels, before the guard depth is reached). INDEPENDENT of the cap (repro @ 16/64/256) and of the guard (a non-speculative `kParenSchema` parses 1000 parens in ~10ms). FIX ATTEMPT 1 FAILED 2026-06-20: a code-trace MIS-diagnosed the cost as O(depth) `SpeculationProbe` state-snapshots (walker `cursorStack_`/`wrapFrameFlags_`, builder `open_`/`scopes_`); the O(1) size-truncation fix had ZERO timing effect AND broke the general non-append-only `SchemaWalker::snapshot/restore` API (`core/test_schema_walker`) — REVERTED. **MEASURED root cause 2026-06-20 (instrumented counters, NOT a code-trace):** the O(N²) is PANIC-MODE RECOVERY running INSIDE doomed speculative `castExpr` probes — `panicInSpec == panicRecovers` (100% of panics are in-probe) and `panicScanTokens ≈ tokensAdvanced` (the parser advances tokens almost solely to panic-scan inside failing cast probes, then rolls them back). For `((((0))))` the `castExpr` probe (tried BEFORE `parenExpr` in the `operand` alt) fails at each inner `(` (castTypeRef can't start with `(`) and `panicRecover` scans forward to the end-of-expression sync point = O(min(N,64)) tokens × N levels. **FIX ATTEMPT 2 FAILED 2026-06-20:** suppressing the panic-scan inside probes (`panicRecover` early-return when `speculationDepth > 0`) was correctness-safe (ctest 333-green) but COUNTERPRODUCTIVE — deep input HUNG WORSE (n=100: ~3 s → timeout, NO diagnostic emitted): the panic-scan is LOAD-BEARING for the failing probe to TERMINATE / make forward progress, NOT pure waste. REVERTED. **Correct direction (UNTRIED — a real engine rework, not a one-liner):** a CHEAP fail-fast for the cast-probe mismatch that PRESERVES termination — either (a) dispatch-level: fail the probe immediately on a required-alt no-candidate while `speculationDepth > 0` (instead of routing through panic recovery), or (b) a k-token candidate prune at the `operand` AltChoice (don't ENTER the cast/compound-literal probe when the token after `(` cannot start `castTypeBase`); both must stay agnostic (FIRST-set / generic dispatch, no language identity) and must not break cast / compound-literal / sizeof / the binder-sketch commit triage. Only manifests on deeply-nested input (valid C nests ≤4 in the corpus). | (closed — LL(k) predictive prune, direction (b)) | `D-PARSE-EXPR-DEPTH-GUARD`; `D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK`; `D-PARSE-PREDICTIVE-PRUNE-CONTEXTUAL-KEYWORD`; `c-subset.lang.json` operand rule |
| `D-PARSE-PREDICTIVE-PRUNE-CONTEXTUAL-KEYWORD` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-23 (FC-deferral close-out cycle 13, branch p14).** Closing the end-to-end "a contextual keyword in a speculative candidate's fixed prefix parses correctly" needed BOTH a PRUNE half (the registry's prescribed fix) AND a deeper PROBE half (the build DISCOVERED it; the anchor did not scope it → §B-surfaced, user chose build-deep). **(1) PRUNE:** a loader-derived token-id-keyed `contextualKinds` set (`computeContextualKinds` in `grammar_schema_json.cpp`, from the per-`LexemeMeaning.contextual` flags) + an O(1) `GrammarSchema::isContextualKind(SchemaTokenId)` query; `predictivePrefixPrunes` (`parser.cpp`) now `continue`s at any offset whose OBSERVED token is contextual → the candidate survives the prune. **(2) PROBE (the crux the build exposed):** even surviving the prune, the candidate's speculative probe `recoverAt(P_UnexpectedToken)`'d — the TokenLeaf MATCH GATE in `stepOnce` tests the UN-demoted keyword kind (`effectiveKind` by design does not model demotion), so the token never reached the builder's `pushToken` contextual-demotion. FIX: the match gate now MIRRORS the builder's demotion (a contextual `tokKind` ∉ expected → treat as a match when `identifierKind` IS expected) and advances the PARSER's walker with the demoted `identifierKind`, keeping it in lockstep with the builder's walker (no spurious desync-latch trip → the probe commits). Both halves AGNOSTIC (config-derived `isContextualKind`; the demotion target REUSES the parser's EXISTING `identifierKind` — the schema's resolved `Identifier` token kind, IDENTICAL to the builder's demotion this mirrors → walker lockstep) — EMPTY `contextualKinds` for a non-contextual grammar ⇒ ZERO behavior change, the deep-nest O(N) prune win preserved. (Review-noted pre-existing residual `D-PARSE-IDENTIFIER-KIND-HARDCODED-VS-CONFIG`: the parser+builder resolve the demotion target via the literal name `"Identifier"` rather than the live `semantics.identifierToken`; latent — all shipped grammars declare `identifierToken: "Identifier"` so they coincide; trigger-gated, NOT introduced here.) 374 ctest green, ZERO regression incl. **tsql** (the `reservedWordPolicy: contextual` grammar where the gate CAN fire). Pinned RED-on-disable with BOTH halves toggled INDEPENDENTLY (prune-skip off → caseId pruned; match-gate off → caseId survives prune but probe rejected → replays wrong candidate) by the synthetic contextual-keyword speculative-alt schema in `test_parser_speculation.cpp`: `ParserSpeculation.{ContextualKeywordInSpeculativePrefixNotMispruned` (soft keyword `kw` in caseId's `[A,Identifier,;]` prefix demotes + commits + asserts the `P_ContextualKeywordResolution` demotion diagnostic fired)`, HardKeywordInSpeculativePrefixStillPruned` (negative control — a HARD keyword stays pruned; the fix doesn't over-broaden)`}`. RESIDUAL: none for this anchor. — *Original OPEN characterization (audit trail):* **registered 2026-06-20 (FC13 predictive-prune soundness fold).** The LL(k) speculative-alt PREDICTIVE PRUNE (`Parser::predictivePrefixPrunes`, the O(N) deep-nest lever that landed alongside `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC`) compares a candidate's exact per-offset FIRST_k prefix against the observed token's `effectiveKind`. `effectiveKind` DELIBERATELY does NOT model contextual-keyword demotion (`parser.cpp` ~L63 — a soft keyword keeps its KEYWORD kind here; demotion to Identifier happens later in the builder against the live cursor expectedSet + scope stack). So for a grammar with contextual keywords (`contextual: true` per entry, or grammar-wide `reservedWordPolicy: "contextual"` — e.g. tsql), at an offset whose admissible set holds the demotion target (Identifier) the prune could see the keyword kind, find it absent, and WRONGLY drop a candidate the demoted token would in fact match — a silent mis-parse. NOT live today: c-subset's speculative prefixes are all hard keywords / punctuation, and tsql's lone `nameOrCall` speculative alt discriminates at offset 1 on `(` / qualified-name punctuation, not on a soft-keyword Identifier slot — so no shipped speculative candidate puts a contextual keyword in its FIXED prefix. The precondition ("sound only for grammars with no contextual / scope-resolvable kind in a speculative candidate's fixed prefix") is DOCUMENTED prominently at both `Parser::predictivePrefixPrunes` and `computePredictivePrefixes`. A clean conservative fix is deferred because no token-id-keyed "is this kind contextual" query exists today — the `contextual` flag is per-`LexemeMeaning` (lexeme-string-keyed); only the grammar-wide `reservedWordPolicy()` lever is exposed, which would NOT cover a per-keyword `contextual: true` under a Strict policy. | Add an agnostic token-id-keyed "is this SchemaTokenId a contextual/scope-resolvable kind" query (derive a `contextualKinds` set in the loader from the `contextual` LexemeMeaning flags + `reservedWordPolicy`), then make `predictivePrefixPrunes` CONSERVATIVE — skip the prune at any offset whose OBSERVED token has a contextual/scope-resolvable kind (do not constrain that offset). Must stay agnostic (no token/language naming) and preserve the deep-nest O(N) win for non-contextual grammars. Pin with a synthetic contextual-keyword speculative-alt schema whose candidate prefix admits Identifier at offset ≥1 + a soft-keyword input (RED-on-disable: the un-skipped prune drops the valid candidate). Priority: **normal (trigger-gated — first contextual-keyword speculative-alt consumer with a soft keyword in a candidate's fixed prefix).** | `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC` (the prune this guards); `parser.cpp` `effectiveKind` / `peekSignificantKind`; `grammar_schema.hpp` `reservedWordPolicy` / `LexemeMeaning::contextual`; tsql `nameOrCall` |

Acknowledged: NOT a crash fix (already mitigated by the 64 MiB worker), NO production consumer — a robustness goal. Cap is RAISED not removed (`P_ExpressionTooDeep` backstop kept). — *Original characterization (audit trail):* **OPEN (trigger-gated) — registered 2026-06-22 (residual deep-expr parse super-linearity characterization cycle).** A deeply-nested expression like `((((0))))` parses with a residual MILD WALL-CLOCK super-linearity (measured ~exp 1.7, Debug, cap=4000 on a large-stack thread: depth 250 ≈23 ms → 500 ≈71 ms → 1000 ≈240 ms → 2000 ≈873 ms → 3000 ≈1897 ms; ns/level rises 93k→632k). DISTINCT from `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC` (the now-FIXED O(N²) cast-vs-paren panic-scan blowup — that made n=300 take 154 s; GONE, n=3000 is now 1.9 s); it is the SAME residual a sibling session flagged (matching ~exp-1.7). **ROOT CAUSE — decisively localized by a CONTROLLED experiment, not a code-trace:** deep `((((0))))` (host-recursion depth = N) vs a flat `0+0+…+0` left-assoc chain (recursion depth ~2, SAME O(N) node/token count, built ITERATIVELY by the Pratt climb). The FLAT chain is perfectly O(N) — ns/level FLAT at ~20.5 µs across 250→3000, node count exactly linear — while only the NESTED case grows. Both exercise the IDENTICAL shared machinery (TreeBuilder frame open/close, the node-arena `std::vector` GEOMETRIC growth, schema-walker advance), so the "TreeBuilder/arena bookkeeping" hypothesis from the QUADRATIC row is **REFUTED**. Exhaustive code reading confirms every per-level op on the direct-descent paren path is O(1) (operand AltChoice dispatch, `candidateBranches` over the fixed 6-branch set, the LL(k) `predictivePrefixPrunes` over the fixed prefix, `peekSignificantKind`, frame open/close, ALL `SchemaWalker` ops, `finish()` once) and the lone-survivor `parenExpr` DIRECT-DESCENDS with NO `SpeculationProbe`/checkpoint/snapshot (so the O(N²)-snapshot path is not taken). The residual is therefore NOT algorithmic (PROVEN: the flat control isolates the shared WORK as O(N)) — it is a constant-factor cost of the N-deep HOST recursion, attributed BY ELIMINATION (not directly cache-instrumented) to that recursion's memory-hierarchy behavior: the live C++ call stack ≈ N × {parseExpressionAt, parsePrimary, parseUntilFrameDepth, stepOnce, walkExpression} frames PLUS the strided unwind re-access of the depth-indexed `frames`/`frameRules`/`cursorStack`/`pendingChildren` vectors as the working set outgrows cache (the rising-not-constant local exponent ~1.6→1.9 is consistent with cache-tier transitions, not a clean algorithmic O(N²)). **BOUNDED / MOOT:** `ParserConfig::maxExpressionDepth` caps depth at 256 (`D-PARSE-EXPR-DEPTH-GUARD`; valid C nests ≤4 in the whole corpus; >256 FAILS LOUD via `P_ExpressionTooDeep`, never parses) AND the whole downstream frontend (semantic/HIR/MIR) is itself recursion-bound to the same 256 cap (`D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK`) — so the residual only appears in a synthetic cap-raised micro-benchmark, never in production. Pinned by `ParserSpeculation.FlatChainParseWorkIsLinear` (the O(N)-WORK regression guard) + the existing `DeepNestCastVsParenIsLinear` (the deep-path O(N²)-regression guard, whose generous 8× bound is explained by this residual). | Convert the recursive-descent EXPRESSION parser (`parseExpressionAt`/`parsePrimary`/`parseUntilFrameDepth` + the `walkExpression` re-entry) to an explicit heap worklist/stack so deep nesting carries no host-recursion memory cost — AND, for any END-TO-END benefit, do the same for the recursion-bound downstream passes (`D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK`'s semantic/HIR/MIR), since the 256 cap is set by THEM. Stay agnostic (no token/rule/language identity). Pin with a deep-nest wall-clock ratio the iterative form keeps ~linear. Priority: **normal (trigger-gated — fires only if a real consumer needs expressions nested beyond the 256 cap AND the cap is first lifted by an iterative frontend; NO in-cap benefit otherwise).** | `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC` (the O(N²) sibling this is the residual OF); `D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK` (the downstream recursion bound that sets the 256 cap); `D-PARSE-EXPR-DEPTH-GUARD` (the cap); `parser.cpp` `parseExpressionAt`; tests `FlatChainParseWorkIsLinear` + `DeepNestCastVsParenIsLinear` |

| `D-FC12A-VARIADIC-MEMORY-CLASS-STRUCT` | ✅ **SHIPPED 2026-06-20 (FC12a-struct-memory).** SysV x86_64 struct-by-value at the variadic boundary for the MEMORY-class (>16B) + register-exhaustion-split shapes. **§B (user 2026-06-20): Option C — a first-class BY-VALUE-AGGREGATE STACK-ARG carrier** (a prior "push eightbytes as ordinary operands" design was REJECTED — an audit proved it a SILENT MISCOMPILE: the operands land in FREE registers, not the stack). SysV §3.2.3/§3.5.7 requires a MEMORY-class aggregate AND a register-exhaustion-split InRegisters aggregate to be passed ENTIRELY in the outgoing overflow (stack) area UNCONDITIONALLY (even when arg registers are free), never split. The greedy register-then-overflow callconv had no per-arg force-to-stack lever, so the carrier IS the lever: a NEW MIR op `ByValueStackArg` (operand 0 = the `freshAggregateTemp` copy address via `lowerByteWiseCopy`, same as the by-ref arg; payload = aggregate byte size; result = pointer, threaded through) sits as ONE Call operand at the aggregate's left-to-right position. `mir_to_lir` lowers it to a `Reg` (the address — kept live by liveness/regalloc) immediately followed by a NEW `LirOperandKind::ByValueStackAgg` size marker (mirroring the leading-Reg + trailing-descriptor memory-operand convention). `lir_callconv` (BOTH `computeMaxOutgoingStackArgs` pre-scan AND the materialize placement loop, via the shared `byValueStackAggSlots` helper) places it at the next overflow offset(s) — reserving ceil(size/outgoingSlot) slots + byte-copying the temp into `[sp + shadowSpaceBytes + overflowIdx*outgoingSlotSize]` (caller-saved scratch GPR avoiding every carrier addr reg + the indirect callee + the count reg + every pending arg-move / FP-dup SOURCE register — the silent-arg-clobber avoid-set, the review-caught BLOCKER-3 fold: the byte-copies run BEFORE the register arg-moves read their sources, so the scratch must not be a live arg source; a blanket argGpr exclusion was REJECTED as over-broad — a dest-only argGpr is written by its own arg-move after the copy, so its transient clobber is dead). It consumes NO arg register (runGpr/runFpr NOT advanced; class counters NOT advanced) and does NOT inflate the SSE/AL count (the GPR-class address Reg fails the FPR test; the marker is non-Reg). CC-NEUTRAL by construction (the byte size is the only datum; the overflow geometry is config-driven) so the Win64 + AAPCS64 struct-vararg cycles REUSE this carrier. Caller routing (`hir_to_mir.cpp` Call arg loop): MEMORY-class ByReference → carrier; register-exhaustion split (`runGpr+numGp > gpSaveCount || runFpr+numFp > fpSaveCount`) → WHOLE struct to carrier. Callee `va_arg(>16B)` (`lowerVaArgAggregate`): an EARLY ByReference dispatch → the overflow-ONLY arm (addr = overflow_arg_area, bump roundUp(size, gpSlotBytes)), never the register-gather diamond (numGp=numFp=0 would make the atomic-fit trivially-true → gather ZERO pieces). Wall-3 (fixed >16B struct param in a variadic fn): the fail-loud removed — `receiveByValueParam`'s ByReference arm receives the hidden pointer as 1 GPR arg (counted in `currentFnFixedGpr_`), so the common case (1 GPR + ≤5 scalars ≤ 6) lowers cleanly. The 4 fail-loud pins inverted to SUCCESS + structural pins (carrier present; va_arg overflow dispatch = no ICmpUle pair; the BLOCKER-1 force-to-stack + BLOCKER-2 outgoing-area sizing LIR pins in `test_lir_callconv.cpp`, both red-on-disable verified). REMAINING (own cycles, REUSE this carrier): Win64 `D-FC12B-WIN64-STRUCT-VARARG`, AAPCS64 `D-FC12C-AAPCS64-HFA-STRUCT-VARARG`; the SEPARATE `D-FC12A-VARIADIC-OVERFLOW-FIXED-STACK-ARGS` (fixed params overflowing to the stack) stays OPEN. | (shipped) | `D-FC12A-VARIADIC-OVERFLOW-FIXED-STACK-ARGS`; `D-FC12B-WIN64-STRUCT-VARARG`; `D-FC12C-AAPCS64-HFA-STRUCT-VARARG`; `D-FC7-STRUCT-BY-VALUE-ARG-RETURN`; `D-FC12A-VARIADIC-CALLEE` |
| `D-FC12B-WIN64-VARIADIC-CALLEE` | ✅ **SHIPPED 2026-06-19 (FC12b).** **§B (user 2026-06-19): Option A — a closed `VaListStrategy` enum with the va_list TYPE DERIVED from the strategy, chosen over Option D (an explicit per-CC `vaListType` config field); derived avoids an unused-flexibility knob that must be kept consistent with the strategy. (Rejected extremes: a va_arg recipe-DSL, and a unified ptr-to-opaque-blob va_list — both break the bar.)** Microsoft x64 (ms_x64) variadic CALLEE support — `va_start`/`va_arg`/`va_end` for SCALAR + FP types, config-driven + source/target/linker-AGNOSTIC. The per-CC va_list TYPE + lowering STRATEGY is a NEW closed enum `VaListStrategy` (`aggregate_layout.hpp`, beside `AggregateClassKind`/`BitFieldStrategy` so the SEMANTIC va_list-type injection reads it without pulling the link/target substrate): `SysVRegisterSave` (FC12a, unchanged-but-now-strategy-tagged), `HomogeneousPointer` (Win64, this cycle), `Aapcs64DualCursor` (declared, fail-loud-until-FC12c). `VaListLayout` gains `strategy` (first field) + `namedArgSlotBytes`; `x86_64.target.json` ms_x64 declares `{"strategy":"homogeneous_pointer","namedArgSlotBytes":8}`. **BLOCKER-2 (va_list TYPE per ABI):** `analyze()` gains an `optional<VaListStrategy>` param threaded from the resolved CC (pipeline reads it where it reads `aggregateLayout`); the sema injection switches on it — SysV → `__va_list_tag[1]` (24B), Win64 → `char*` (8B), AAPCS64 → loud `S_VariadicCalleeUnsupported`. A wrong sizeof(va_list) would mis-size the `ap` local + corrupt the stack — pinned `sizeof(va_list)`==8 ms_x64 / 24 sysv. **BLOCKER-1 (no-shadow contiguous base):** Win64's named-arg HOME space (rcx/rdx/r8/r9 slots = the caller's shadow space) and the 5th+ stack args are CONTIGUOUS from `totalFrameSize + callPushBytes` (NO shadowSpaceBytes — adding it would skip the home and read past every named arg). A NEW MIR leaf `VaHomeArgAreaAddr` (payload = the slot-aligned named-arg count) + LIR `va_home_arg_area` op materializes to `lea [sp + totalFrameSize + callPushBytes + payload*outgoingSlotSize]`; the Win64 prologue spills the named int regs into the SAME base (spill-target == va_arg-read-target). HIR→MIR lowers va_start (Win64) to `Store(VaHomeArgAreaAddr, ap)`, va_arg to a LINEAR pointer bump (NO diamond: Load ap → Load T → Gep +namedArgSlotBytes → Store ap), va_end to nothing. **FP-dup (PART 5):** Win64 passes each FP vararg in BOTH the xmm AND the matching integer (home) reg; the callee reads va_arg(double) from the home GPR slot, so the CALLER duplicates each register-resident FP VARARG (operand past `fixedOperandCount`) into argGprs[slot] via a NEW dedicated opcode `movq_xmm_to_gpr` (`66 REX.W 0F 7E /r`; byte-pin `movq rdx, xmm1` = `66 48 0F 7E CA`). A dedicated opcode (not `movq_xclass`) because the encoding-variant guard keys only on (operandKinds, width) and cannot disambiguate the two MOVQ directions, and `movq_xclass` is consumed bidirectionally by Bitcast — overloading would force a silent miscompile on GPR→FPR Bitcast. Every va seam dispatches on `VaListStrategy` with a fail-loud default (no half-migrated site silently runs the SysV path on a Win64 layout). Run-witnessed on PE x86_64 (this Windows host): `examples/c-subset/varargs_win64_sum` (int+double varargs, anti-folded via a mutable-global seed). FAIL-LOUD: Win64 struct-by-value varargs (`D-FC12B-WIN64-STRUCT-VARARG`); Aapcs64 at every seam (FC12c). | (shipped) | `D-FC12B-WIN64-STRUCT-VARARG`; `D-FC12A-VARIADIC-CALLEE`; `D-FC7-STRUCT-BY-VALUE-ARG-RETURN`; `D-LANG-VARIADIC`; plan 23 FC12 |
| `D-FC12C-AAPCS64-VARIADIC-CALLEE` | ✅ **SHIPPED 2026-06-19 (FC12c).** AAPCS64 (ARM64-ELF) variadic CALLEE support — `va_start`/`va_arg`/`va_end` for SCALAR int+fp, config-driven + source/target/linker-AGNOSTIC, the THIRD `VaListStrategy` (`Aapcs64DualCursor`, beside SysVRegisterSave + HomogeneousPointer). `va_list = __va_list`, a typedef to the 5-field STRUCT DIRECTLY (NOT an array like SysV, NOT a pointer like Win64): `{void* __stack; void* __gr_top; void* __vr_top; int __gr_offs; int __vr_offs;}` (32B; sizeof pinned). Config = a `vaListLayout` block on `aapcs64` with the 5 field locators + GR/VR save geometry (gpSaveCount8/gpSlotBytes8/fpSaveCount8/fpSlotBytes16, regSaveAreaBytes()=192); the semantic injection + isVaList accept the struct shape for the strategy. **BLOCKER-1:** a NEW `fstur_q` opcode (STUR Qt,[Xn,#simm9], 128-bit, fixedWord `0x3C800000` — NOT `0x3C000000`=STURB which would spill 1 byte/FP slot → va_arg(double) garbage; byte-pin STUR Q0,[X1,#0]=`0x3C800020` + a disasm Imm9/MemBaseNoScale round-trip arm). The AAPCS64 prologue spills x0..x7 (GR block, 8B via the class GPR store) then v0..v7 (VR block, 16B via `fstur_q`) into the callee-local register-save-area at `vaRegSaveAreaOffset()`, ascending order. va_start inits the 5 fields: __gr_top=rsa+64, __vr_top=rsa+192, __stack=overflow base, __gr_offs=-(8-fixedGpr)*8, __vr_offs=-(8-fixedFpr)*16 (NEGATIVE i32 cursors). **BLOCKER-2:** va_arg's per-class diamond — Load the NEGATIVE class cursor, `ICmpSlt(offs,0)` (a reg slot remains while <0), reg arm: **SIGN-EXTEND the i32 cursor to i64 (SExt) BEFORE the byte Gep** (a 32-bit -40 zero-extended → 0xFFFFFFD8 ≈ +4 GiB wild addr → segfault), addr = `<gr|vr>_top + SExt(offs)`, bump by the slot stride; stack arm: addr = __stack, bump by gpSlotBytes=8 (the NSAA round-up quantum, even for a double); Phi the two → Load T. va_end = no-op. Every va seam dispatches on `VaListStrategy` with a fail-loud default. The callee reg-save-area zone is gated on strategy ∈ {SysVRegisterSave, Aapcs64DualCursor}. FIX: add `cc.indirectResultRegister`'s ordinal to the scratch avoid-set (→ x9, genuinely free). Structural pin `Aapcs64VariadicStructReturnPrologueScratchAvoidsX8` (red-on-disable verified: revert → scratch=x8) + the `_sret` qemu witness (red-on-disable: scratch=x8 → exit 0, not 126). **Also fixed a latent SHARED-regalloc bug surfaced by the FP-overflow witness:** `pickScratchRegs` (`lir_rewrite.cpp`) keyed its register-in-use mask by the GLOBAL register-table ordinal in a uint64 bitmask, but arm64's 33 GPR table slots push d31 to global ordinal 64 — past the mask → a fail-loud `out of 64-bit bound` on any function spilling an FPR up to d31 (the 9-double case). Re-keyed to an unbounded per-class `unordered_set` of global ordinals, mirroring `buildFreeLists` (lir_regalloc.cpp). Pin `LirRewrite.Arm64HighFprSpillScratchPoolHandlesOrdinalsBeyond64`. | `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-IMM12` | ✅ **ADD/SUB/LEA-IMMEDIATE half CLOSED 2026-06-22 (FC12-deferral 2 / Item 3②)** — the PRACTICAL large-frame blocker. A function with a frame > 4095 bytes (`int big[9000]` = 36000B) failed to encode at THREE sites, all an AArch64 `add`/`sub`/`lea` IMMEDIATE > 4095 (the imm12 slot): prologue `sub sp,#36032`, epilogue `add sp,#36032`, and the high-element FRAME-ADDRESS `lea` (`&big[8999]` = 35996). NON-leaf (saved-reg spill + call) AND register-pressure-spill large frames also confirmed correct at runtime (exit 42 / 104) — the frame layout keeps saved-regs/spills LOW (in imm12), so only the high array-element address goes beyond imm12 and routes through the now-fixed lea. Independent plan-lock + independent pr-review both CLEAN. **DIRECT frame LOAD/STORE displacement (the encodable scaled-imm12 reach) ✅ CLOSED 2026-06-24 (branch feature/0-0-2-p14, HEAD 15c728a, 389 ctest MSVC Release + MinGW + corpus `large_spill_frame_arm64` exit 42 qemu-aarch64 baseline+release).** The scaled-imm12 selection (`load`→`load_u`, `store`→`store_u` when the frame offset exceeds the unscaled imm9 ±256 reach and is encodable: non-negative, access-size-aligned, scaled ≤4095) is now applied at the SINGLE frame load/store CHOKEPOINT `selectFrameMemOp` inside `emitFrameLoad`/`emitFrameStore` (`lir_callconv.cpp`) — so EVERY frame access (spill reload/store, saved-reg save/restore, incoming + outgoing stack args, by-value copy, va spills) is covered BY CONSTRUCTION (the prior incoming-stack-arg-only selection was REMOVED and re-routed through the chokepoint; the encoder `Imm12Scaled` handler + the `load_u`/`store_u` JSON opcodes from `D-ASM-AARCH64-LARGE-FRAME-IMM12` needed NO change). AGNOSTIC: the swap is gated on `baseOp == h.store/h.load` (the universal GPR form — an FPR `fldur`/`fstur`/`fstur_q` keeps its class encoding) AND `h.storeU/h.loadU != 0` (0 on x86_64 → inert, byte-identical goldens). **The earlier "UNREACHABLE in shipped codegen / no producer emits one" claim was FALSIFIED 2026-06-24: the plan-24 `deep_stmt_mir` corpus (600-deep nested-if + the full-release optimizer spills ~590 vregs → frame > 256 B) hit this DIRECT frame `ldr/str [sp, #off]` residual on the macos-clang-release CI leg** — a real producer (heavy register-pressure spill under optimization) DOES emit a direct frame load/store beyond imm9. Closed + RUN-witnessed by a NEW deterministic corpus `examples/c-subset/large_spill_frame_arm64` (a 30-fixed-param AAPCS64 callee `g` called with 30 args → the 9th+ INCOMING stack-arg loads in `g` + the OUTGOING stack-arg stores + caller spill reload/store all exceed imm9 at offsets 256/264 → scaled `load_u`/`store_u`; returns p28+p29+p08 = 1+40+1 = 42, miscompile-sensitive; arm64-only because the un-optimized x86_64 caller exhausts its 16-GPR scratch pool materializing 30 args — a SEPARATE pre-existing regalloc limit, not this fix; qemu-aarch64 exit 42 VERIFIED + macho arm64 leg; RED-on-disable: revert the selector → the arm64 compile fails loud `A_ImmediateOperandOutOfRange` at offsets 256 AND 264 (store AND load) → cannot build) + the host-independent structural callconv pin `Aarch64HighStackParamUsesScaledImm12FrameLoad` (a 40-param callee → asserts `load_u` present in the materialized module + clean assembly, red-on-disable, runs on EVERY CI leg) + the agnostic counter-pin `X8664HighStackParamHasNoScaledImm12FrameOps` (x86_64 declares no `load_u`/`store_u`) + imm9/scaled BOUNDARY byte-pins (offset 255→imm9 STUR, 256→scaled STR, 32760→scaled imm12-max, 256 on the unscaled `store`→fail-loud). The genuinely-UNENCODABLE tail (offset NEGATIVE outside imm9, aligned >4095*accessSize=32760, or non-access-aligned outside imm9 — needs a register-offset / address-materialization form) STAYS fail-loud → the narrower residual `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-SCALED-IMM12` (row below). | `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-16MIB` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-23 (FC-deferral close-out c12, branch feature/0-0-2-p14, 374 ctest + corpus `large_frame_beyond_16mib` exit 42 qemu-aarch64 baseline+release).** AS-BUILT (§B Option A — encoder macro, x16 baked): a NEW `EncodingSlotKind::Imm32MovzMovk` (value-bearing fixed32 slot; the encoder splits a 32-bit value lo16→word0 / hi16→word1 into the MOVZ/MOVK imm16 windows, mirroring `materializeViaMovkLadder`'s chunk split) + a NEW 3-word `fixedWords` variant per `add`/`sub`/`lea` in `arm64.target.json`, magnitude-routed by the variant `immMin:16777216`/`immMax:2147483647` guard. The macro is `MOVZ Xs,#(V & 0xFFFF)` + `MOVK Xs,#((V>>16) & 0xFFFF),LSL #16` + an EXTENDED-register op: for the sp-adjust `sub sp,sp,x16` (0xCB3063FF) / `add sp,sp,x16` (0x8B3063FF) with **x16 (AAPCS64 IP0 scratch) BAKED** into all 3 base words (NO resultSlot — sp=31 baked into the op word, validate's rule-G `imm32.movzmovk` baked-dest exemption); for the lea `add Xd,sp,Xd` (0x8B2063E0 base) SCRATCH-FREE — the displacement materializes into the lea's OWN dest reg Xd, threaded through all 3 words via resultSlot+extraResultSlots (the operand-0→rn wire sets Rn from the ACTUAL frame-base operand — sp here, so Rn=31=sp, byte-pinned; the override is general so a non-sp base would get its own Rn). The EXTENDED-register form (bit 21, option=011 UXTX) is the make-or-break: the shifted-register form (0xCB000000) would write XZR not sp → corrupt frame. AGNOSTIC (x86_64 has no imm16/movzmovk slot → never reached; slot-kind `==` + value-magnitude arithmetic only; the x16 identity is config-baked like XZR=31/sp=31). Byte-pinned (sub sp #0x1234000 → MOVZ/MOVK + 0xCB3063FF full 32-bit word; lea → MOVZ/MOVK + 0x8B2263E2; boundary pins 0xFFFFFF→2-word / 0x1000000→3-word / 0x7FFFFFFF→3-word / 0x80000000→fail-loud) + a callconv F4 structural pin (prologue's first word = `MOVZ x16` + x16 not value-allocated, durable scratch-safety) + **objdump-confirmed + run-witnessed `examples/c-subset/large_frame_beyond_16mib` exit 42 under qemu-aarch64 (baseline+release, Inlining ON) + x86_64-linux** (RED-ON-DISABLE: removing the variant's reachable range → A_NoMatchingEncodingVariant on the sub/add sp-adjust → the arm64 leg cannot produce a binary). Genuinely-unencodable residual → `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-2GIB` (row below; a >2 GiB frame goes negative through the int32 frame size → no variant matches → fail-loud). _Original deferral below._ NEW RESIDUAL of `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-IMM12` (FC12-deferral 2, 2026-06-22): the SCRATCH-FREE shifted-imm12 word-pair (`EncodingSlotKind::Imm12HiLo24` + the `add`/`sub`/`lea` 2-word variants `op Xd,Xn,#lo` then `op Xd,Xd,#hi,LSL #12` in `arm64.target.json`, magnitude-routed by the variant `immMin`/`immMax` guard) now lands an `add`/`sub`/`lea` IMMEDIATE in (4095, 0xFFFFFF] — a 16 MiB frame reach, covering every realistic frame (e.g. `int big[9000]` = 36000B prologue + `&big[8999]` lea). A value > 0xFFFFFF (16 MiB) STILL fails loud: the add/sub/lea variant selector rejects it (`A_NoMatchingEncodingVariant`, since `immMax:16777215` excludes it), and the encoder's `writeHiLo24` 24-bit gate (`A_ImmediateOperandOutOfRange`) is the defense-in-depth backstop. No shipped corpus has a > 16 MiB single frame; this row keeps the ledger honest about the genuinely-unencodable tail. Priority: **low** (only a single function with > 16 MiB of locals). | Add a THIRD word to the macro (`#hi2,LSL #24` reaching 36 bits) OR materialize the offset into a scratch register via MOVZ/MOVK + a register-form `add/sub Xd,Xn,Xm` and select it when the value exceeds 0xFFFFFF. | `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-IMM12`; `D-ASM-AARCH64-LARGE-FRAME-IMM12`; plan 13 (asm encoding) |
| `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-SCALED-IMM12` | **OPEN (trigger-gated) — registered 2026-06-24 (scaled-imm12 frame load/store close-out, branch feature/0-0-2-p14).** NEW narrower residual of `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-IMM12` (row above): now that the ENCODABLE scaled unsigned-offset frame load/store (`load_u`/`store_u`, LDR/STR `[Xn,#imm12]`, reach 0..4095×accessSize = 0..32760 for an 8-byte slot) is selected at the `selectFrameMemOp` chokepoint, a frame `ldr/str [sp, #off]` whose `off` is GENUINELY UNENCODABLE by BOTH the unscaled imm9 (−256..255) AND the scaled unsigned imm12 STAYS fail-loud `A_ImmediateOperandOutOfRange` at the fixed32 encoder (`src/asm/format/fixed32.cpp` Imm12Scaled handler). Three sub-cases: (a) a NEGATIVE offset outside imm9 (the scaled form has no sign bit), (b) an aligned offset > 32760 (scaled field > 4095), (c) a non-access-size-aligned offset outside imm9 (the scaled field is byteOffset/accessSize — an unaligned LDR is architecturally undefined). The chokepoint keeps `baseOp` (the unscaled form) in each case → the encoder fail-louds. NOT reachable by any shipped corpus: case (a) needs a base-relative negative beyond −256 (frame offsets are non-negative sp-relative), (b) needs a single frame spill/saved-reg/stack-arg offset > 32760 B (a ~32 KB spill area — far past the deepest corpus pressure), (c) needs an unaligned frame slot (all slots are slotSize-aligned). This row keeps the ledger honest about the genuinely-unencodable tail. Priority: **low** (the closing form is the register-OFFSET LDR/STR `ldr Xt,[Xn,Xm]` or an address-materialization into a scratch — only needed for a >32 KB single-access offset or a future unaligned/negative frame access, neither of which a producer emits today). | Emit the register-offset frame form (`ldr/str Xt,[sp,Xm]` after MOVZ/MOVK-materializing the offset into a scratch `Xm`), OR materialize the address `add Xd,sp,#off` (via the shipped shifted-imm12 / MOVZ-MOVK macro) then `ldr/str [Xd,#0]` — selected when the offset fits NEITHER imm9 nor the scaled imm12; stay agnostic (slot-kind `==` + value-magnitude arithmetic, no arch/cc identity). Pin with a synthetic >32760 frame-offset case (fail-loud red-on-disable) + a runtime corpus only if a producer ever emits a >32 KB single-access frame offset. | `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-IMM12` (the parent, load/store-displacement half closed 2026-06-24); `D-ASM-AARCH64-LARGE-FRAME-IMM12` (the scaled-imm12 encoder + opcodes); `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-16MIB` (the add/sub/lea-immediate sibling); plan 13 (asm encoding) |
| `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-2GIB` | NEW RESIDUAL of `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-16MIB` (FC-deferral close-out c12, 2026-06-23): the MOVZ/MOVK + EXTENDED-register 3-word form (`EncodingSlotKind::Imm32MovzMovk` + the `add`/`sub`/`lea` 3-word variants in `arm64.target.json`, magnitude-routed by `immMin:16777216`/`immMax:2147483647`) now lands an `add`/`sub`/`lea` IMMEDIATE in (0xFFFFFF, 0x7FFFFFFF] — a ~2 GiB frame reach, far past any realistic frame. A value > 0x7FFFFFFF (2 GiB) STILL fails loud: the frame size flows through `emitSpAdjust`'s `static_cast<int32_t>(bytes)` and `variantImmMagnitude`'s `immInt32` (int32) — a >2 GiB magnitude goes NEGATIVE, so `variantImmMagnitude` returns nullopt → NO variant matches → `A_NoMatchingEncodingVariant`; the encoder's `writeMovzMovk` 0..0x7FFFFFFF gate (`A_ImmediateOperandOutOfRange`) is the defense-in-depth backstop. | `D-WIN64-LARGE-FRAME-STACK-PROBE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-23 (FC-deferral close-out c11, branch p14, 372 ctest + corpus `large_frame_win64` exit 42 native Windows baseline+release).** AS-BUILT: an INLINE page-walking stack probe emitted by the x86_64 encoder from a NEW `stack_probe` LIR op (chosen over `__chkstk` because dss PE exes are FREESTANDING — import only kernel32, not msvcrt where __chkstk lives; verified). Config-driven `stackProbePageBytes` on TargetCallingConvention (ms_x64=4096, all others 0/absent → no probe; validate() requires a power of two). `emitPrologue` (threaded `cc`) emits `StackProbe(sp, frameBytes, pageBytes)` when `cc.stackProbePageBytes>0 && totalFrameSize>pageBytes`, else the plain `sub rsp,F` (byte-identical small-frame/non-Windows path). The encoder hand-emits the loop `mov r11d,frame / .L: sub rsp,page / or qword[rsp],0 / sub r11d,page / cmp r11d,page / ja .L (0x77, compile-time rel8, no reloc) / sub rsp,r11` — r11 is ms_x64 caller-saved, not arg/return, probe runs before arg-home. AGNOSTIC (no `if arch/format==`; page step from the op operand, not hardcoded; arm64 OMITS the op → A_NoEncodingDeclared if ever emitted). RED-ON-DISABLE (the strongest kind): the corpus CRASHES (SIGSEGV exit 139) without the probe, exit 42 with — native on the Windows box. Byte-pins (frame 36000 non-multiple + 8192 exact-page, exact 0x77 ja) + prologue structural pins (ms_x64>4096→probe; ≤4096 + sysv>4096→plain). **★ the unforgeable native witness caught a real bug in the build: a first `sub rsp,r11` mis-encoded as `49 29 DB` (=`sub r11,rbx`) segfaulted EVEN WITH the probe → fixed to `4C 29 DC`, byte-pinned.** ORIGINALLY: **OPEN — a SILENT RUNTIME CRASH** (surfaced 2026-06-22 while adding the `large_frame_arm64` corpus, but ENTIRELY ORTHOGONAL to the arm64 fix — a pre-existing x86_64-Windows gap). DSS did NOT emit a stack-probe (`__chkstk` / page-walk) for `ms_x64` / `pe64` functions whose frame exceeds one guard page (4096B). A function like `int main(){ int big[9000]; ... }` for `x86_64:pe64-x86_64-windows-exec` emits a bare prologue `sub rsp, ~36016` that jumps ~9 pages PAST the stack guard page WITHOUT touching the intermediate pages → the first deep-slot access raises `STATUS_ACCESS_VIOLATION` (0xC0000005) at runtime. The Windows x64 ABI REQUIRES a function allocating >1 page to probe each page (`__chkstk`, or an inline `sub rsp,0x1000`/`test [rsp],eax` loop) so the guard page walks down one page at a time and the kernel commits each. Empirically verified: a 400B + a 4400B frame exit 42, a 36000B frame segfaults. Linux x86_64 + AArch64-ELF do NOT need it (kernel stack-growth guard-gap absorbs the multi-page jump — which is why `large_frame_arm64` exits 42 on x86_64-linux + qemu-aarch64). This is WHY the `x86_64:pe64` target was excluded from `examples/c-subset/large_frame_arm64/expected.json` (see its `$comment`). Priority: **normal** (a real silent-crash class on >1-page Windows frames — large local buffers; converting it to FAIL-LOUD is a cheap interim). | Implement Windows large-frame stack probing in the prologue SP-adjust (`lir_callconv.cpp` emitPrologue/emitSpAdjust), gated AGNOSTICALLY on a CC/format-declared stack-probe-threshold field (mirroring `redZoneBytes`/`shadowSpaceBytes`, NOT `if(arch=="x86_64")`): when the frame exceeds the page size, emit the page-walk probe (or a `call __chkstk`) before/in place of the single `sub rsp,N`; add a runtime corpus witness (re-add the `x86_64:pe64` target to `large_frame_arm64`) + a structural pin. INTERIM (cheaper, kills the silent crash now): a fail-loud guard refusing a >1-page ms_x64 frame until probing lands. | plan 13 (asm encoding); plan 14 (linker); `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-IMM12` (the arm64 sibling, closed) |
| `D-WIN64-PDATA-XDATA-UNWIND` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-07-06 (p19 Cluster G c114) — the pe64 leg emits Windows x64 SEH/unwind tables (`.pdata` RUNTIME_FUNCTION[] + `.xdata` UNWIND_INFO) per function and points `IMAGE_DATA_DIRECTORY[3]` (EXCEPTION) at `.pdata`; sqlite3.exe compiles SEH-only (no `SQLITE_DISABLE_INTRINSIC`) + RUNS on Windows (`--version`→3.54.0, canonical smoke `SELECT sum`→42, full CRUD 52, index-filter 40).** WHY: the x64 ABI needs each function's PROLOGUE described so `RtlVirtualUnwind` can reconstruct the caller's context; without `.pdata` a fault (or, later, a `__try`) cannot unwind. WITNESSES: host-independent byte pin `PeExecWriter.FunctionUnwindInfoEmitsPdataXdataAndExceptionDataDir` (frame 0x20 + saves [xmm6@0, rbx@8, rbp@16] → CountOfCodes=5 [xmm6 omitted, else 7], rbx CodeOffset 23 [proves xmm width 8 via hwEncoding 6, not 9 via ordinal 30], EXCEPTION dir→.pdata; RED-on-disable=revert FPR-omit→fail-loud, or drop emission→no .pdata) + runtime corpus `examples/c-subset/pe_unwind_selftest` (main takes `&target_fn`, calls kernel32 `RtlLookupFunctionEntry`, asserts the OS-found entry's BeginAddress==the fn RVA → exit 42; RED-on-disable→NULL→91; pe64-only, `release`-pipeline arm). objdump on sqlite3.exe: `Entry 3 … Exception Directory [.pdata]`, 3200 RUNTIME_FUNCTIONs + 86 KB `.xdata`. **Trigger:** FIRED — sqlite's os_win.c saves xmm callee-saves, so the compile hit the FPR path. | (closed — `.pdata`/`.xdata` emission + the EXCEPTION data dir + the FrameUnwindInfo projection) | [[D-WIN64-XMM-UNWIND-RESTORE]] (c116 handler restore) · [[D-WIN64-CHKSTK-LARGE-PROLOGUE]] + [[D-WIN64-HUGE-FRAME-ALLOC]] (fail-loud siblings) · `D-WIN64-LARGE-FRAME-STACK-PROBE` (the probe whose length allocLen recomputes) · the SEH arc c115 (`__try`/`__except` parse) + c116 (funclets); plan 14 linker / plan 23 SQLite-green Windows leg |

| `D-WIN64-XMM-UNWIND-RESTORE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-07-06 (c116) via option (b) PROVE-NO-CONSUMER + an ENFORCED fail-loud invariant.** The trigger fired (the c116 handler funclets landed). RESOLUTION: sqlite's 7 `__try`-guarding WAL-recovery functions spill ZERO non-volatile xmm (empirically — `.pdata`/`.xdata`-extracted; WAL recovery is pure integer/pointer code), so no `__except` handler resumes into a frame reading an unrestored xmm → the omitted `SAVE_XMM128` is harmless for the shipped corpus. This proof is now an ENFORCED INVARIANT, not a hope: `pe.cpp buildFunctionUnwindInfo` FAILS LOUD (`K_NoMatchingObjectFormat`) if a scope-table-bearing (SEH-guarding) function saves a NON-volatile xmm — so a future SEH-fn-with-xmm cannot silently ship a broken unwind table; it forces the option-(a) work (spill xmm6-15 with `movaps` + emit `UWOP_SAVE_XMM128`) to land first. PINNED red-on-disable: `PeExecWriter.SehGuardingFunctionSavingNonVolatileXmmFailsLoud` (a scope-bearing fn + an xmm6 save → the encoder errors; drop the `guardsSeh` arm → it silently omits the restore) + the paired non-SEH negative (`FunctionUnwindInfoEmitsPdata...` — the same xmm6 save on a NON-SEH fn encodes fine). [SUPERSEDED OPEN TEXT:] c114 OMITS FPR callee-saves (MS-x64 xmm6..15) from the `.xdata` unwind codes because DSS spills them low-64 via `movsd`, for which there is NO matching x64 UWOP (`UWOP_SAVE_XMM128` restores a full 16-byte `movaps` slot at an offset/16 node). This is CORRECT for c114's scope — an xmm save does not affect RSP/return-address reconstruction, so `RtlVirtualUnwind`'s STACK walk stays exact — but a language-level exception HANDLER that RESUMES after catching (SEH `__try/__except`, c116) needs the non-volatile xmm6..15 RESTORED to their entry values, which the unwinder can only do from a described `SAVE_XMM128` slot. CLOSING WORK (at c116): either (a) spill xmm callee-saves with a 16-byte `movaps` to a 16-aligned slot + emit `UWOP_SAVE_XMM128` (widen the DSS FPR save form on ms_x64), or (b) prove no `__C_specific_handler` scope resumes into a frame reading a clobbered xmm. Until then a handler that reads a non-volatile xmm after unwinding gets a stale value — a LATENT gap with NO shipped consumer (c114 has no exception handlers). | (closed c116 — prove-no-consumer + the fail-loud invariant) | [[D-WIN64-PDATA-XDATA-UNWIND]] (parent, c114) · [[D-WIN64-SEH-FUNCLETS]] (c116) |

| `D-FC12B-WIN64-STRUCT-VARARG` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-20 (FC12b-struct).** Win64 (ms_x64, `VaListStrategy::HomogeneousPointer`) struct-by-value at the variadic boundary + `va_arg(ap, struct)`. **NO new MIR op / LIR kind / carrier, NO lir_callconv / aggregate_abi change** — the design REUSED proven mechanisms: the Win64 ABI passes a by-value struct in EXACTLY ONE arg slot (pow2-≤8B → `classifyAggregate(Win64BySize)` InRegisters[1 GPR piece] = the bytes BY VALUE; ByReference → copy-to-temp + push the temp POINTER → 1 operand) + `runGpr += numGp` (==1) so a subsequent vararg's slot index is right; the SysV atomic-fit/`gpSaveCount` split + `appendByValueStackArg` carrier + the AAPCS64 guard are SKIPPED for HomogeneousPointer and PRESERVED byte-unchanged for SysVRegisterSave/Aapcs64DualCursor. **Callee (`lowerVaArgAggregate` HomogeneousPointer arm):** classify via `byValueClassify(T)` — InRegisters (≤8B) → the slot IS the storage, return apVal (the slot addr), NO extra Load (mirrors the SysV overflow-arm `return ovfArea`); ByReference (>8B) → Load the pointer from `*apVal` → the caller-copy addr; both bump `ap` by `namedArgSlotBytes` (one slot, value or pointer — NOT roundUp(size,8)), LINEAR (no diamond), mirroring the scalar HomogeneousPointer va_arg. **Pins (red-on-disable verified):** the 2 fail-loud pins INVERTED to success + 2 new (`Win64VaArgStructLeq8ReturnsSlotAddr` / `Gt8DerefsPointer` — no ICmpUle/carrier, the >8B deref adds a Load; | `D-CSUBSET-LINKAGE-UNKNOWN-SPECIFIER-DIAGNOSTIC` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-04 (cycle 14).** Built as decided (agnostic specifier-identity + fail-loud ERROR). **Mechanism**: new per-decl facet `linkageSpecifierIgnoredKinds` (the prefix's STRUCTURAL token KINDS to skip — c-subset: AttributeKeyword/ParenOpen/ParenClose); loader resolves names→SchemaTokenId (unknown→C_UnknownToken, mirrors variadicMarker; non-array/non-string→C_InvalidSemantics); `linkageFrom` skips ignored-kind tokens and emits `H_UnknownLinkageSpecifier=0xF00C` on any non-ignored prefix token missing from `linkageSpecifiers` (skip-list DEFAULT = fail-loud). Behavior = Error (NOT GCC warn-and-ignore), per the original design-lock + §A.4. Priority: **high (next cycle).** — Cycle-13 review finding (silent-failure-hunter, MEDIUM): an UNRECOGNIZED specifier identifier inside `__attribute__((...))` — a typo (`((wek))`) OR a valid-C attribute c-subset doesn't model (`((noinline))`, `((packed))`) — is SILENTLY ignored by `linkageFrom` (facet miss → no effect, no diagnostic); the decl silently keeps default (Global) linkage. NOT a valid-code miscompile (static/weak are correct + proven) and GCC-compatible leniency (GCC ignores unknown attributes with a `-Wattributes` warning), but misses the project's fail-loud preference on unrecognized input. **§B DECISION (needs user input before building)**: (a) the AGNOSTIC MECHANISM — `linkageFrom`'s flat token-walk cannot distinguish an unknown SPECIFIER from structural SYNTAX (`__attribute__`, parens) without language config; the reviewer's "Identifier-directly-under-attrSpec" distinguisher is c-subset-grammar-specific (would break agnosticism if hardcoded), so a clean fix needs the language to DECLARE which prefix tokens/positions are specifier-IDENTITIES vs pure-syntax (a new facet or a per-rule marker), then the engine emits on an identity-token that misses the facet while still skipping syntax; (b) the BEHAVIOR — Error (strict) vs Warning (GCC `-Wattributes`) vs silent-ignore (current). Priority: **normal** (missing-diagnostic on unrecognized input, not a correctness bug for valid input). | Resolve the §B (mechanism + behavior) with the user, then implement the agnostic specifier-identity recognition + emit the chosen diagnostic; pin with `__attribute__((bogus))` → diagnostic. | `D-CSUBSET-GLOBAL-AGGREGATE-RELOC-MEMBER` | **OPEN — pre-existing limitation surfaced p18 c12, 2026-06-26; fail-LOUD, normal.** A FILE-SCOPE/global aggregate (`struct`/array) whose initializer contains a RELOCATION-bearing member — a function pointer (`struct Ops g = { dbl };`, the SQLite VFS/method-table vtable shape) OR a data pointer (`struct P g = { &x };`) — fails LOUD: `H_UnsupportedLoweringForKind ... aggregate compound-literal/initializer must be lowered into a slot by ADDRESS ... The global-init path (`hir_to_mir.cpp` `tryClassifyAsSymbolAddr`) recognizes only SCALAR symbol-address inits (`int* p = &x;` AddressOf(Ref), `char* g = "...";` Cast(string)) — an aggregate `ConstructAggregate` initializer returns nullopt, const-eval can't fold a reloc, and the runtime-init path can't store an aggregate RVALUE. NOT fn-ptr-specific (a `{&x}` data-ptr member fails identically); NOT a silent miscompile (fails loud); the LOCAL case works (runtime store-into-slot). The aggregate analog of F5's scalar symbol-address globals. | Closing work = extend the global-aggregate emitter to lay out per-FIELD data items with per-member abs64 relocations (mixed const + symbol-address members at their byte offsets — `lowerMirGlobalsToDataItems` per-field, the F5 scalar path generalized to aggregate members). | `D-CSUBSET-PER-TARGET-STRUCT-LAYOUT` | ✅ **MECHANISM DONE 2026-06-26 (p18 Cluster G c13, plan 25); ALL 6 linux POSIX headers DONE (c14a-e); the per-target `variants` axis EXTENDED to constants/typedefs/macros + macOS errno PROVEN (c15a 187a54a / c15b 73c5763); remaining 5 macOS headers OPEN (c15c).** §B decision (user, 2026-06-26): build the FULL per-target struct-layout mechanism (not linux-x86-64-only) so macOS/arm64 SQLite are reachable without reworking descriptors. | `D-CSUBSET-LABEL-BUDGET-CLIFF` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-28 (p19 Cluster G c31).** sqlite3.c:213922 — a C label before a LARGE statement: `json_parse_restart:` preceding a ~900-case JSON `switch` failed P0001 "got ':'". ROOT: `declOrExprStmt` (`alt:[labelStmt,identVarDecl,exprStmt]`, speculative lookahead 256 ⇒ a `lookahead*16` = 4096-token probe budget) speculatively parses `labelStmt = Identifier Colon statement` to COMPLETION; a labeled statement >4096 tokens exhausts the probe budget → rollback → exprStmt → P0001 at the `:` (confirmed empirically: a small labeled switch parses, a ~900-case one does not). | ✅ FIX = a NEW general parser facet `commitAfterPrefix` (a PEG "cut"), AGNOSTIC (names no token/rule/keyword/language). `labelStmt` KEEPS its `Identifier Colon statement` shape (so a label stays correct in EVERY context, incl. a braceless control-flow body — `if(x) L: s;` ⇒ `s` IS the if's body). The facet: once a candidate's FIXED leading token-prefix (`predictivePrefixLen` — here `Identifier Colon` + the first `statement` token) is consumed in a speculative probe WITHOUT failure, the parser COMMITS (`probe.commit()`) and hands the STILL-OPEN frame to the non-speculative dispatch loop — the rest of the rule parses with NO budget (exactly the unique-production direct-descent's "open frame, let the outer loop drive it"). SOUND because after `Identifier Colon` no other `declOrExprStmt` alt can match (neither identVarDecl nor exprStmt has Colon in 2nd position), so committing discards nothing; a non-label `foo + bar;` fails at the `Colon` slot BEFORE the prefix is consumed, so the cut never fires (falls through to exprStmt). Wiring: `CompiledRule::commitAfterPrefix` (bool) ← loader parses an optional boolean `commitAfterPrefix` on the shape body (fail-loud if non-boolean; mutually-exclusive with `commitRequiresTypeName`); `GrammarSchema::commitAfterPrefix(RuleId)` accessor; the cut block inside `trySpeculativeBranch`'s probe loop after the post-`stepOnce` diag/desync rechecks; `SpeculationProbe::startPos()` accessor. Only `labelStmt` carries the flag (`"commitAfterPrefix": true`). NO HIR/MIR/verifier/lowering change (`git diff --stat`: 6 files — parser.cpp, compiled_shape.hpp, grammar_schema.{hpp,cpp}, grammar_schema_json.cpp, c-subset.lang.json). ★ BRACELESS-BODY CORRECTNESS (the case that doomed any flatten-labelStmt alternative) VERIFIED at runtime: `if(x) L: g=42;` exits 5 for x=0 (the labeled `g=42` is the if's body and is NOT executed) and 42 for x=1. | `D-CSUBSET-FNPTR-PARAM-SCOPE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-28 (p19 Cluster G c32).** sqlite3.c:1175-1176 (`struct sqlite3_io_methods`) — the PARAMETER NAMES of a function-POINTER declarator collided across sibling declarators AND leaked into the enclosing scope: `int (*xRead)(... int iAmt ...); int (*xWrite)(... int iAmt ...);` → `error[S0002] S_RedeclaredSymbol: got iAmt`. (2) STRUCT+LOADER: `DeclaratorConfig::prototypeParamScopeRule` (+ name field) loaded via the same `readOptionalRuleRole` discipline + added to the closed-keys set (15→16). (3) SCOPE-OPEN: Pass-1 opens a THROWAWAY scope for any node of that rule UNLESS it is a function DEFINITION's OWN param list — detected by the SHARED config-driven shape tests (`directDeclaratorIsNameBearing` — the suffix sits on a NAME-bearing direct declarator, NOT a fn-pointer whose base is a `parenDeclarator`) AND `declNodeIsFunctionDefinition` (the enclosing decl's kindByChild resolves to Function — a body present). So: a fn-ptr member/typedef/param ⇒ base is a parenDeclarator ⇒ ISOLATE; a bare prototype ⇒ name-bearing but no body ⇒ ISOLATE (its name re-homes to file scope via the separate `isProto` path); a definition ⇒ name-bearing + body ⇒ do NOT open (params bind into the topLevelDecl scope, body-visible). (4) ★ 3-PASS CONSISTENCY: the whole "does this node open a child scope (and which)" decision is FACTORED into ONE shared predicate `nodeOpensChildScope` (folding the c25 `scopeByRule`+`isDefinitionAtNode` gate AND the c32 prototype case) used by ALL THREE passes — `pass1Node` (pushes), `resolveDeclTypes` + the `pass2` driver (re-derive by anchor lookup) — so a param can never bind in one scope yet be looked up in another. | `D-CSUBSET-ARRAY-SIZE-INFERENCE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-28 (p19 Cluster G c34).** sqlite3.c:506 `SQLITE_API const char sqlite3_version[] = SQLITE_VERSION;` (i.e. `const char x[] = "3.x.y";`) — an array declared with an EMPTY bound `[]` AND an initializer was rejected `error[S000B] S_NonConstantArrayLength` (the resolver returned an incomplete array ONLY in a flexible-array-member context; a `[]` VARIABLE with a missing length always erred). C 6.7.9p22: such an array infers its length from the initializer — `char x[] = "abc"` → `char[4]` ("abc"+NUL), `int a[] = {1,2,3}` → `int[3]`. | ✅ FIX (config-driven, REUSE; one completion site so all downstream agree). (1) The array-suffix `[]` (absent length) already yields an INCOMPLETE array when "missing-length-is-OK" (`allowFlexibleArray`); REUSE that path for a VARIABLE by RELAXING the flag at the Pass-1.5 var/global declared-type site (`resolveDeclTypes`, semantic_analyzer.cpp) to `decl.allowFlexibleArray || <this declarator has an initializer>` — so a `[]`-with-init resolves to `T[]` (incomplete) instead of erroring, while a `[]` with NO init keeps the original flag (false for a var/global rule) ⇒ `S_NonConstantArrayLength` still fires (never a silently-sized array). The group recursion into a nested declarator still passes false (a nested fn-ptr param's `[]` errors). (2) A NEW helper `completeIncompleteArrayFromInit` (Pass-1.5, the SINGLE completion site → sizeof/layout/element-access/BOTH HIR paths observe the SAME sized array) completes the incomplete array: a STRING-literal init → N = decoded-bytes + 1 (the NUL), counted via the SHARED `decodeAdjacentStringBodies` chokepoint (escapes count once — `"\x41\x42"` → 2+NUL=3; adjacent concat `"ab" "cd"` → 5); a BRACE init → N = the count of TOP-LEVEL `initElement` children of the brace list. The element type is recovered from the incomplete array's `operands()[0]`, so a malformed escape leaves it incomplete (no guessed size; the HIR tier fails loud on the bad literal). NO HIR/MIR change — the existing explicit-size lowering (`char x[4]="abc"`, `int a[3]={…}`) applies once the type is completed to the same sized array (the HIR var/global path reads the symbol's resolved `.type`). AGNOSTIC: two new by-NAME index rules (`braceInitList`/`initElement`, resolved like `stringLiteralExprRule`) + the existing `stringLiteralExprRule`/body-token; no lang/arch/format/keyword hardcode. PRESERVE-verified: explicit `[N]` unchanged (completion is a no-op on an already-sized array — `char x[8]="abc"` stays `[8]`, not re-derived to 4); over-long explicit `char x[2]="abc"` keeps its current S0003; a bare `[]` no-init stays incomplete/error. ★ AUDIT-CAUGHT REGRESSION (fixed before commit): an EMPTY brace `int a[] = {}` (top-level count 0) returned the incomplete array with NO diagnostic — and the unguarded HIR/MIR tier LOOPED on the -1 sentinel length (a compiler HANG; a fail-loud VIOLATION the relaxation introduced — pre-c34 it was a clean S_NonConstantArrayLength). | `D-CSUBSET-DIVISION-CORPUS-MATERIALIZE-BUG` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-04** (cycle 10r BUG FIX). Root cause identified + fixed: NOT a materialize-pass bug. The cycle-10q compound encoding packed `[REX.W 0x99, REX.W 0xF7 /7]` as a single opcode's `opcode` array. The x86-variable encoder auto-emits ONE REX prefix at instruction start computed from operand high bits (e.g., 0x41 = REX.B for R14). Per x86 decode the LAST REX before the opcode wins — the embedded second literal 0x48 (REX.W only) superseded the auto-REX, losing REX.B. IDIV operand decoded as RSI (without REX.B) instead of R14 → divide-by-zero trap. Cycle 10r SPLIT the compound into separate `cqo`/`idiv_op`/`xor_rdx_zero`/`div_op` opcodes (each a single instruction with its own auto-REX). | (closed) | plan 12 ML5 (asm encoder) + ML6 (regalloc); paired with D-CSUBSET-DIVISION-OP-CODEGEN closure |

| `D-CSUBSET-SYMBOL-ADDRESS-GLOBAL` | **✅ CLOSED 2026-06-25 (Cluster F F5 — 8 stage commits; 405/405 ctest Release; PE+ELF runtime exit 143; Mach-O rebase byte-verified + macOS-CI-leg runtime CONFIRMED GREEN — run 28150522650 (headSha 191b756) macos-clang-release ✓).** A global initialized to the LINK-TIME-CONSTANT address of another symbol — `char* g = "...";` (string→rodata), `int* p = &x;` (&global), or a function-pointer table. The semantic tier fails LOUD: a Variable-kind declarator whose folded type is a bare `FnSig` emits `S_InvalidFunctionDeclarator` ("function prototype declarations are not supported here; use 'extern'") rather than silently minting an FnSig-typed data global (which would miscompile at MIR). NOT a miscompile (coerce's conversions are correct; non-arith mismatches still fail loud via the verifier as `H_VerifierFailure`) — a DIAGNOSTIC-QUALITY + consistency gap. | `D-CSUBSET-BITFIELD-INIT` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-18 (FC8 cycle 4 "bit-field aggregate init", branch p10).** Aggregate INITIALIZATION of a bit-field struct/union now PACKS per allocation unit at all three sites (replacing the cycle-2 fail-louds): (1) LOCAL `struct S s = {…};` → `lowerBitfieldAggregateInitIntoSlot` (`hir_to_mir.cpp`) zeroes every bit-field allocation unit in a PRE-PASS (before any field value is written) then RMWs each field in via the SAME `emitBitfieldInsert` the field-by-field write uses (single packing chokepoint); ordinary fields among the bit-fields lower normally. Fixed via the TWO-PASS above (zero ALL units, then write ALL fields — order-independent; the RMW preserves the zero in bits it does not set, ordinary fields occupy disjoint bytes; dedup on `(offset,unitBytes)` covers mixed-width units sharing an offset). Today's corpus runs Win64 only because `pe64-x86_64-windows-exec` is the sole `targets[*].spec`, but the `long`→I64 binding bakes a data-model decision into the source-language config in a way that violates the agnosticism rule (lang config should not assume ABI). **SCOPE EXTENSION (2026-06-09, the `#include puts` 3-OS string-FFI capstone — STILL OPEN):** this anchor now ALSO covers the **shipped-lib descriptor surface**. That is CORRECT for the runnable linux/macos targets (LP64), but the **Windows LLP64 form for these 6 (where `long` = i32) is now LATENTLY DEFERRED** — confirmed UNEXERCISED by any corpus (no shipped-`fseek`/`strtol`/etc. call compiles to a Windows target today; the running `puts`/`abs` corpora touch no width-divergent symbol). The proper fix is the SAME as the `long`-keyword case: an abstract `long`/`size_t` resolved per-target (the descriptor signatures would spell `long`/`size_t` abstractly, the data-model axis below would bind them per active target). Do NOT file a duplicate anchor — this is one and the same "config baked an ABI/width decision" gap, now spanning both the c-subset `long` keyword AND the neutral shipped descriptors. | Extend the `SemanticConfig` schema with a `dataModel` axis (e.g., `"ILP32"` / `"LP64"` / `"LLP64"`) that `builtinTypes[*].core` can vary on; OR add an ABI-conditioning layer in the HIR→MIR lowering that overrides core types per active target. | `D-FC7-STRUCT-BY-VALUE-ARG-RETURN` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-16 (FC7 C3, branch p9, commits d25696d + 03ba02d) — ALL 4 ABIs done.** C3 = AAPCS64 + Apple arm64 via the **IRR-reroute design** (§B Option A — explicit indirect-result register, refined at build time from the plan-lock's `WriteIndirectResult` op, which was UNSOUND because x8 is allocatable: emitting `mov x8,R` before arg-setup could clobber an arg parked in x8). As-built: the caller reuses the existing sret-pointer PREPEND (operands[1]) + a new `call_payload::kIndirectResultBit` (bit 30) that lir_callconv reads to ROUTE that operand to `cc.indirectResultRegister` (x8) via the SAME `argMoves` parallel-move set (inherits the hazard detection; R is a real Call operand ⇒ regalloc keeps it live; an arg-in-x8 is read by its own earlier arg-move before the appended IRR move writes x8 — no clobber, genuine cycle fails loud like D-ML7-2.3). Callee reads x8 via a new `ReadIndirectResult` op (mirror of `Arg`) + returns VOID (`WriteIndirectResult` was DESIGNED but proved dead → removed). HFA classifier (`aapcs64_hfa`: 1–4 same-FP-type leaves → that many FPR pieces, width-honoring `pieceType` F32/F64; non-HFA ≤16B → ceil(size/8) GPR; >16B → x8-sret) + config (both arm64 CC rows: strategy/maxRegBytes=16/indirectResultRegister=x8/returnFprs=d0..d3). SF-1 ✅ (the `emitParallelRegMoves` >2-cycle guard raised — the scratch-break linearizes any cycle). **★ FOUND + FIXED a HIGH PRE-EXISTING silent miscompile (the crux of this cycle):** every MIR `Return`-CLONE site (`mir_merge.cpp` cross-CU + `mir_rebuild_helper.cpp` shared rebuild [the baseline `runPruneUnreachableBlocks` path] + `inlining.cpp` caller-clone) mapped ONLY `oldOps[0]`, TRUNCATING every multi-piece struct return to piece 0 — and `Return.maxOperands` was `1` (the verifier's upper guard of the same bug). C1c's multi-piece return therefore NEVER worked end-to-end; it was masked on x86_64 because the dropped piece's value usually still aliased its arg register at the return register (a 3rd field passed in rdx == returnGprs[1]) — AAPCS64's distinct arg/return mapping exposed it (`mkTri` read field 3 as field 2). Fix: all clone sites map ALL operands via `addReturnMulti` + `Return.maxOperands`→N + a fail-loud guard for inlining a multi-piece return (`D-FC7-INLINE-MULTI-PIECE-RETURN`).
