| `D-FC7-SYSV-STRUCT-ARG-MULTIREG` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-16 (FC7 C1b, §B Option A, commit b7f547d).** A 2-eightbyte (9–16 byte) struct now passes/receives IN REGISTERS. **As-built (simpler than the registered plan):** (1) HIR→MIR emits each param + struct-piece `Arg` with a MONOTONIC PER-CLASS counter (`ArgOrdinalCounter` — GPR/FPR separate for an independent CC, flat for a slot-aligned one; `argSlotAligned` threaded from the CC like `dataModel`), so the payload is the per-class physical register ordinal and N pieces land in consecutive regs. (2) The `mir_verifier` bound changed from `argIndex < FnSig paramCount` to `argIndex < (number of physical `Arg` instructions in the function)` — sound because a per-class payload < its class count <= the total, and a flat payload < the total — so NO classifier/ABI threading into the verifier was needed (simpler than the planned "classifier threaded into mir_verifier"). The C1a caller + callee multi-register fail-loud guards were removed. **ALSO CLOSED `D-ML7-2.10`** (the per-class change fixes the latent mixed-class scalar-arg payload — a scalar param's payload is now its per-class index, not the param index). Runtime-witnessed x86_64-ELF: `{int,y,z}` 12B in rdi:rsi (exit 42, debug+release) + `{long,long}` 16B + the D-ML7-2.10 mixed int/double/int call (the double correctly in xmm0, exit 42). | `D-FC7-SYSV-STRUCT-RETURN-IN-REGS` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-16 (FC7 C1c, §B Option A, commit 1016d47).** A struct/union RETURNED by value now works across ALL SysV return classes. **§B (user) = Option A: a new MIR `ReturnPiece` opcode** (the caller-side mirror of `Arg`) for the multi-register capture — over (B) a side-table + post-regalloc memory synthesis or (C) sret-everything (ABI-non-conformant for ≤16B, rejected). **As-built:** (1) **callee** loads the eightbyte pieces and emits a MULTI-operand `Return` (maxOp bumped to N); the lir_callconv materialization moves each piece → `returnReg[class][per-class cursor]`. (2) **caller** (`emitStructReturningCall`): the struct Call's result IS piece 0 (returnReg ordinal 0 of its class) and each further eightbyte is a `ReturnPiece(call, ordinal)` read; all pieces store into the result slot `R` (a frame Alloca), and `R`'s address is the call's value (consumed by every aggregate-by-address consumer via the new `lowerLvalueAddress(Call)` arm). (3) **sret** (>16B MEMORY): a hidden result-pointer `Arg` (GPR ordinal 0, shifting the real params via the shared `ArgOrdinalCounter`) the callee copies the result through (`lowerByteWiseCopy`) + returns; no new opcode. (4) **MF-1 cycle-break** (BUILT — the arg path only REJECTS cycles, D-ML7-2.3): `emitParallelRegMoves` breaks a return-register 2-swap with a caller-saved scratch (≥3-cycle = AAPCS64 HFA, fails loud → C3). **Latent-crash fix:** `lowerFunction` copied the `interner.fnParams` SPAN into an owning vector — the sret/by-value `interner.pointer(…)` interning can REALLOCATE the pool and dangle a retained span (an interner-state-dependent "TypeId out of range"; also hardened the C1a/C1b struct-arg path). Verifier relaxed: a struct-returning func's Return may carry the first-class aggregate VALUE, N register pieces (I64/F64), or an sret Ptr. Runtime-witnessed x86_64-ELF exit 42 (reg-pair rax:rdx + sret + mixed {double;long} xmm0:rax, debug AND release). Pins: MF-2 callconv swap unit pin (pre-colored {rdx,rax}, value-correct sim) + 4 MIR pins (multi-Return shape, sret hidden-ptr, mixed-class split, call-once SF-2) + `struct_return_sysv` corpus. | `D-LIR-INT-MEMORY-WIDTH-EXACT` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-17 (array-storage cluster, branch p9, user §B "all widths, one cycle").** DISCOVERED by the array work's self-audit: integer memory access was 8-byte-wide for every int except `char` (`memAccessWidthFlags` returned width-default; the x86/arm64 schemas had only width-64 + width-8 mem variants), so a 64-bit load/store of a PACKED sub-8-byte element (array element or struct field) overran — `array_storage_index` CRASHED (ACCESS_VIOLATION) under the REAL release pipeline; FC7 struct-field writes were latently affected too. FIX (width-exact integer memory access): a new `kLirInstFlagWidth16` LIR flag; `memAccessWidthFlags` now returns the EXACT width per integer byte size (8: Char/I8/U8/Bool/Byte; 16: I16/U16; 32: I32/U32; default-64: I64/U64/Ptr — incl. `long`→I32 under LLP64); NEW width-32 + width-16 memory load/store encoder variants on BOTH targets (x86 `mov r32` 0x8B / `mov r16` 0x66 0x89 / `movzx r32,word` 0F B7; arm64 LDUR/STUR Wt + LDURH/STURH — no-index only, the index folds into the `lea`); the schema-loader accepts `width:16`. Also fixed the latent `lowerByteWiseCopy` I32-chunk overrun (it was silently a width-64 access). Witness tiers: int(32) RUNTIME-witnessed (`array_storage_index` exit 42, x86-PE/ELF + arm64 qemu, under the REAL release pipeline) + char(8) by the pre-existing `char_ptr_indexed`; I8/U8/Bool(8) + I16/U16(16) are BYTE-PINNED (`WidthAxisX86/Arm64.Int32And16MemFormsEmit*`) + fail-loud-safe — their VALUE codegen (Trunc/SExt/ZExt to/from sub-32) is the SEPARATE `D-CSUBSET-SUBNATIVE-ALU-FORMS` gap, so they cannot be runtime-exercised yet (no miscompile — they fail loud at value codegen). | `D-CSUBSET-INDEX-INTEGER-PROMOTION` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-22 (FC-deferral close-out loop cycle 4, branch p14).** A `char` subscript of a WIDE-element array/pointer (`int a[N]; char c; a[c]`) now integer-PROMOTES to `int` (C 6.3.1.1 / 6.5.2.1) BEFORE the index arithmetic. **As-built (small, front-end, the BEST-long-term placement — not a MIR band-aid):** the CST→HIR `Index` lowering (`cst_to_hir.cpp` ~1862) coerces a sub-int index via the SAME `integerPromotedType`+`coerce` the binary-op path uses (config-driven C 6.3.1; gated on `arith_.has_value()` so block-less toy/tsql are byte-identical) — so the HIR index node is already `int` and `scaleIndexToBytes` sees a promoted index. **`builder.makeIndex` has EXACTLY ONE call site** in all of `src/` (independently verified), so EVERY subscript — rvalue load, lvalue store, compound-assign, `&a[i]`, `a[i]++` — funnels through the one promoted chokepoint (no §A.5 multi-site miss). The crux is OVERFLOW: an un-promoted `(char)100 * 4` = 400 wraps mod 256 → reads/writes the WRONG element; promotion computes 400 at int width. Signedness preserved (signed `char`→SExt, unsigned→ZExt; a negative index sign-extends). int/long index untouched (`integerPromotedType` returns the same TypeId → no coerce). **Witnesses:** corpus `index_integer_promotion` exit 42 — char load AND char-indexed STORE both overflow-sensitive (`c=100`/`d=120`, value-divergent) + signed-char — on x86_64-PE (ctest) + x86_64-ELF (WSL) + arm64-ELF (qemu) [macho macos leg]; MIR pin `CharIndexIntegerPromotesToI32BeforeStrideMul` (the stride `Mul` is I32-typed, its lhs is the SExt/ZExt promotion not the raw char Arg) DEMONSTRATED red-on-disable (promotion off → inst-count 8→7, Mul Char-typed, example walls/overflows). Independent review VERIFIED-CLEAN. 365/365 ctest. **SHORT residual (orthogonal, fail-loud, NOT this anchor):** a `short` index promotes CORRECTLY (the cycle emits the SExt) but the I16 SExt/Trunc ENCODING is unrealized at the backend → loud `L_UnsupportedLoweringForOpcode` on x86 + arm64 — the separate sub-native I16-codegen gap `D-CSUBSET-32BIT-ALU-FORMS`/`D-CSUBSET-SUBNATIVE-ALU-FORMS`, NOT the promotion. — ORIGINAL: First need a `char`/`short`-typed subscript of a WIDE-element array/pointer (`int* a; a[c]` where `c` is `char`) to compile. DISCOVERED 2026-06-17 (array-storage cluster re-audit, NIT). Today FAIL-LOUD (NOT a miscompile — and strictly better than the pre-cycle SILENT scale-1 form): `scaleIndexToBytes` types the scaling `Mul(idx, stride)` at the index's OWN type (`hir.typeId(kids[1])`), so a `char` subscript makes a `Char`-typed Mul that walls at the Char-ALU gap (`D-CSUBSET-SUBNATIVE-ALU-FORMS`). Per C 6.3.1.1 the subscript should integer-PROMOTE to `int` before the index arithmetic — a pre-existing FRONT-END promotion gap the scaling faithfully reflects. `char`-index-of-`char`-array (stride 1, no Mul) and `int`-index both work. | (closed) | `cst_to_hir.cpp` Index lowering (integerPromotedType+coerce); `D-CSUBSET-32BIT-ALU-FORMS`/`D-CSUBSET-SUBNATIVE-ALU-FORMS` (the orthogonal I16-codegen gap blocking the short end-to-end); `D-MIR-STORAGE-ARRAY-INDEX-GEP` (the cycle that surfaced it) |

| `D-FFI-SHIPPED-LIB-PLATFORM-SELECT` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-09 — DISSOLVED by Model 3** (the `#include puts("hello")` 3-OS string-FFI capstone cycle). The per-platform-dir SELECTION problem this anchor tracked no longer exists: the 15 per-platform `shippedLibs/<os-arch>/<h>.json` descriptors were COLLAPSED into 5 **NEUTRAL** `shippedLibs/<h>.json`, each carrying platform-neutral signatures + a per-format **`library` MAP** `{pe,elf,macho}`; `shippedLibDirs` became the single neutral root `["shippedLibs"]`. The map is threaded target-AGNOSTICALLY through the front-end (descriptor→`ShippedExternSymbol`→`HirExternRecord`) and resolved to ONE library string per-target LATE, at `compile_pipeline.cpp` (via `objectFormatKindName(format.kind())`; missing key → `externLibraryByFormat` fallback; unknown key → fail loud) — so there is no longer a *directory* to pick by active target, and the front-end stays target-blind. This is **dissolution, NOT the registry's hinted per-dir platform-predicate remediation** (that fix is no longer needed — the platform axis moved INTO the neutral descriptor as the format-keyed library map). Cite: the Model-3 §B decision (plan-00 §0.2). — ORIGINAL trigger/context retained below. FF11 (2026-06-05, cycle 18+; was STILL OPEN after v0.0.2 V2-2 2026-06-06): the angle-form `#include <h>` system search path (`SemanticConfig.shippedLibDirs`) lists its platform EXPLICITLY (c-subset ships `["shippedLibs/windows-x86_64"]`, the only dir). Trigger = the FIRST time a SECOND platform's shipped-lib descriptors land (e.g. a `shippedLibs/linux-x86_64/` with a libc-flavored `stdio.json` descriptor) AND a single c-subset source must compile to BOTH — the resolver would then need to PICK the dir matching the active target (`ObjectFormatKind` / OS / arch) instead of searching every declared dir. Today: `applySystemDirs` (program.cpp) resolves EVERY `shippedLibDirs` entry and the resolver searches all of them, so a Windows + Linux shipped pair would both be on the path (first-match wins → wrong-platform descriptor could shadow). Priority: **normal** (the single-dir path is correct for the Win64-only corpus). UPDATE (2026-06-08, shippedLibs build-out): the `linux-x86_64` + `macos-arm64` descriptor sets NOW EXIST (stdio/stdlib/string/ctype/math each, all decode-validated by `AllShippedDescriptorsDecode`) — so the trigger's "a SECOND platform's descriptors land" half HAS fired. But they are STAGED data only: c-subset `shippedLibDirs` still lists ONLY `["shippedLibs/windows-x86_64"]`, so nothing is on the path to shadow and no source compiles to a non-Windows target yet. The REMAINING (unfired) trigger half is purely the resolver needing to SELECT the dir by active target. NOTE: V2-2 (2026-06-06) replaced the c-subset-source `stdio.h` with the neutral JSON descriptor (`D-FFI-SHIPPED-LIB-DESCRIPTOR-AGNOSTIC` ✅); the platform-select mechanism is unchanged. | Add a per-`shippedLibDirs`-entry platform predicate (e.g. `{ "dir": "shippedLibs/linux-x86_64", "format": "elf", "os": "linux" }`) OR derive the platform subdir from the active target spec at `applySystemDirs` time; the resolver then searches only the matching dir(s). Keep it config-driven (the language declares the platform axis; the engine selects) — NO `if (format == pe)` in the resolver. | `D-FFI-DESCRIPTOR-VARIADIC-SIGNATURE` | A shipped-lib descriptor (`shippedLibs/<platform>/*.json`, V2-2 2026-06-06) needs a VARIADIC function (e.g. `printf`) OR a signature form the shared `parseTypeFromText` codec does not yet accept. Today the hir-text `fn(...) -> ...` type grammar parses the param list + a trailing `cc` but has NO variadic marker, while the `FnSig` `isVariadic` scalar EXISTS in the IR but is not spellable in type-text — so a descriptor cannot express `printf`'s `(ptr<char>, ...)`. | `D-FFI-EXTERN-CALL-DISPATCH` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-08** — format-driven extern-call dispatch (the fix for a CONFIRMED latent x86_64-ELF FFI miscompile). The plan-lock proved byte-level that the ELF linker points an extern's `symbolVa` at its PLT STUB (code: `jmp [GOT]`), yet MIR→LIR unconditionally emitted `call_indirect_via_extern` (`FF 15` = `call [rip+disp32]`), dereferencing the stub's bytes as a function pointer → SIGSEGV. The extern-call shape is a property of the OBJECT FORMAT, not the CPU target (x86_64-PE vs x86_64-ELF need OPPOSITE opcodes). Fix: new closed enum `ExternCallDispatch` (`core/types/object_format_kind.hpp`) + a per-format `externCallDispatch` field on `ObjectFormatSchema` (`indirect-slot` = PE IAT / Mach-O __got, deref a pointer slot via `call_indirect_via_extern`; `direct-plt` = ELF, plain direct `call`/BL to the linker-synthesized PLT stub). `lowerToLir`/`lowerCall` selects the opcode from the active format's value as DATA — ZERO `if (arch/format == …)`; ELF needs NO new codegen opcode (reuses the existing `call`/BL→PLT-stub). The 4 live exec formats declare it (pe64 + macho64-x86_64 = `indirect-slot`; elf64-x86_64 + elf64-aarch64 = `direct-plt`). NOT validate-required (an exec format built for a non-FFI purpose may omit it); the real fail-loud is at LOWERING — a module with extern imports under a nullopt-dispatch format → `L_RequiredLirOpcodeMissing`; an unknown value → load fail-loud. Pins: `MirToLir.{ExternCallEmitsCallIndirectViaExternOpcode, ExternCallOnDirectPltFormatEmitsPlainCall, ExternImportsWithNoDispatchFailLoud, IndirectSlotWithoutOpcodeFailsLoud}` + the `extern_call_elf` runtime corpus (x86_64-ELF `abs` FFI → exit 42; RED-on-disable by flipping the ELF format to `indirect-slot`). | (closed) | plan 14 linker + plan 11 FFI |
| `D-FFI-PE-IMPORT-THUNK` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-07-05 (c112) — the pe64 leg's LAST run-green blocker: sqlite3.exe RUNS on Windows (`--version` 3.54.0 + full CRUD `SELECT sum`→62), so all 3 legs (win pe64 + linux x86_64 + arm64-qemu) now run real SQL.** The follow-up to `D-FFI-EXTERN-CALL-DISPATCH`: PE was the sole `indirect-slot` format, so `symbolVa[extern]` named the raw `.idata` IAT *data* slot. A DIRECT extern call worked (`call [IATslot]` derefs the slot), but an ADDRESS-TAKEN import (sqlite os_win.c `aSyscall[]` = a static-init array of `(SYSCALL)Win32Func` called indirectly) got the slot ADDRESS as a value → `call *reg` jumped INTO `.idata` and executed the pointer bytes as code → 0xC0000005 (no output). ELF/Mach-O ran the identical construct green because a `direct-plt` format points the extern's VA at a callable STUB (ELF PLT / Mach-O `__stubs`). FIX (user-chosen A; §B GO-WITH-FIXES design-audit, all 7 fixes folded): the PE walker synthesizes one `FF 25 disp32` import THUNK per extern at the tail of `.text` (`jmp *[IAT slot]` — the PE analog of Mach-O `__stubs`; `peThunkSizeFor`/`emitX86_64PeThunk`/`emitPeThunk` MIRROR `emitMachoStub`, machine-dispatched on 0x8664 with a fail-loud default), sets `symbolVa[extern]` = the THUNK VA (a `.text` code address, not the IAT slot), and flips `pe64-x86_64-windows-exec` `externCallDispatch` `indirect-slot`→`direct-plt` so every extern reference (call OR address-taken) is a callable address — PE now matches ELF/Mach-O (NO `if(format==)`; thunk block reserved before `.text` is sized, emitted after IAT VAs known; shared `applyExecRelocations` UNCHANGED). Pins: `PeExecFormatJson.ShippedPeExecIsDirectPlt` (host-independent format pin, mirrors `MachOArm64Exit.ShippedX86DarwinExecIsDirectPlt`) + `PeExecWriter.AddressTakenImportResolvesToTextThunkNotIdataSlot` (host-independent byte-scan: one `FF 25` thunk in `.text`, the extern call resolves to it, the thunk jumps into `.idata`; RED-on-disable=revert→resolves to `.idata`) + `examples/c-subset/addr_import` 3-leg runtime corpus (volatile-load fold-proof; PE 0xC0000005→exit 42; elf/arm64 already green). | (closed — sqlite3.exe run-green on Windows) | `D-FFI-EXTERN-CALL-DISPATCH` (parent dispatch enum); `D-LK6-8` (ELF PLT) + macho `__stubs` (mirror precedents); `D-RUNTIME-PE-MAIN-ARGS` (c111, prior pe64 blocker); plan 14 linker |
| `D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-FFI-ISEL` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-08** — the END-TO-END ARM64-ELF runnable FFI call-WITH-RESULT path is complete. **The gap was the `lea`/GlobalAddr lowering, NOT a "reg-move-class op"** (the D-FFI-EXTERN-CALL-DISPATCH cycle's first guess) — empirically re-confirmed this cycle: with the arm64 `lea` opcode disabled, BOTH the MIR→LIR fixture AND the `extern_call_elf` arm64 compile fail with the EXACT diagnostic `L_RequiredLirOpcodeMissing: target 'arm64' declares no 'lea' opcode (required for lowering MIR GlobalAddr)` — the raw `lowerToLir` lowers a `Call`'s callee `GlobalAddr` via `lowerGlobalAddr`→`lea` (the peephole that folds the symbol into the call's SymbolRef is an OPTIMIZED-path thing, absent in the raw lowering). The D-AS4-3 ARM64 `lea` (ADRP+ADD, commit 92386d3) supplied the missing opcode; this cycle PROVES the FFI path: (1) the MIR→LIR pin `MirToLir.Arm64ExternCallWithResultLowersUnderDirectPlt` (the dropped pin, reconstructed — lowers clean, 2 direct calls, 0 indirect; RED-on-disable demonstrated above), (2) the runnable corpus `examples/c-subset/extern_call_elf` gained an `arm64:elf64-aarch64-linux-exec` arm (compiles host-independently → valid AArch64 ELF; RUNS on the native `ubuntu-24.04-arm` CI leg + qemu via the cross-arch gate → exit 42). The ELF-aarch64 PLT/GOT (`emitArm64PltStub`, D-LK6-8 ✅) + the format-driven `direct-plt` dispatch (D-FFI-EXTERN-CALL-DISPATCH ✅) complete the chain. **⚠️ CORRECTION (2026-06-08, same-day next cycle): the "→ exit 42" RUNTIME claim above was an OVER-CLAIM** (exactly the runtime risk that cycle's own self-audit flagged). The compile-to-valid-AArch64-ELF half was real, but the binary SIGSEGV'd at runtime (CI exit 139; locally reproduced under qemu once the file's execute bit was set). Root cause = a SEPARATE codegen bug, NOT the FFI path: non-leaf ARM64 functions did not spill the link register x30, so `main`'s epilogue `ret` returned to a clobbered LR (an infinite self-loop overrunning the stack). The FFI dispatch itself was always correct — `abs(7-49)` returned 42 in x0. The corpus GENUINELY runs to exit 42 only after `D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-NONLEAF-LINK-REGISTER` (below) landed the x30 spill. | (closed — runtime corrected by the NONLEAF-LINK-REGISTER fix) | plan 14 (D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64 family); D-AS4-3 (the lea that closed the compile path); D-FFI-EXTERN-CALL-DISPATCH + D-LK6-8 (the PLT/dispatch chain); D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-NONLEAF-LINK-REGISTER (the x30 fix that made it actually run) |
| `D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-NONLEAF-LINK-REGISTER` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-08** — non-leaf ARM64 functions now spill + reload the link register x30. **This is the ACTUAL root cause of the arm64-FFI SIGSEGV (CI exit 139)** that `D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-FFI-ISEL`'s "→ exit 42" over-claimed away (the prior cycle's self-audit had flagged exactly this runtime risk). A calling convention that carries the return address in a LINK REGISTER (AAPCS64 x30) rather than pushing it on the stack (x86_64 `call`; callPushBytes=8) makes x30 live across the whole body of a non-leaf function — every `bl`/`call` clobbers it. The frame logic spilled the `calleeSaved` set (x19–x29) but NOT x30 (deliberately the `linkRegister`, NOT in `calleeSaved`, so it stays un-allocatable), so `main`'s epilogue `ret` returned to the clobbered LR (the address after the last call) → an infinite self-loop whose repeated epilogue `add sp` walked SP off the stack into a guard page → SIGSEGV. **The FFI dispatch was always correct** — `abs(7-49)` returned 42 in x0; the PLT stub (ADRP x16/LDR x17/BR x17) + the GLOB_DAT relocation both worked. **Fix** (`src/lir/lir_callconv.cpp::materializeOneFunc`, agnostic + config-driven): when `hasCalls && cc.linkRegister.has_value()`, fold the link register into `savedRegs` so the existing prologue/epilogue machinery spills it at entry + reloads it before `ret`. ZERO `if(arch/format==…)` — x86_64 (no `linkRegister`) takes the no-op path; the schema's long-declared `linkRegister` field (whose `target_schema.hpp` comment PROMISED "ML7 lowering checks linkRegister.has_value()") is finally consumed. **Pins**: `LirCallconv.NonLeafAarch64FunctionSpillsLinkRegister` (non-leaf SAVES x30 + leaf does NOT; RED-on-disable: revert the fold → x30 absent → fail) + `LirCallconv.NonLeafX8664FunctionHasNoLinkRegisterToSpill` (agnosticism control: x86_64 cc has no linkRegister → no-op path) + the `extern_call_elf` arm64 runtime corpus (now genuinely exit 42 under qemu + native-arm64; was SIGSEGV → CI red — so red-on-disable by construction). **+ HOST-INDEPENDENT BYTE-PIN (2026-06-08, same-day hardening)**: `LirCallconv.NonLeafAarch64FramePrologueEpilogueByteExact` drives the real production tail (legalizeTwoAddress → materializeCallingConvention → assemble) and byte-pins the ASSEMBLED non-leaf prologue+epilogue EXACT — incl. `stur x30,[sp,#16]` (f80103fe) at prologue offset 12 + `ldur x30,[sp,#16]` (f84103fe) reloaded before `ret` — against hand-verified ARM-ARM literals, plus a leaf-control (g spills x28/x29 but no `stur x30`). RED-on-disable DEMONSTRATED (disable the fold → frame 0x20→0x10 → both byte windows diverge). Closes the gap where the COMPOSED frame's byte-correctness was witnessed ONLY by the native-arm64 runtime leg (the per-instruction arm64 byte-pins prove instructions in isolation, never the composed frame). The THREE layers — structural (savedRegs, every leg) + this byte-pin (assembled bytes, every leg incl. Windows MSVC) + runtime corpus (exit 42, native-arm64 leg) — are complementary; none replaces another. 207/207 (no frame-size regression — x86_64 has no linkRegister so its frames are byte-identical; no arm64 non-leaf frame-size pin existed pre-fix). | (closed) | plan 14 (D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64 family); `D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-FFI-ISEL` (the over-claim this corrected); `D-LK10-ENTRY-ML7-FRAME-BIAS-UNIFY` (the frame substrate it extends); `target_schema.hpp` linkRegister field |
| `D-AS3-BLOCK-REL-IMM19/26` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-08** — AArch64 intra-function branch displacement resolution. The cycle-13.5 substrate (`BlockRelPatchKind { X86Rel32, Arm64Imm19, Arm64Imm26 }` on `BlockRelPatch`) left the two ARM64 arms as a fail-loud stub (`A_NoEncodingShapeWalker`); this cycle implements the real resolver in `src/asm/asm.cpp`. The displacement is PC-relative TO THE INSTRUCTION ITSELF (`disp = (target - patchOffset) >> 2`, NO +4 bias — unlike x86 rel32's relative-to-after-the-disp) and SCALED by 4 (branch targets are word-aligned); Imm19 (B.cond) occupies bits 5..23, Imm26 (B) bits 0..25. The resolver READ-MODIFY-WRITES only that bit-field (a `writeU32LEAt` would clobber the opcode/cond bits), masks the two's-complement displacement to the field width BEFORE the shift (negative-disp sign bits cannot bleed past the field), asserts 4-byte alignment (`A_NoMatchingEncodingVariant` on a non-multiple delta — never a silent low-bit drop), and signed-range-checks against the field width (`A_ImmediateOperandOutOfRange`; >reach → `D-CSUBSET-LONG-BRANCH` thunk is the future generalization). The fixed32 encoder selects `Arm64Imm19`/`Arm64Imm26` purely from `wire.slotKind` (config-driven; the new `EncodingSlotKind::Imm19={5,19}` added in lockstep) and queues a `BlockRelPatch` into `blockPatches`. ZERO `if(arch/format==…)` — the dispatch is on config-selected patch-kind DATA, symmetric with the x86 `X86Rel32` arm. **Pins**: `LirCallconv.Arm64ControlFlowSkeletonEncodesCmpBcondBWithResolvedOffsets` — a 6-word byte-exact pin through the real `assemble()` path covering forward Imm19 (+2), forward Imm26 (+3), and the **negative Imm26 back-edge** (−4 → `0x17FFFFFC`, two's-complement); RED-on-disable DEMONSTRATED (remove the `>>2` scaling → `0x14000003`→`0x1400000C` + `0x17FFFFFC`→`0x17FFFFF0`). **Runtime**: the `arm64_control_flow` while-loop corpus (exit 42) executes the resolved branches end-to-end — PROVEN LOCALLY under qemu-aarch64 (exit 42 ×3); the native `ubuntu-24.04-arm` CI leg (real arm64 hardware) CONFIRMED it GREEN — run 27170873148, 2026-06-08 (§A.5 cross-target runtime closure SATISFIED). | (closed — runtime CONFIRMED green on the native ubuntu-24.04-arm CI leg, run 27170873148) | plan 13 §AS3 (block-rel substrate, cycle-13.5); plan 14 (D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-CONTROL-FLOW); `D-CSUBSET-LONG-BRANCH` (the >reach thunk, still open) |
| `D-AS3-COND-CODE-ARM64` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-08** — AArch64's condition-code table + the generic cond-placement knobs. `arm64.target.json` now declares a `condCodeEncoding` table (10 entries: eq:0 ne:1 slt:11 sle:13 sgt:12 sge:10 ult:3 ule:9 ugt:8 uge:2) consumed by BOTH `jcc` (B.cond, the cond nibble at bits 0..3) AND `setcc` (CSET). The cycle generalized `condCodeFromPayload` with two NEW template fields — `condBitPos` (uint8, default 0) + `condInvert` (bool, default false) — so the SAME generic encoder line (`words[0] |= (condNib & 0x0F) << condBitPos`) serves x86 (the defaults → byte-identical to pre-knob) AND ARM64 B.cond (condBitPos=0) AND ARM64 CSET (condBitPos=12, condInvert=true: `CSET Xd,cond` = `CSINC Xd,XZR,XZR,invert(cond)`, the AArch64 cond-inversion `cond ^ 1`). ZERO `if(arch==…)` — the bit position + inversion are config DATA. Fail-loud: a variant declaring `condCodeFromPayload` on a schema with no `condCodeEncoding` table errors. **Pins**: `Arm64Encoder.CsetEncodesInvertedCondAtBits12` (cset x0,gt=`0x9A9FD7E0` GT 0xC→0xD; cset x0,eq=`0x9A9F17E0` EQ 0x0→0x1 — two conditions defeat a "constant nibble" bug; RED-on-disable DEMONSTRATED: disable `condNib ^= 1u` → 0xD7→0xC7) + `Arm64Encoder.ZextEncodesOrrW` (zext x0,w1=`0x2A0103E0`) + the B.cond cond-at-bit-0 path pinned via the skeleton's `b.sgt`=`0x5400004C`. **Runtime**: the `arm64_control_flow` corpus exercises cmp+jcc end-to-end (PROVEN LOCALLY under qemu, exit 42; native-arm64 CI CONFIRMED green, run 27170873148). Note: lowerCondBr FUSES the loop's ICmp into cmp+B.cond, so the separately-lowered setcc(CSET)/zext are emitted-but-dead in that corpus — their CORRECTNESS is pinned host-independently by the byte-tests, not the corpus. | (closed — runtime CONFIRMED green on the native ubuntu-24.04-arm CI leg, run 27170873148) | plan 13 §AS3 (cond-code table, cycle-13.5); pairs with `D-AS3-BLOCK-REL-IMM19/26` |
| `D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-CONTROL-FLOW` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-08** — the CONTROL-FLOW half of plan-14's combined `D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-CONTROL-FLOW + NON-LEAF` row (the NON-LEAF/x30 half closed 2026-06-08 by `D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-NONLEAF-LINK-REGISTER`). A c-subset function with `if`/`while`/loops now compiles + runs on ARM64: `cmp` (SUBS XZR,Rn,Rm — flags), `jcc` (B.cond imm19 → ifTrue + B imm26 → ifFalse, a target-blind 2-WORD MACRO via `fixedWords`+`wordIndex`), `jmp` (B imm26), `setcc` (CSET), `zext` (ORR Wd,WZR,Wm), and `alloca` (virtual → callconv materializes a frame-relative `lea` = ADD Xd,sp,#imm12) all land. | `D-OUTPUT-EXEC-BIT` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-24 (deferral loop iteration 1, branch feature/0-0-2-p16).** `writeImage` now sets the POSIX execute bits (owner/group/others, `std::filesystem::permissions(..., perm_options::add)`) on an executable-flavor output; `compile_pipeline::linkAndWrite` decides executability CONFIG-DRIVENLY via `ObjectFormatSchema::isImageFlavor()` (no arch/format identity branch — `writeImage` switches on a `bool executable = false`, staying format-blind). A rare chmod failure is a fail-loud WARNING `K_ImageExecBitFailed` (0x8014), NOT a write failure: the bytes are valid, the exec bit a best-effort convenience. No-op on Windows (PE ignores Unix modes). Pins: `LinkWriter.ExecutableOutputCarriesExecuteBitPosix` (#ifndef _WIN32 — red-on-disable BOTH ways: `true`→`+x` present, `false`→absent; the POSIX-CI-leg witness) + `LinkWriter.ExecutableWriteSucceedsEveryPlatform` (host-independent smoke, runs on the MSVC gate). `run_binary.hpp`'s test chmod kept as a now-no-op safety net (by its own design). — *Original row (audit trail):* The compiler writes the output executable (`src/link/writer.cpp`, the `--output` path) at the host umask default — mode 0644 on POSIX, NO execute bit. A user running the produced binary directly (`dss-code-prime --output foo; ./foo`) hits "Permission denied"/ENOEXEC (qemu's `prepare_binprm` rejects a file lacking `mode & 0111`; the kernel's execve too). NOT currently blocking: the examples/integrated test runners `chmod +x` the spawned binary before `posix_spawn` (`tests/test_support/run_binary.hpp`), so the corpus runs green on every CI leg. Discovered 2026-06-08 while root-causing the arm64-FFI failure — the 0644 mode masked the real x30 SIGSEGV under a *manual* `qemu-aarch64 <file>` invocation (ENOEXEC fired before any guest code ran). Trigger = the first non-test consumer running a `--output` binary directly, OR a decision to ship runnable-out-of-the-box output. Priority: **normal**. | When the output object-format is EXECUTABLE (`format.type == "exec"` — config-driven, read from the active format, NOT an arch/format identity branch), set the execute bits on the written file via `std::filesystem::permissions(path, perms::owner_exec \| perms::group_exec \| perms::others_exec, perm_options::add)` (portable; effectively a no-op on Windows where PE ignores Unix modes). | `D-LK1-ELF-EXEC-DATA-SECTIONS` | 🟡 **RODATA PATH CLOSED (rodata-only scope)** — the ELF ET_EXEC writer (`src/link/format/elf.cpp`) now emits a loadable `.rodata` section from `module.dataItems` (SHF_ALLOC, folded into the single R+X `.text` PT_LOAD via `shFlagsToPFlags`; data-symbol VAs added to the static `symbolVa` map so code→rodata relocations resolve through `applyExecRelocations`). The rodata-path runtime is now witnessed BOTH locally (WSL+qemu) AND on the authoritative native CI legs. **DYNAMIC-PATH ARM ALSO CLOSED (2026-06-09, the `#include puts` string-FFI capstone):** the `.rodata` emission was originally wired into the STATIC `encodeElfExec` writer ONLY; the capstone extended it to `encodeElfExecDynamic` (the dynamic-linked ELF exec path, which every libc-importing program now takes — string-literal args reach a DYNAMIC extern, and exit routes through libc) via the SAME shared `buildExecRodata`/`addDataSymbolVas` helper — byte-IDENTICAL when no rodata. So a string-literal pointer arg to a dynamic FFI call (`puts("hello")`) now lands its data in `.rodata` on the dynamic path too; runtime-proven by the `shipped_include_puts` corpus → stdout `"hello\n"` + exit 42 on linux-x86_64 (WSL) AND linux-arm64 (qemu). **WRITABLE PATH CLOSED 2026-06-19** (by `D-LK4-DATA-PRODUCER-MUTABLE-GLOBAL`): writable `.data` + zero-fill `.bss` now emit into a SEPARATE 2nd R+W PT_LOAD (W^X; bss extends p_memsz not p_filesz), on BOTH the static + dynamic ELF arms — runtime-proven (`global_write` exit 42 x86_64-ELF WSL + arm64-ELF qemu). **STILL DEFERRED:** the data→data dataItem-reloc path (`D-LK1-ELF-RODATA-DATAITEM-RELOC`). Historical context — the original blocker: the ELF ET_EXEC writer emitted only `.text`/`.symtab`/`.strtab`/`.shstrtab` — NO data section. So a module-level data global (`int g = 42;`) could not reach an ELF executable. This is the blocker for a RUNNABLE ARM64 `lea` corpus: the D-AS4-3 ARM64 `lea` (ADRP+ADD) encoder is built + proven by byte-pins (`Arm64Encoder.Lea*`) + the linker reloc-formula tests (`test_aarch64_reloc_formulas.cpp`), but an end-to-end `static int g=42; int *p=&g; return *p;` corpus that exercises lea→load→exit-42 needs `g` in a loadable data section (and a 2nd R+W PT_LOAD), which the static ET_EXEC path lacks. Same gap affects x86_64-ELF data globals (the format-dispatch cycle's `extern_call_elf` corpus avoided strings for exactly this reason). NOTE (2026-06-08): the FFI direct-call path that REQUIRES the lea to COMPILE now runs end-to-end (`extern_call_elf` arm64 arm → `D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-FFI-ISEL` ✅ CLOSED) — but that exercises the lea on the COMPILE path only (the lea materializes `&abs` yet the direct BL targets the symbol via the PLT, so the lea's runtime RESULT is dead there). OBSERVING the lea's runtime VALUE still needs either this data-global deref path OR an indirect call through a function POINTER (`D-ML7-2.4`, a separate isel gap). **UPDATE 2026-06-12 (FC4 c2): the fn-pointer option LANDED — `D-ML7-2.4` closed; the `fnptr_call`/`fnptr_callback` arm64-ELF arms BLR through an ADRP+ADD-materialized `&helper` at RUNTIME (qemu exit 42), so the arm64 lea's runtime VALUE is now observed end-to-end.** Priority: **normal** (the lea ENCODER, the user-directed deliverable, is complete + strongly pinned; only the lea's runtime-VALUE observation is gated). | Extend the ELF ET_EXEC writer to lay out a `.rodata`/`.data` section with the module's `AssembledData` bytes, assign each data symbol a VA, add a 2nd page-aligned PT_LOAD (R[+W]), and let the existing relocation applier patch code→data references. Then reuse `global_int`-style sources (`int g=42; return g;`) with an `arm64:elf64-aarch64-linux-exec` target arm under the qemu/native cross-arch gate → exit 42 proves lea→load end-to-end. | plan 14 LK1 (ELF exec data sections); pairs with `D-AS4-3` (the lea encoder it would make runnable) + the `D-LK4-RODATA-PRODUCER-*` family (the constant-encoding walker) |

| `D-LK1-MACHO-RODATA-DATAITEM-RELOC` | First Mach-O `__const` rodata item carrying its OWN relocation (a data→data reference — e.g. a const pointer table / 8-byte rodata pointer slot). **F5 UPDATE (2026-06-25):** `exec_data_section.hpp` now PATCHES such relocs in-place (`applyDataItemRelocations`, `allowItemRelocations=true`), but `macho.cpp` then fails loud (`K_NoMatchingObjectFormat`) on any abs64 site collected from `__TEXT,__const` — because that segment is read-execute + code-signed and dyld CANNOT PIE-rebase it (a relocated pointer is inherently load-writable). | `D-LK1-MACHO-X8664-DARWIN-DATA-SECTION` | The `macho64-x86_64-darwin-exec` format was NOT given a `__const` row / `supportedDataSections` this cycle (only `macho64-arm64-darwin-exec` was). | `D-LK-RODATA-HELPER-PE-PARITY` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-24 (deferral loop, branch feature/0-0-2-p16) — ALREADY-SATISFIED (stale-open row), verified this cycle.** PE was retrofitted onto the shared helper by the **D-LK4-DATA-PRODUCER** cycle: `pe.cpp` calls `buildExecDataSection` (660-677) + `addDataSymbolVas` (921-938) for ALL three section kinds — NO inline rodata→symbolVa loop remains (the premise of this row is stale). **M1** (anonymous-`SymbolId{}` skip) is handled by `addDataSymbolVas` and chokepoint-tested via `test_elf_exec_writer.cpp:2107` (PE inherits it by-construction through the shared chokepoint). **H1** (over-aligned item) is **STRUCTURALLY IMPOSSIBLE** for PE, not merely masked: the `Alignment` type CAPS at 256 bytes (`alignment.hpp` `fromBytes`/`of<N>` reject > 256) while PE `sectionAlignment` is ≥ page (4096), so a section's `maxAlign` can NEVER exceed its alignment — a `checkMaxAlign` fail-loud guard would be untestable dead code (no constructible over-aligned item). Verified the live code state directly; no honest code or test to add. — *Original row (audit trail):* PE (`src/link/format/pe.cpp`) is NOT yet converted to the shared `src/link/format/exec_data_section.hpp` helper (`buildExecRodata` + `addDataSymbolVas`) — elf.cpp + macho.cpp are. Plan-lock chose to DEFER PE (Option b): PE is the Windows-critical-path runtime and its latent H1 (max-item-align) is MASKED by page-aligned `.rdata`, and its M1 (anonymous-symbol-skip) is dormant — so retrofitting it carries Windows-runtime risk for no current correctness gain. Priority: **normal** (DRY/maintainability + closes PE's latent H1/M1; not a correctness bug today). | Retrofit `pe.cpp`'s inline rodata→symbolVa loop onto `buildExecRodata`/`addDataSymbolVas` (this ALSO fixes PE's latent H1 over-aligned-item + M1 anonymous-item gaps). Trigger: the next PE-touching cycle, OR a producer ever emits an anonymous / over-aligned data item (which would surface PE's H1/M1 as a real bug). Supersedes the residual-consumer half of `D-LK4-RODATA-WALKER-RELOC-EXTENSION-HOIST`. | plan 14 LK1/LK2-RODATA; residual of `D-LK4-RODATA-WALKER-RELOC-EXTENSION-HOIST` (the hoist's 3rd consumer); shares `exec_data_section.hpp` with the ELF + Mach-O arms |

| `D-LK6-AARCH64-ADDABSLO12-HIGH-VA` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-09 — RUNTIME-PROVEN on Apple Silicon** (run **27192415923**, same witness as `D-LK1-MACHO-EXEC-DATA-SECTIONS`: the `macos-clang-release` leg ran `global_int` macos-arm64 → ctest **#184 Passed** → exit 42, which means the high-VA ADD_ABS_LO12_NC reloc RESOLVED at runtime — else exit ≠ 42). Cited at `exec_reloc_apply.hpp` `Aarch64AddAbsLo12`. The ADD_ABS_LO12_NC ("No Check") reloc applier carried an ELF-centric `S+A ≤ UINT32_MAX` upper bound that WRONGLY rejected valid Mach-O PIE VAs (which sit above the 4 GiB `__PAGEZERO`, e.g. 0x1'0000'4040) — it blocked the macOS-arm64 data-global access path (`global_int` → `__const`). Root cause: `(S+A) & 0xFFF` is a magnitude-INDEPENDENT low-12 extraction (the uint32 cast cannot perturb the low 12 bits), and the address magnitude is range-checked by the PAIRED ADRP companion (`adr_prel_pg_hi21`, signed-21-bit page delta) — so the ADD itself needs no upper bound. A code-correctness relaxation, byte-pinned host-independently by `Aarch64AddAbsLo12.ResolvesSplusAAboveUint32Max` (`test_aarch64_reloc_formulas.cpp`) + `MachOArm64Exit.MachoArm64ConstAdrpAddLeaHighVaResolvesLowTwelve` (`test_macho_arm64_exit.cpp`), with RED-on-disable demonstrated (restore the `> UINT32_MAX` clause → the high-VA pins fail). The relaxation is confirmed NO-OP for ELF/PE (their VAs are < UINT32_MAX) by the `linux-gcc-release` + `linux-clang-asan` + `linux-arm64-gcc-release` + `windows-msvc-release` legs of run 27192415923 all staying GREEN. | (closed) — dropped the `S+A > UINT32_MAX` clause; kept `S+A ≥ 0` (a negative VA is nonsensical). RUNTIME witness = run 27192415923 `macos-clang-release` #184 (`global_int` macos-arm64 → exit 42). | plan 14 LK6; macOS data-section cycle; runtime witness shared with `D-LK1-MACHO-EXEC-DATA-SECTIONS` |

| `D-FFI-ANGLE-INCLUDE-LINE-SCOPED-HEADER` | A UX pass on include diagnostics, OR a header name legitimately needing multi-token content. Priority: **normal** (fail-loud today — a malformed `#include <foo` is reported, see `tests/tokenizer/test_tokenizer.cpp::FF11MalformedAngleIncludeNoCloserFailsLoud`; only the diagnostic flavor + consumption scope are deferred polish). | A malformed `#include <foo` (no closing `>`) currently runs the coalescing `header-body` mode to EOF and reports the generic `P_UnterminatedString` (matching `string`-body semantics — `header-body` mirrors the `string` body: coalesced `defaultToken`, `endsAt: ">"`, no `popAtNewline`). The long-term polish is a header-specific unterminated flavor (a new `UnterminatedFlavor::Header` → a dedicated `P_*` code) PLUS line-scoped termination (stop the header body at the newline, like `popAtNewline`) so the error is header-specific AND the rest of the file is not consumed past the directive line. Do NOT re-engineer this cycle (scope creep) — the current behavior is consistent established fail-loud, NOT a regression. | FF11 angle-include (`c-subset.lang.json` `include-directive`/`header-body` modes); pairs with the general `popAtNewline` capability; do NOT cite in `src/` (future-work pin only) |
| `D-FFI-CROSS-HEADER-ODR-FIDELITY` | Full C ODR fidelity becomes a goal, OR a corpus surfaces two included headers declaring the same name as DISTINCT symbols. Priority: **normal** (rare — the common case of two headers declaring the SAME `extern` is correctly idempotent). | FF11 goal-2 flags a PROGRAM `extern` conflicting with an INCLUDED header's decl (`S_RedeclaredSymbol`), but NOT the header-vs-header case: two included headers each declaring the same name as DISTINCT symbols currently last-writer-wins silently (idempotent cross-tree `injectBinding` visibility — deliberately not flagged, correct for FF11's program-vs-header scope). Closing work = extend the cross-tree redeclaration check to also flag header-vs-header same-name conflicts (distinct symbols), leaving the program-vs-header path + the same-symbol idempotent case unchanged. | FF11 goal-2 (`semantic_analyzer.cpp` cross-tree redeclaration loop); surfaced by the cycle-21 self-audit; do NOT cite in `src/` (future-work pin only) |
| `D-FFI-STDINT-PTR-WIDTH-ILP32` | The first ILP32 (32-bit-pointer) target lands (e.g. i386 / armv7 / wasm32). Today EVERY DSS exec target is 64-bit (x86_64-PE/ELF, arm64-ELF/Mach-O) and LP64 + LLP64 agree on pointer width (8 bytes), so the pointer-width + greatest-width typedefs in the neutral `stdint.json`/`stddef.json` (`intptr_t`/`uintptr_t`/`intmax_t`/`uintmax_t`/`size_t`/`ptrdiff_t`) are correctly i64/u64. Priority: **normal** (trigger-gated — the 64-bit-only values are correct for every current target; first surfaced by the p18 SQLite-readiness Cluster G headers cycle as the FIRST consumer of the descriptor typedef path). | When an ILP32 target is added, the pointer-width typedefs (`intptr_t`/`uintptr_t`/`size_t`/`ptrdiff_t`) must become 4-byte for THAT target while staying 8-byte on the 64-bit ones. A single literal hir-text typedef can't express "pointer-width" across both ABIs, so the close is a per-target width resolution: the descriptor declares the typedef as a width-CLASS the semantic phase resolves against the active target's `dataModel`/pointer width (NOT an `if (target == i386)` in the engine — the descriptor/loader declares the width axis, the engine reads it). Pin: an ILP32 target compiles a program asserting `sizeof(intptr_t)==4` while a 64-bit target sees 8. | cited in `src/dss-config/shippedLibs/{stdint,stddef}.json` ($comment); pairs with `D-LANG-PLATFORM-DEPENDENT-PRIMITIVE-WIDTH` + `D-FFI-WCHAR-WIDTH` (both "a descriptor baked an ABI/platform width") + `D-FFI-STDINT-LIMIT-MACROS` (the width-dependent *_MAX inherit this); SQLite-readiness Cluster G (p18) |
| `D-FFI-STDINT-LIMIT-MACROS` | A program references a `<stdint.h>` limit macro — `INT8_MAX`/`INT64_MIN`/`UINT32_MAX`/`SIZE_MAX`/`INTPTR_MAX`/etc. Today the neutral `stdint.json` ships ONLY the typedefs (no `constants` surface), so a direct limit-macro reference fails loud as an undefined identifier (never silent). Priority: **normal** (trigger-gated — SQLite's amalgamation mostly self-defines these via `#if !defined(...)`, but a direct reference would need them; first noted p18 Cluster G). | Add a `constants` surface to `stdint.json` carrying the *_MAX/*_MIN integer macros (INT8_MIN=-128 … INT64_MAX=9223372036854775807, the UINT*_MAX, plus SIZE_MAX/PTRDIFF_MIN/PTRDIFF_MAX/INTPTR_*/INTMAX_*), each integer-typed (rides as i64/u64 via the descriptor `constants` mechanism). The pointer-width + greatest-width limits (SIZE_MAX/INTPTR_MAX/INTMAX_MAX) are 64-bit-target values that inherit the ILP32 deferral [[D-FFI-STDINT-PTR-WIDTH-ILP32]]. Pin: a program using `INT32_MAX` compiles and the value is byte-exact. | cited in `src/dss-config/shippedLibs/stdint.json` ($comment); pairs with `D-FFI-STDINT-PTR-WIDTH-ILP32` (width-dependent limits) + the descriptor `constants` mechanism (FC14 item-1, cf. `limits.json`); SQLite-readiness Cluster G (p18) |
| `D-FFI-WCHAR-WIDTH` | A program needs `wchar_t` at its platform-correct width — 16-bit on Windows (PE), 32-bit on POSIX/Linux+macOS (ELF/Mach-O). The neutral `stddef.json` ships `wchar_t = i32` (the Linux+macOS width); on a PE/Windows target the conforming C width is 16-bit. Priority: **normal** (trigger-gated — SQLite is UTF-8/`char` internally and uses no `wchar_t`, so the i32 default is correct for the Linux+macOS deliverables and no current corpus exercises it; first noted p18 Cluster G). | Make `wchar_t`'s width per-target (2 bytes on PE/Windows, 4 on ELF/Mach-O) via the SAME per-target width resolution as [[D-FFI-STDINT-PTR-WIDTH-ILP32]] (a `dataModel`/format-keyed typedef value the semantic phase resolves against the active target — NOT an `if (format == pe)` in the engine). Pin: a Windows-target program sees `sizeof(wchar_t)==2`, a Linux-target one sees `4`. | cited in `src/dss-config/shippedLibs/stddef.json` ($comment); pairs with `D-FFI-STDINT-PTR-WIDTH-ILP32` + `D-LANG-PLATFORM-DEPENDENT-PRIMITIVE-WIDTH`; SQLite-readiness Cluster G (p18) |
| `D-FFI-OFFSETOF-MACRO` | A program references `offsetof(type, member)` from `<stddef.h>`. Today `stddef.json` ships `size_t`/`ptrdiff_t`/`wchar_t`/`NULL` but NOT `offsetof` (a function-like macro — no descriptor surface for it yet), so an `offsetof` reference fails loud. Priority: **normal** (trigger-gated — SQLite uses `offsetof` in a few spots, so this may fire during the SQLite compile; first noted p18 Cluster G). | `offsetof` is the function-like macro `((size_t)&((type*)0)->member)`. The cleanest agnostic home is a `__builtin_offsetof`-style intrinsic the semantic phase recognizes and const-folds to the member's layout byte-offset via the EXISTING FC6 aggregate-layout machinery (exact, no UB null-pointer arithmetic) — preferred over (b) shipping a textual function-like macro in the descriptor (which needs a function-like-macro surface the descriptor schema lacks today). Pin: `offsetof(struct S, b)` const-folds to the correct byte offset for a known-layout struct. | cited in `src/dss-config/shippedLibs/stddef.json` ($comment); pairs with the FC6 aggregate-layout offset computation + the descriptor `typedefs`/`constants` mechanism; SQLite-readiness Cluster G (p18) |
| `D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-MISCOMPILE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 Cluster G c2 — ROOT CAUSE = INLINING a variadic callee).** A variadic function SILENTLY MISCOMPILED under the RELEASE optimizer pipeline. Minimal repro (`examples`-shaped): `static int vsum(int n, ...){ va_list ap; int acc=0,i; va_start(ap,n); for(i=0;i<n;i=i+1) acc=acc+va_arg(ap,int); va_end(ap); return acc; } int main(void){ return vsum(3,10,13,19); }` → **baseline (debug pipeline) exit 42 (CORRECT); release (`--config=release`) exit 0 (WRONG)** on x86_64-PE (reproduced HEAD 0e3a550, `build/bin/dss/Release`). **Priority: HIGH — correctness-critical, silent miscompile.** BLOCKS SQLite-green RELEASE: SQLite is variadic-heavy (`sqlite3_mprintf`/`sqlite3_snprintf`/`sqlite3VXPrintf`/its test harnesses). ROOT of the blind spot: FC12 shipped the variadic feature BASELINE-ONLY (its corpus carried no `{"shippedPipeline":"release"}` arm), so the optimizer×`va_list` composition was NEVER witnessed — exactly the masked-effectiveness trap the dss-cycle `release`-arm corpus rule exists to prevent. | ✅ (CLOSED) ROOT CAUSE = the INLINER inlined the static single-call variadic callee into `main`; the spliced `va_start` leaves (`VaRegSaveAreaAddr`/`VaOverflowArgAreaAddr`/`VaHomeArgAreaAddr`) bound to MAIN's frame (which never spilled the varargs) → `ap` read garbage. FIX = `inlineLegalityGate` (`src/opt/passes/inlining.cpp`) refuses any callee whose body contains one of those three va_start leaves — the universal "a variadic fn that calls va_start is not inlinable" rule; agnostic (MIR opcodes only), sibling of the `RecvByValueStackParam` refusal. PINS (both red-on-disable): `tests/opt/test_inlining.cpp::VariadicCalleeCallingVaStartIsNotInlined` (callsInlined==0) + corpus `examples/c-subset/varargs_inline_release` (release arm exit 42, PE-runnable). ★ Closing this surfaced 2 MORE variadic-release optimizer bugs the FC12 BASELINE-ONLY corpus masked (a CLUSTER, NOT a single bug) → [[D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-MEM2REG-PHI]] + [[D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-ARGINDEX]]; the broad "add a `release` arm to EVERY variadic example" closure follows each fix (this cycle adds only `varargs_inline_release` — the other arms stay off until their bug lands). | CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 c2); cited in `src/opt/passes/inlining.cpp` (gate refusal) + `tests/opt/test_inlining.cpp` + `examples/c-subset/varargs_inline_release/`; pairs with `D-OPT7-INLINE-FRAME-SENSITIVE-INTRINSIC` (the hypothetical-intrinsic sibling — va_start in DSS is these dedicated MIR leaves, not an IntrinsicCall) + `D-FFI-DESCRIPTOR-VARIADIC-SIGNATURE` + the FC12 variadic cycle + the dss-cycle `release`-arm corpus discipline |
| `D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-MEM2REG-PHI` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 Cluster G c3) — was the variadic SYMPTOM of a GENERAL Mem2Reg bug; fixed together as [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-LOOP-BODY-LOCAL-DEAD-PHI]].** Compiling `examples/c-subset/varargs_win64_sum` under RELEASE aborted FAIL-LOUD `Mem2Reg fatal: phi ... has no reaching value from predecessor`. ★ The c3 PROBE OVERTURNED the scope: it is NOT Win64/variadic-specific — the trigger is the `int iv = va_arg(ap,int); double dv = va_arg(ap,double);` LOOP-BODY-LOCALS, and a minimal NON-variadic `int f(int n){int t=0,i=0;while(i<n){int iv=i*2;t=t+iv;i=i+1;}return t;}` reproduces the IDENTICAL fatal. The variadic example was just the FIRST to exercise it under release (FC12 shipped the variadic corpus baseline-only). | ✅ (CLOSED) FIXED by [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-LOOP-BODY-LOCAL-DEAD-PHI]] (semi-pruned SSA — see that row for the mechanism). `varargs_win64_sum` gained a `{"shippedPipeline":"release"}` arm (exit 39, was Mem2Reg-fatal); the general witness is `examples/c-subset/loop_body_local`. | CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 c3); subsumed by [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-LOOP-BODY-LOCAL-DEAD-PHI]]; pairs with [[D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-MISCOMPILE]] (the inlining sibling) + [[D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-ARGINDEX]] (the still-open 3rd cluster member) |
| `D-OPT-MEM2REG-DEAD-PHI-PRUNE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 Cluster G c3 — the COMPLETE fix; HIGH, GENERAL Mem2Reg correctness bug).** Under the RELEASE pipeline Mem2Reg ABORTED FAIL-LOUD (`phi at block ... has no reaching value from predecessor`) whenever a promoted alloca got a DEAD phi at an IDF block where it was not LIVE but its incoming was undefined. TWO classes: (1) a loop-BODY-LOCAL (`while(){ int x=expr; use(x); }`, dead at the header) — the first-found symptom [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-LOOP-BODY-LOCAL-DEAD-PHI]]; (2) the SUBTLER NESTED-LOOP case — an inner counter `j` re-initialized each OUTER iteration is LIVE across the inner back-edge yet DEAD at the OUTER header. Class (2) (and a single loop whose body contains an `if`-merge) crashes with ZERO body-locals → an ENORMOUS class of ordinary C (nested loops saturate SQLite). The c3 pr-review's RUNTIME battery caught (2) after the initial semi-pruned commit (ecf40c3) only handled (1) — the green-but-incomplete trap; upgraded to the complete fix the same cycle. | ✅ (CLOSED) FIX = FULLY-PRUNED SSA (Choi/Cytron/Sarkar) in `src/opt/passes/mem2reg.cpp`: place a phi for alloca A at IDF block S ONLY IF A is LIVE-IN at S (a backward live-in dataflow: `live_in[B]=use[B] ∪ (live_out[B]\def[B])`, use=upward-exposed Load, def=Store, alloca-site NOT a def). Strictly stronger than semi-pruned (upward-exposure): a name DEAD at one IDF block but live elsewhere (the nested counter) is pruned THERE specifically. PROVABLY SAFE: every KEPT phi is at a block where A is live → a needed merge is never pruned (no miscompile, verified by a base==release battery: diamond/induction/nested/triple-nested/body-local-live-across all correct on both pipelines). PRESERVES fail-loud: a genuine uninitialized read IS live-in at its use → phi kept → still aborts (verified). PINS (red-on-disable): `tests/opt/test_mem2reg.cpp::{LoopBodyLocalAllocaNeedsNoPhi, NestedLoopInnerCounterNoOuterHeaderPhi}` + corpus `examples/c-subset/{loop_body_local (exit 20), nested_loop_release (exit 4)}` release arms. Agnostic (MIR/SSA only). | CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 c3); cited in `src/opt/passes/mem2reg.cpp` (the live-in gate) + `tests/opt/test_mem2reg.cpp` + `examples/c-subset/nested_loop_release/`; subsumes [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-LOOP-BODY-LOCAL-DEAD-PHI]] (class 1); pairs with the Choi/Cytron/Sarkar pruned-SSA literature |
| `D-OPT-MEM2REG-CONDITIONAL-INIT-UNDEF` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-07-07 (post-sqlite C23+perf arc, cycle 1) — the RELEASE-pipeline Mem2Reg abort on benign CONDITIONAL-INIT; the blocker to `--config=release` sqlite.** Root: Mem2Reg's rename walk `std::abort()`'d whenever a promoted alloca had NO reaching value at a phi-incoming edge (`mem2reg.cpp:627`) or a Load (`:599`) — a LIVE-but-conditionally-defined local (`int x; if(c) x=1; return x+c;`) or a dead-path uninit read. Both are VALID C (gcc compiles sqlite, full of them); p18 [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-DEAD-PHI-PRUNE]] deliberately "preserved the fatal" (its comment), which was WRONG — a compiler must compile valid C. DISCOVERED by the T1.0 perf-profiling probe: sqlite-green was only ever verified in the DEFAULT (debug) config, which runs no Mem2Reg; `--config=release` aborted at the first sqlite conditional-init (block 1492). FIX (agnostic, MIR/SSA only): materialize undef-as-zero for the missing incoming — a new `ReachingValue::Kind::ZeroConst` (value = element TypeId.v), ONE `Const 0` per element type emitted in the ENTRY block (dominates every edge → verifier-legal incoming everywhere; entry is `selectBlocks[0]` so it precedes any Load resolve). GPR-Const-zeroable element types stay PROMOTED (the common case, no perf loss); FPR (float — no float-immediate) + aggregates have no scalar zero → the alloca is DE-PROMOTED (left as memory = what debug does; detected PRE-walk via `liveIn[entry]` = read-before-write), a narrow perf loss pinned [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-FPR-CONDITIONAL-INIT-RODATA-ZERO]]. Uninit-read DIAGNOSTIC responsibility moves to a frontend warning [[D-SEMANTIC-MAYBE-UNINITIALIZED-WARN]]. Independent design-audit GO-WITH-FIXES (caught the float-`Const`-poison blocker → the de-promotion; resetPerFunction clears + fail-loud-on-miss — all folded). WITNESSES: 3 red-on-disable units (`ConditionallyInitializedLiveAllocaZeroFillsUndefEdge` [phi zero-fill + MirVerifier dominance] / `...LoadZeroFillsUninitPath` / `...FloatAllocaIsDepromoted`) + 2 release-arm corpus (`examples/c-subset/cond_init_release`→2, `cond_init_float_release`→1) + the 2-TU sqlite `--config=release` compile clears the Mem2Reg wall + the minimal repro `int f(int c){int x;if(c)x=1;return x+c;}`+`main(argc)`→exit 2. | ✅ (CLOSED) | post-sqlite C23+perf arc cycle 1 (2026-07-07); `src/opt/passes/mem2reg.cpp` + `tests/opt/test_mem2reg.cpp` + `examples/c-subset/{cond_init_release,cond_init_float_release}`; discovered by T1.0 profiling; pairs with [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-DEAD-PHI-PRUNE]] (complements the p18 dead-phi prune) |
| `D-OPT-MEM2REG-FPR-CONDITIONAL-INIT-RODATA-ZERO` | ⏳ **GATED (perf; opened 2026-07-07 by [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-CONDITIONAL-INIT-UNDEF]]).** A CONDITIONALLY-INITIALIZED FLOAT/aggregate local is DE-PROMOTED (left as memory) at the missing-incoming site because a float has no directly-lowerable zero `Const` (register machines have no float-immediate; DSS routes float constants through rodata `GlobalAddr+Load`) and aggregates have no scalar zero. CORRECT but a minor perf loss (those allocas stay in memory under release; rare — most floats are init-before-use). Trigger: a profile shows conditionally-initialized float promotion matters. Resolution: mirror the HIR→MIR float-literal promotion (`hir_to_mir.cpp:559-578`) — mint an anonymous rodata `MirGlobal` holding the zero bit-pattern + `GlobalAddr`+`Load` in the entry block — so FPR conditional-init allocas promote too; fail-loud-in-place for F16/F128 (no encodings). | (gated — perf refinement; de-promotion is correct today) | post-sqlite C23+perf arc; `src/opt/passes/mem2reg.cpp` (the de-promotion loop) + the `hir_to_mir.cpp` float-promotion precedent; plan 12 MIR/LIR optimizer |
| `D-SEMANTIC-MAYBE-UNINITIALIZED-WARN` | ⏳ **GATED (opened 2026-07-07 by [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-CONDITIONAL-INIT-UNDEF]]).** Removing the Mem2Reg abort on conditional-init (a compiler must compile valid C) dropped the incidental "genuine uninitialized read" signal it provided. Its correct home is a FRONTEND/semantic WARNING (gcc/Clang's `-Wmaybe-uninitialized`), not a hard optimizer abort — a promoted automatic scalar Load not dominated by any Store, no address taken. Trigger: a maybe-uninitialized diagnostic is prioritized (or a corpus wants it). Resolution: a semantic-tier maybe-uninitialized warning. NOT a blocker — silently materializing undef-as-zero is conforming (LLVM's mem2reg does the same; the diagnostic is a frontend concern). | (gated — a diagnostic-quality improvement, non-blocking) | post-sqlite C23+perf arc; `src/semantic/` (frontend); the mem2reg.cpp comment records the move |

| `D-OPT-MEM2REG-LOOP-BODY-LOCAL-DEAD-PHI` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 c3) — ★ SUPERSEDED by [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-DEAD-PHI-PRUNE]] (the COMPLETE fix).** The SEMI-PRUNED fix this row first described (commit ecf40c3, gate phi placement on UPWARD-EXPOSURE) was INSUFFICIENT: the c3 pr-review's runtime battery found NESTED loops still crashed (a name DEAD at one IDF block but live elsewhere — upward-exposure cannot prune that); upgraded to FULLY-PRUNED (live-in) the SAME cycle. The loop-body-local class IS fixed by the general fix. Original c3 record (the first-found symptom):** GENERAL Mem2Reg correctness bug — HIGH, was masked. Under the RELEASE pipeline, Mem2Reg ABORTED FAIL-LOUD (`phi at block ... has no reaching value from predecessor ... uninit/unreachable input`) on ANY function with a local declared AND used entirely inside a LOOP BODY (`while (...) { int x = expr; use(x); }`) — an enormous, ordinary class of C (it would have blocked vast swaths of SQLite). ROOT: minimal (un-pruned) SSA placed a DEAD phi for the block-local at the loop HEADER (the body-Store's iterated dominance frontier reaches the header via the back-edge); that phi's entry-predecessor incoming was genuinely undefined (the slot was never stored before the loop) → the rename walk's empty-stack guard aborted. Surfaced (re-scoped) from the variadic symptom [[D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-MEM2REG-PHI]] by the c3 probe (a non-variadic `while(){int iv=...}` reproduces it). Was masked because release-arm corpus examples never declared a loop-body-local (the dss-cycle masked-effectiveness trap, again). | ✅ (CLOSED) FIX = SEMI-PRUNED SSA (Briggs/Cooper) in `src/opt/passes/mem2reg.cpp`: gate phi PLACEMENT on UPWARD-EXPOSURE — only place a phi for an alloca read-before-written in SOME block (a "global" name). A block-local (Store-before-Load in its block) is not upward-exposed → no dead phi. PROVABLY SAFE: a global alloca's placement is BYTE-IDENTICAL to before (induction vars / diamond joins unchanged), so the fix ONLY removes the spurious dead phis. CRUCIALLY PRESERVES fail-loud: a genuine uninitialized read (`int x; if(c) x=1; use(x)`) IS upward-exposed at the use → stays global → still gets its phi → still aborts on the undefined path (verified: that case still fatals). | `D-CSUBSET-DESCRIPTOR-TYPEDEF-POINTER-DECL` | ★ **FIRED — discovered 2026-06-25 (p18 SQLite-readiness Cluster G c1, while strengthening the `shipped_int_headers` corpus with a NULL witness).** A DESCRIPTOR-injected typedef name (from a shipped-header JSON descriptor — `int32_t`/`uint8_t`/`size_t`/…) used in POINTER-DECLARATOR position (`int32_t* p` / `size_t *p`) is NOT recognized as a type-name by the PARSER, so `int32_t * p` parses as a MULTIPLICATION expression (`int32_t` × `p`) → fails loud `S_UndeclaredIdentifier` (p) + `S_TypeMismatch` (initializer). ROOT: descriptor typedefs are injected SEMANTICALLY (post-parse, into cuRoot by `semantic_analyzer`), so the parser's `T * x` declaration-vs-multiply disambiguation never learns them. CONTRAST (all verified this cycle): a USER `typedef int myint; myint* p` WORKS (the parser sees the typedef decl → type-name visible); a BUILTIN `int* p` WORKS (keyword); and descriptor typedefs WORK in the UNAMBIGUOUS positions — scalar decl (`int32_t r`) + cast (`(int32_t)n`) — which need no parser type-name table. Only the pointer-declarator ambiguity exposes it. **FAILS LOUD (never a silent miscompile).** Priority: **normal — SQLite blast-radius UNMEASURED** (SQLite mostly uses its OWN amalgamation typedefs [`u8`/`u32`/`sqlite3_int64`, parser-visible → fine], but a direct `size_t *`/`uint8_t *` on a stdint/stddef typedef would mis-parse; re-probe sqlite3.c for descriptor-typedef pointer usage to set the real priority). | Make descriptor typedef-names parser-visible BEFORE the `T * x` disambiguation. Two designs (likely a §B fork): **(a)** pre-scan the source's `#include <...>` set → resolve descriptors → SEED the parser's type-name table before parsing (today includes resolve POST-parse in `import_resolver`, so this needs include-set-at-parse-time — the classic C lexer-hack ordering); **(b)** make the declaration-vs-multiply disambiguation SEMANTIC — speculatively parse both, resolve by whether `T` names a type in the semantic scope (incl. descriptor injections). | `D-OPT7-INLINE-LEGALITY-GATE` | OPT7 cycle 1 (2026-06-05): the §2.9 inline-legality gate is LIVE in `src/opt/passes/inlining.cpp` (`inlineLegalityGate` — refuses Weak/recursion/address-escape/IntrinsicCall-non-leaf/out-of-range-arity; the Weak refusal is the correctness rule the `D-OPT7-WEAK-INLINE-NEGATIVE-PIN` corpus proves). **Cycle 27 (2026-06-05) CLOSED the conservative recursion arm + the regular-`Call` non-leaf arm:** (1) the gate now LIFTS the non-leaf refusal for a callee whose body contains a regular `Call` — admitted, since the splice's generic arm clones an inner Call correctly (operands remapped via the `local` map; the inner Call's `GlobalAddr` re-emits the SAME symbol → same callee), pinned GREEN by `tests/opt/test_inlining.cpp::NonLeafCalleeIsInlined` + `MultiBlockNonLeafCalleeIsInlined` (both RED-on-disable when the line-209 `Call`-leaf refusal is re-added) + the runtime corpus `examples/c-subset/non_leaf_inline/` (`twice`/`helper`/`main`, `["Inlining"]` arm == baseline 41). (2) The recursion refusal is now SCC-based: a NEW agnostic substrate `src/opt/analysis/call_graph_scc.{hpp,cpp}` (`computeCallGraphSccs(Mir const&)` → `funcId.v → sccId`, iterative Tarjan over the self-contained direct call graph) lets the gate refuse ALL recursive-cycle inlining via `funcToScc.at(caller.v) == funcToScc.at(callee.v)` — which SUBSUMES self-recursion (a self-call is the singleton-SCC case, caller==callee → same id) AND generalizes to MUTUAL recursion (`f→g→f` share a multi-member SCC). Pinned by `tests/opt/test_call_graph_scc.cpp` (3-cycle / acyclic-chain / self-edge / mixed, RED-on-disable) + `tests/opt/test_inlining.cpp::MutualRecursiveCallIsNotInlined` (mutual f↔g refused + an ACYCLIC non-leaf A→B→C control that DOES inline; RED-on-disable: disabling the SCC refusal → `callsInlined` jumps to 2) + the retained `SelfRecursiveCallIsNotInlined` (now ALSO RED-on-disable via the SCC path, proving subsumption). The anchor stays OPEN for the STILL-DEFERRED relaxations: **(a) depth-bounded RECURSIVE inlining** — allow BOUNDED recursion (a depth/unroll policy), ADDITIVE on top of the SCC refusal; each bounded form needs its OWN miscompile pin (a wrongly-unrolled recursion = miscompile). **(b) the SOPHISTICATED cost model — PARTIALLY CLOSED cycle 28:** the conservative SIZE/cost bloat bound LANDED — `OptPipeline.inlineThreshold` (default 50, max `kMaxInlineThreshold`, config-driven via the pipeline JSON's optional `inlineThreshold`, loader-validated `[1, kMaxInlineThreshold]` → `X_PipelineMalformed`, threaded `runInlining(...,inlineThreshold)` → `inlineLegalityGate`) so the gate now REFUSES a callee whose instruction-count (summed across all blocks during the body scan) EXCEEDS the threshold (`if (instCount > inlineThreshold) return std::nullopt;` — `>` not `>=`, so an at-threshold callee inlines), and **`Inlining` now SHIPS in `release.pipeline.json`** (at index 1, after Identity, before ConstFold, with `inlineThreshold: 50`) bounded by that size cap. (The pre-cycle-28 bound "(ii) `Inlining` is NOT in release.pipeline.json" is NO LONGER TRUE — inlining ships, and the SIZE threshold is now the load-bearing bloat bound in its place.) **(c)** tightening the conservative address-escape refusal once an escape-analysis substrate can prove a taken address never reaches an indirect call. **(d) IntrinsicCall inlining — ✅ CLOSED cycle 29 (2026-06-05):** the gate's `IntrinsicCall` refusal was REMOVED — a callee whose body contains an `IntrinsicCall` (single-block OR multi-block) is now ADMITTED. | `D-OPT7-INLINE-FRAME-SENSITIVE-INTRINSIC` | The first FRAME-SENSITIVE intrinsic is registered/emitted by a frontend — a `va_start`/`va_arg`, `frameaddress`/`returnaddress`, `stacksave`/`stackrestore`, or `setjmp`-class intrinsic whose semantics depend on the ENCLOSING function's stack frame. | `D-OPT7-MULTIBLOCK-SPLICE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-05** (OPT7 cycle 2). The inliner now splices a GENERAL MULTI-BLOCK LEAF callee (cycle 1 was single-block-only). `inlineLegalityGate` LIFTED the `funcBlockCount(callee) != 1` refusal but keeps the leaf scan across ALL callee blocks (no `Call`/`IntrinsicCall` anywhere). Because the `tryRewrite` hook (1 Call → 1 value, mid-block-fill) structurally cannot create blocks, a function with any multi-block target is rebuilt by a new `MultiBlockInliner` (`src/opt/passes/inlining.cpp`): per original caller block kept as a branch target (`blockMap_`); the call-site block SPLIT at the Call (a fresh CONTINUATION block holds the after-Call insts); the callee CFG CLONED in RPO (fresh block+inst ids, shared callee→caller `local` map); each cloned `Return` rewritten to `Br(continuation)` collecting (value, cloned-pred) edges; a RETURN-MERGE PHI in the continuation joins them (elided to the single value for a 1-return callee; void callee → no Phi). StructCfMarker RE-DERIVED to `Linear` for every cloned + continuation block (SimplifyCfg cycle-9 precedent) — a clone of the callee's `EntryBlock`/`ExitBlock` would violate the verifier's entry/exit rules, and transplanting If/Loop marker COUNTS would break caller marker-parity; `Linear` is parity-neutral. Caller `Phi` incomings redirect `pred` through `blockExitMap_` (the last continuation of a split chain). **Proven**: runtime corpus `examples/c-subset/multiblock_inline/` (`pick(x){if(x>0)return 7;return 9;}`; `main` = `pick(1)+pick(0)` = 16) with an `optimizedPipelines:["Inlining"]` arm == baseline 16; **REGRESSION-PROVEN RED** — mis-wiring the merge to always pick the first return edge makes the optimized arm fail to compile (the then-clone value doesn't dominate the else→continuation path → MirVerifier rejects via verify-after-every-pass → differential ASSERT fires). MIR-tier pins in `tests/opt/test_inlining.cpp`: `MultiBlockLeafCalleeIsInlined` (Call gone + caller block count +4 [3 clones + 1 cont] + exactly 1 merge Phi + merge-Phi incomings CORRECTLY value↔pred paired [`instBlock(value)==pred` for the 7-from-then + 9-from-else edges; a swapped incoming → RED, catching a mis-merge the MIR tier alone would miss] + verifier-clean, RED-on-disable) + (at cycle-2 time) `MultiBlockNonLeafCalleeIsNotInlined` (scope boundary — **SUPERSEDED in cycle 27**: that scope boundary was the multi-block leaf restriction, which `D-OPT7-INLINE-LEGALITY-GATE` cycle 27 LIFTED; the test was flipped to `MultiBlockNonLeafCalleeIsInlined`, and a multi-block non-leaf callee now inlines). **Robustness gate (review fold 2026-06-05):** `inlineLegalityGate` ALSO refuses a leaf callee with NO RETURNING PATH (no `Return` in any block; every path ends in `Unreachable` — e.g. `int f(){ while(1){} }`). Without the refusal the splice routes each callee `Return` to a continuation block; a never-returning callee leaves that continuation predecessor-less → the MirVerifier (run after every pass) rejects the module → an otherwise-valid program becomes a build error UNDER inlining. Refusing keeps the Call out-of-line so the program compiles (conservative, never a miscompile). Pinned by `tests/opt/test_inlining.cpp::NonReturningLeafCalleeIsNotInlined` (multi-block entry→`Unreachable` leaf → callsInlined==0, Call survives, module still verifies; RED-on-disable: removing `if (!hasReturn) return nullopt;` admits it → the splice's `mapCallerValue` fail-loud aborts the build). | (closed) | plan 22 §2.9 OPT7; cited in `src/opt/passes/inlining.{hpp,cpp}` + `tests/opt/test_inlining.cpp` + `examples/c-subset/multiblock_inline/`; pairs with `D-OPT7-MULTIBLOCK-SPLICE-PHI` (callee-Phi deferral) + `D-OPT7-INLINE-LEGALITY-GATE` |
| `D-OPT7-MULTIBLOCK-SPLICE-PHI` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-13** (OPT7 callee-Phi cycle — §B design brief signed off, then built to the bar). `inlineLegalityGate`'s callee-`Phi` refusal is DROPPED (TOTAL — no shape gate replaces it); `MultiBlockInliner` now CLONES callee Phis via a DEFERRED-incoming-flush, a sibling of the return-merge `returnEdges` with a DISJOINT map (they compose without interference): a placeholder `dst_.addPhi(instType)` is emitted in the RPO clone loop (recorded into `deferredCalleePhis` + `local`, so later insts referencing the phi resolve), and AFTER the whole clone loop each incoming is flushed — the VALUE remapped via the shared `local` map (`mapCalleeOperand`), the PRED via the `calleeBlockMap` (callee-block→caller-block clone), with a fail-loud `std::abort` on a pred-not-in-clone-map (structurally unreachable — every callee block is pre-created in phase 1). The deferral is LOAD-BEARING for a LOOP-phi: the back-edge incoming VALUE is defined later in RPO (in the latch), so an inline flush would hit `mapCalleeOperand`'s def-before-use abort — flushing after the loop (when `local` is complete) is what makes it resolve. The `emitCalleeInst` Phi arm is KEPT as a defensive fail-loud guard (a Phi is handled in the clone loop and never reaches it; rationale comment corrected). Correctness comes from the remap, NOT from restricting shape — handles any incoming count / multiple phis / Arg-or-instruction incomings / loop back-edges uniformly. AGNOSTIC: purely opcode/map-structural; no language/CPU/format branch (routing keys only on `funcBlockCount != 1`). **Pins** (`tests/opt/test_inlining.cpp`, all RED-on-disable): `CalleePhiJoinAndReturnMergeCoexist` (a callee join-phi AND the inserted return-merge phi coexist + compose via disjoint maps), `LoopPhiCalleeInlinesBackEdgeRemapped` (the back-edge deferral — the ONLY shape that needs it; verifier-clean incl. the `I_LayoutUseBeforeDef` layout rule), `ArgKeyedTernaryPhiCalleeInlinesPaired` (the corpus wiring mirror — `pick(k){return k?7:9;}`), `CalleePhiValueTranspositionIsCaughtOnlyStructurally` (the MirVerifier provably CANNOT catch a value↔pred transposition when both values dominate from a common dominator — both modules verify GREEN; the structural pairing is the only signal), `CalleePhiPredMisremapGoesVerifierRed` (the complementary catchable case — a pred mis-remap DOES go verifier-red via `I_PhiPredNotInCfg`/`I_NotDominated`), and `CalleePhiCommonDominatorArmsPairedThroughInliner` (the design-audit's headline blind-spot, closed THROUGH the real inliner: an Arg-valued ternary `f(int k,int a,int b){return k?a:b;}` called `f(0,7,9)` — after the splice the cloned phi's values are main's consts {7,9} in a COMMON DOMINATOR, so a transposition is verifier-GREEN, making the source-intent pairing [then→7/else→9, navigated via the spliced CondBr since `instBlock(value)==pred` cannot apply] the SOLE red-on-disable guard; mutation-proven RED-on-transposition while `verify()` stayed GREEN). | `D-MERGE-UNREACHABLE-BLOCK` | Cycle 25 Stage B (2026-06-05): `mergeCuMirs` (`src/mir/merge/mir_merge.cpp`, `FunctionCloner::clone`) clones each surviving function's REACHABLE CFG — it pre-creates every natural block then fills in RPO from the entry (a valid def-before-use order for SSA). A pre-created block NOT reached by RPO (genuinely unreachable from the entry) is left unfilled, which the `MirBuilder`'s every-block-must-be-filled invariant would abort on at `finish()`; the cloner instead FAILS LOUD first (named abort) with attribution. This is correct for the merge's real inputs because the **c-subset frontend does not emit entry-unreachable blocks** (every block it lowers is reachable from the function entry; DCE, when the active pipeline runs it, additionally removes any dead block), and the hand-built tests are likewise all-reachable — so the unfilled-block case never arises today and the limitation is unobservable. The reachable-only assumption is NOT load-bearing for soundness, though: the **fail-loud abort is the actual backstop** — if a future input ever carried an unreachable block, the merge aborts with attribution rather than emitting a malformed function, so it is never a silent miscompile. Trigger = the first merge input carrying an unreachable block (e.g. a future frontend that emits an entry-unreachable block, or a debug/identity pipeline that runs no DCE on input that happens to contain one). Priority: **normal** (fail-loud today; never a silent miscompile). | Either (a) run DCE / dead-block elimination on each CU's MIR BEFORE the merge so only reachable blocks remain, OR (b) extend `FunctionCloner` to clone unreachable blocks too (fill them after the RPO pass in natural order; their intra-block SSA is self-contained, and cross-block operands into a dead block can't be live, so a second natural-order fill pass over the unfilled set suffices). Pin with a hand-built callee carrying a provably-unreachable block → the merged function preserves it (option b) or the merge runs post-DCE (option a). | plan 22 §2.9 OPT7 (cross-CU MIR merge); cited in `src/mir/merge/mir_merge.cpp`; pairs with `D-OPT7-CROSSCU-MIR-MERGE` |

| `D-PARSE-RECOVERY-MULTI-LEVEL-UNWIND` | The 2026-06-10 missing-initializer recovery fix (`synthesizeMissingRule`, `src/analysis/syntactic/parser.cpp`) synthesizes ONE absent required rule and advances the PARENT cursor ONE slot, so the enclosing frame consumes the stop-point — perfect for `int x = ;` (the missing `initValue` is one level below `varDeclHead`, which then eats the `;` + the block scope-closes its `}`). It does NOT unwind MULTIPLE frame levels to the resync owner: a missing production whose enclosing context spans several rule frames (e.g. tsql `SELECT FROM Users;` — the absent select-list sits under a multi-level select-statement) still gets a clean POSITIONED diagnostic at the error (an improvement) but leaves a RESIDUAL EOF `P_MissingRequiredChild` because the outer select-statement frames don't fully resync (pre-existing — `broken_select.sql.diag`'s EOF cascade predates this fix and only shifted LATERALLY this cycle, `P_NoAlternativeMatched`→`P_UnexpectedToken` at the `;`). NOT a regression; a recovery-COMPLETENESS gap. Priority: **low/normal** (positioned diagnostics already land; only the residual outer-frame cascade remains). | Generalize recovery to unwind the parser-frame stack down to the frame whose FOLLOW/sync OWNS the resync token (the "frame-aware panic" the plan-lock sketched), so ALL abandoned inner frames close cleanly + scope-balanced in one recovery event. Pin with a multi-level synthetic grammar + the tsql `broken_select` golden shedding its residual EOF `P_MissingRequiredChild`. | 2026-06-10 parser-recovery fix (`synthesizeMissingRule` in `src/analysis/syntactic/parser.cpp`); closes the single-level case of the V2-4 Part-B `task_5647346f` deficiency; future-work pin (do NOT cite in src) |
| `D-PARSE-INFIX-ASSOCIATIVITY-STRUCTURAL` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-12 (created + closed same cycle — the audit-trail row for a SILENT-MISCOMPILE class).** Same-precedence infix chains parsed RIGHT-associative in every Pratt-walked grammar (c-subset + toy; tsql IMMUNE — its `flatBinaryOpRule` path already left-folded in `lowerFlatExpr`; that path is table-blind for PRECEDENCE too, a sibling latent class pinned as `D-HR10-FLAT-EXPR-TABLE-BLIND`, trigger-gated): `10 - 3 + 1` → 6 (correct 8), `a/b/c` (100,5,2) → 50 (correct 10), the dss-state `ptr_swap_through` probe's `return x - y + 4;` → 34 (correct 42) — target-independent (PE + ELF-x86_64 + ELF-arm64 all wrong identically). ROOT CAUSE: `DefaultPrattWalker::parseExpressionAt` parsed the infix RHS at `op.precedence` unconditionally (right-recursive trees) while its class-doc claimed "a downstream semantic pass reads associativity from the operator table" — **no such consumer ever existed**; the declared `associativity` was a knob-that-lies, and every tree consumer (semantic const-eval, HIR combineBinary, MIR ConstFold) inherited the wrong grouping. Survived 263 green tests because NO corpus example contained a result-changing same-prec chain. FIX (engine, table-driven, zero identity): infix + ternary arms switched to **wrap-in-place** (`wrapLastChildExprFrame` — the mechanism the postfix arm already used) with **RHS minPrec = (assoc==Right ? prec : prec+1)** (Left AND None → structurally left); the climb-level WalkerSnapshot rollback-replay machinery DELETED (caller-less; diag-snapshot + sketch-truncate equivalence argument recorded at the site); **trivia hold-then-place** at the climb top (held until the wrap decision, placed inside the wrapper before the operator) — which ALSO fixed the pre-existing spaced-postfix bug (`f (40)` previously wrapped WHITESPACE → internal H0001, red-on-baseline demonstrated). Left chains now build ITERATIVELY (a 2000-op chain parses clean; previously the depth guard aborted). Pins: exact-tree-shape tests c-subset + synthetic (left/right/None-omitted/ternary-chain/postfix-mix/mixed-prec/spaced/comment-trivia/2000-op) with red-on-disable DEMONSTRATED (rhsMin reverted → right-nested shapes captured → restored hash-identical); semantic const-eval pin (`int g = 10-3+1;` == 8); MIR ConstFold pin; corpus `ptr_swap_through` + `assoc_chains` (LEFT→42, old-RIGHT→26/34 documented in manifests; one deliberately SPACED call) — exit-42 witnessed PE + WSL x86_64-ELF + qemu arm64-ELF; Mach-O = macos leg. dss-state battery: MISCOMPILES section EMPTY, `--strict` exit 0. 265/265. | (closed in the same cycle that created it — recorded for the audit trail; the closing work IS the row above) | `src/analysis/syntactic/parser.cpp` DefaultPrattWalker; dss-state probe `ptr_swap_through`; plan-05 (walker design history — superseded note added); plan-00 §0.2 D15 (the cycle-sequencing decision) |
| `D-HR10-FLAT-EXPR-TABLE-BLIND` | **OPEN (created 2026-06-12, the associativity-fix audit). Priority: trigger-gated.** The HR10 FLAT expression path (`lowerFlatExpr`, `src/hir/lowering/cst_to_hir.cpp` — grammars whose expression rule is a flat `operand (binaryOp operand)*` sequence instead of a Pratt `expr` shape, e.g. tsql-subset) left-folds `acc = combineBinary(op, acc, next)` and consults the declared operator table NOT AT ALL — **precedence included**: tsql declares precedence groups 10..40 that nothing consumes, so a flat-path `1 + 2 * 3` would fold `(1+2)*3` (≠ real T-SQL), and a hypothetical right-assoc flat operator would silently mis-group — the same knob-that-lies class the 2026-06-12 associativity fix closed for the Pratt path, surviving in the sibling path. | `D-HIR-LOOP-BODY-ONLY-RETURN-DOUBLE-ATTACH` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-13 (pre-FC5 deferral mini-arc).** Root cause was NOT loop-specific: `maybeAppendImplicitReturnZero` (src/hir/lowering/cst_to_hir.cpp) re-wrapped the body's ALREADY-PARENTED children via `makeBlock(oldKids+ret)`, and `makeBlock`→`addParent` aborts on a re-parented child (HIR is immutable) — so ANY non-empty non-terminating `main` crashed (the infinite-loop shapes AND `int main(){int x;x=1;}` are instances; the empty `int main(){}` survived only because oldKids was empty). FIX: immutability-safe nest — wrap the (unparented) body block + the synthetic return in a fresh outer block (`makeBlock({body,ret})`), never re-parenting children; the `addParent` guard is untouched.
