| `D-HIR-INFINITE-LOOP-NOT-TERMINATING` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-13 (pre-FC5 deferral mini-arc).** Implemented the documented design: `lowerWhile`/`lowerFor` (cst_to_hir.cpp) now wrap a PROVABLY-INFINITE loop (const-truthy/absent condition via the shared `evalCstConstInt` const-eval, AND no `break` reachable in this loop's own frame — a frame-respecting body scan that does NOT descend into nested loops/switches) as `Block{ loop, Unreachable }`, so `pathTerminates` (recursing to the Block's last child) recognizes the function terminates. `int f(){while(1){return 5;}}` now compiles + runs (exit 5); `for(;;)`/`do-while(1)` likewise. | `D-PP-FUNCTION-LIKE-MACRO` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-19 (FC13 cycle 2 — function-like macros).** The config-selected C preprocessor now implements function-like `#define F(a,b) ...` definitions AND invocations over the common direct-invocation subset of §6.10.3 (full hide-set deferred → `D-PP-MACRO-HIDESET-PRECISE`). `MacroExpander::handleDefine` parses the parameter list (comma-separated `Word` params, adjacency `(`-after-name detection on raw spans, empty `()` ⇒ zero params); the redefinition-compatibility check compares kind + params + replacement text (`sameDefinition`). The cycle-1 token-by-token `expandInto` was reworked into a STREAM expander `expand(std::span<Token const>, painting, depth)` (object- AND function-like uniformly): a function-like name is an invocation ONLY if the next significant token is the configured `(` (else emitted verbatim, §6.10.3p10); `collectArgs` collects paren-balance-tracked arguments (depth via the configured open/close paren; a depth-1 comma separates, the depth-0 close ends; trivia-trimmed); each argument is PRE-EXPANDED (`expand` in the current paint context, the invoked macro not yet painted, §6.10.3.1); `substitute` maps param-name tokens → pre-expanded arg tokens; the result is RESCANNED with the macro painted blue (§6.10.3.4 self-reference freeze). Zero-PARAM `M()` is normalized to zero args at the call site. FAIL-LOUD: arity mismatch + unterminated invocation (`P_PreprocessorMacroArgument`, new 0x0017); duplicate parameter + malformed param list (`P_PreprocessorDirective`); VARIADIC `#define V(...)` (`P_PreprocessorUnsupported` → `D-PP-VARIADIC-MACRO`, deferred). | `D-PP-MACRO-HIDESET-PRECISE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-19 (FC13 cycle 4 — the precise per-token hide set).** The recursion-scoped blue-PAINT set was REPLACED by Prosser's precise per-token hide set (the standard realization of C §6.10.3.4) — within FC13's no-`#`/`##` scope this now realizes the FULL §6.10.3.4, not merely the cycle-2/3-softened "common direct-invocation subset of §6.10.3". `Token` is a 16B trivially-copyable POD that cannot carry a set, so the expansion WORKING set is a wrapper `struct ExpToken { Token tok; HideSet hide; }` where `HideSet = shared_ptr<set<string> const>` (IMMUTABLE-once-built → copies are a refcount bump, every token of one replacement shares the SAME set object; a null pointer is the canonical EMPTY hide set, so the parser-bound body lifts in with `nullptr` and pays no allocation; `std::set` makes the hot intersection/union a linear merge). `run` lifts `vector<Token>` → `vector<ExpToken>` (empty hide sets), runs `expand`, drops hide sets back to `vector<Token>`. `expand` is now a SPLICE-RESCAN cursor (no longer isolated recursion): on each expansion it splices the produced tokens — each carrying its computed hide set — back over the consumed `[i,past)` region of the working set and rescans from the splice point, so a function-like name and a `(` that become adjacent only ACROSS the replacement/parent boundary RE-PAIR. A token (name M) expands iff `M ∉ hideset(T)`. OBJECT-like M: replacement tokens carry `hideset(T) ∪ {M}`. FUNCTION-like M (next significant token is the configured `(`, matching `)` exists): `HS' = (hideset(name) ∩ hideset(closeParen)) ∪ {M}` (the Prosser intersection — `collectArgs` surfaces the close paren's hide set; an argument's own accreted hide set is UNIONED with `HS'`, never dropped). The cycle-2/3 cross-boundary witnesses were FLIPPED: `#define A(x) x`+`#define F(x) ((x)+100)`+`A(F)(3)` → `((3)+100)` (was the literal `F(3)`); `#define NAME SQ`+`#define SQ(x) ((x)*(x))`+`NAME(4)` → `((4)*(4))` (was a frozen bare `SQ`). PRESERVED: direct object/function self-reference freeze (`#define X X`→`X`; `#define F(x) F(x)`+`F(1)`→`F(1)`), mutual recursion termination (`P↔Q`+`P(1)`), nested/argument-pre-expansion, variadic, object — all unchanged. The `depth` backstop is RETAINED as defense-in-depth but now bounds NESTING (argument pre-expansion) rather than chain length: a finite object CHAIN (`M0`→…→`M300`→0) now expands ITERATIVELY in one frame to `0` (the cycle-2/3 `DeepMacroExpansionFailsLoudNotSilent` premise was a recursive-engine artifact — FLIPPED to `DeepFiniteMacroChainExpandsToValue`), while a pathological 256-deep-nested argument (`F(F(…F(0)…))`) still FAILS LOUD (`DeepNestedMacroArgumentFailsLoudNotSilent`). AGNOSTIC: the new machinery operates on `Token`/`SchemaTokenId` + macro NAMES only; `(`/`)`/`,`/`...`/`__VA_ARGS__` remain config-driven (no new hard-coded lexeme/arch/format string). +6 net preprocessor unit tests (2 cross-boundary FLIPs, 4 preserved-freeze) + reframed deep-chain (1→2) + runnable 4-target corpus `examples/c-subset/preprocessor_hideset` (object-macro-names-function-macro + function-returns-function-name, runtime-seeded via `ident`, exit 42). 333 ctest; all object/function/variadic preprocessor tests + corpora unregressed; RED-on-disable demonstrated (reverting object-like to isolated recursion mis-freezes `NAME(4)` → bare `SQ`, `test_preprocessor.cpp` `HideSetObjectMacroNamingFunctionMacroExpands` fails). *(Original status, preserved:)* FC13 cycle 2 (2026-06-19): the function-like macro rescan uses a recursive blue-PAINT set (`expand`'s `painting` keyed on the macro NAME) — an APPROXIMATION of the precise per-token §6.10.3.4 hide-set. It is correct for the common DIRECT-invocation forms (a name immediately or near-adjacently invoked, self-reference freeze, nested/argument-as-macro pre-expansion — all pinned), but does NOT expand cases where a function-like name and its `(` are produced across SEPARATE expansion streams: `#define A(x) x` + `#define F(x) ((x)+100)` + `A(F)(3)` → the `A(F)` yields a bare `F`, and the trailing `(3)` is NOT re-paired with it, so the result is the literal `F(3)`; likewise `#define NAME SQ` + `#define SQ(x) ((x)*(x))` + `NAME(4)` freezes to bare `SQ` (the object expansion of `NAME` does not re-scan to collect `(4)`). These residual cases are a COMPLETENESS gap, NOT a silent miscompile: each FAILS LOUD downstream at the PARSER (verified: `got F` / `got SQ` — a bare function-like name with a stray `(…)` is a syntax error), never producing wrong code. `A(F)(3)` is the constructible loud-failure witness. Co-designed with FC15's `#`/`##` token-marker cluster (the precise per-token hide-set is the same machinery that tracks `#`/`##` placemarkers). Priority: **normal / trigger-gated** — closes with FC15, or sooner if a real corpus needs cross-stream re-pairing. | Replace the name-keyed blue-paint with a precise per-token hide-set (each replacement token carries the set of macro names disabled for it, per §6.10.3.4): a token's hide-set is the intersection of the invoked-macro's hide-set with the next-token's, plus the invoked macro; re-pairing of a function-like name with a `(` produced by a SEPARATE expansion then follows. Pin: `A(F)(3)` → `((3)+100)`; `NAME(4)` → `((4)*(4))`. Implement alongside the FC15 `#`/`##` placemarker tokens. | plan 23 FC13/FC15; `src/analysis/preprocess/preprocessor.cpp` `expand`/`painting`; witness `A(F)(3)` (today fails loud `got F` at the parser); FC15-area cluster (precise hide-set co-designed with `#`/`##`) |

| `D-PP-CONDITIONAL-COMPILATION` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-22 (Item 2 / FC14 — C conditional compilation).** `#if`/`#ifdef`/`#ifndef`/`#elif`/`#else`/`#endif` + the `defined` operator in the config-selected C preprocessor (`MacroExpander`). A single-pass CONDITION STACK (`CondFrame{enclosingActive, anyBranchTaken, thisBranchActive, seenElse}`): the 6 conditional directives are dispatched UNCONDITIONALLY (always balance-track nesting), while `#define`/`#undef`/`#include` + the unsupported-directive diagnostic + body-token emission are gated on `stackActive()` (a dead `#if 0` group is elided — only nesting is tracked, no errors, C 6.10.1); `seenElse` fail-loud on `#elif`/`#else` after `#else`; unterminated-at-EOF fail-loud. The `#if` integer-constant-expression evaluator is a NEW LIGHTWEIGHT preprocess-time TOKEN-Pratt (`src/analysis/preprocess/pp_if_eval.{hpp,cpp}`) that REUSES the main const-eval with ZERO duplication (§B): `opFromName`/`opEntryFor` extracted to a shared `src/hir/const_eval_operators.hpp` (CST evaluator byte-identical), the `const_eval_arith` core (`applyBinaryInt`/`applyUnaryInt`/`asBool`/`makeBoolLiteral`), `decodeInteger`, and `schema->operatorTable()` for PRECEDENCE (config-driven — no hardcoded operator/token names). `defined(X)`/`defined X` resolved BEFORE expansion (config parens, MF-1) into synthetic int-literals; then macro-expand the operand; surviving identifiers → 0 (incl. `sizeof`, which is NOT keyword-special-cased — C-faithful per C 6.10.1p4, so `sizeof(int)` fails loud as malformed; the agnosticism-breaking `"SizeofKeyword"` hardcode was removed in review-fold). | `D-PP-CONDITIONAL-INCLUDE-ORDERING` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-26 (p18 Cluster G c17).** Both symptoms fixed: a quote-`#include` guarded by a dead `#if`/`#ifdef` is no longer resolved (P0016), and an illegal char (`$`/`@`/`` ` ``) in a dead branch no longer reports (P000E) while a LIVE one STILL fails loud. **★ The originally-planned Option A (a pre-scan dead-region oracle) was IMPLEMENTED then CAUGHT by the in-cycle review as a CRITICAL SILENT MISCOMPILE: the SynthBuilder pre-scan cannot see predefined (or header-supplied) macros, so a predefined-macro-guarded LIVE branch (`#if __STDC__`) was folded to 0 -> recorded DEAD -> a genuinely-live illegal char consumed before the parser (e.g. on a `#define` line) was SILENTLY suppressed (reproduced end-to-end via the CLI: `#if __STDC__\n#define M $\n#endif` compiled with zero diagnostics).** §B (user, 2026-06-26): **Option 1 — authoritative dead-regions.** The P000E suppression is now driven by the AUTHORITATIVE `MacroExpander` pass's liveness (`MacroExpander::deadRanges()`, recorded in `run()` from the full `table_`+`predefined_` state) — the SAME liveness the compiler emits/skips tokens on — so the illegal-char oracle can NEVER diverge from the real branch decision (the silent class is gone by construction). NOT a silent miscompile: the elision is correct, and a missing dead-branch include errors LOUDLY (over-approximation, never a silent mis-include). | `D-PP-LINE-COMMENT-BEFORE-DIRECTIVE` | ✅ CLOSED 2026-06-26 (c22) — ROOT CAUSE: the `//` token's `stringStyle.endsAt:"\n"` CONSUMED the terminating newline as a comment-body token, so a `code // comment` line's only newline vanished → a following `#` directive lost its line boundary → `firstOnLine` judged it not-first-on-line → leaked to the parser (P0001). FIX: a new GENERIC `StringStyle.endsAtExclusive` (config-driven, agnostic) — the `//` mode ends AT but EXCLUDES the `\n`, which survives as a Newline token; handled at BOTH endsAt-consume sites (per-codepoint + coalesced). The c19 `firstOnLine` hypothesis was correctly DISPROVEN — the real gate was the TOKENIZER, not firstOnLine. Indep review+audit VERIFIED-CLEAN (adversarial: corpus exit 42 WITH the fix, directive-leak + NO binary WITHOUT); 445/445. (EOF line comment w/o trailing newline still fails loud P_UnterminatedComment — pre-existing, intended, C-conforming.) [orig NEW c18, refined c19] A `//` line comment AFTER code on a line, IMMEDIATELY followed by a `#` directive on the next line, makes the preprocessor FAIL to recognize the directive: it leaks to the parser → `D0004 <malformed include>` + `P0001 expected 'IncludeKeyword' got 'define'`, then a full cascade. Precise repro (CLI-confirmed): `int a; // c\n#define Z 1\nint b=Z;` → P0001. A `//` comment ALONE on its line before a directive (`// c\n#define Z 1`) WORKS; a trailing `//` comment ON the directive line (`#define Z 1 // c`) WORKS; a `/* */` comment before a directive WORKS — only `<code> // comment` then a directive breaks. NOT silent (loud parse error). Likely root (confirm at fix time): `MacroExpander::firstOnLine` + the `//`-comment token swallowing its trailing newline, so the `#` after `code // comment` scans back through the comment (trivia, not-newline) to the code `;` and is judged not-first-on-line → not stripped as a directive. PRE-EXISTING (FC14-era `firstOnLine`; NOT introduced by c17/c18 — neither touched directive recognition). NOT on the SQLite path (sqlite3.c uses `/* */`, so the c18 re-probe did not hit it — IncludeKeyword count 0). Priority: **normal** (rare pattern; loud, not silent; NOT on the SQLite path). ★ **c19 UPDATE (2026-06-26): the `firstOnLine` hypothesis was TESTED and DISPROVEN** — adding a LineComment line-boundary check to `MacroExpander::firstOnLine` did NOT fix it (a clean rebuild still failed `int a; // c\n#define Z 1`). The `#` IS first-on-line, so `firstOnLine` is not the gate. Variant probes narrowed it: `int a; // c\n#define` FAILS, but `int a;\n// c\n#define` (comment on its own line) and `int a;\n\n#define` (blank line) both WORK — so the trigger is specifically a `//` comment SHARING A LINE WITH CODE, before a directive. The real mechanism is a preprocess-tier `//`-comment interaction not yet root-caused (`ppLexemes` at the preprocess tier shows `//` lexed as `/`+chars, but the full CLI pipeline handles `//` elsewhere — so the dump is misleading; needs a parse-tier token dump of the failing vs passing case). DEEPER than a one-liner — its own focused investigation cycle. | Root-cause the `code // comment`-then-directive desync (dump the synth + parse token streams for `int a; // c\n#define Z 1` vs `int a;\n// c\n#define Z 1`); fix at the real gate. Pin: `int a; // c\n#define Z 1\nint b=Z;` compiles clean AND `b` expands to `1`. | plan 25 c18/c19; `src/analysis/preprocess/preprocessor.cpp` + the `//`-comment tokenizer mode |

| `D-PP-VARIADIC-GNU-COMMA-ELISION` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-24 (cycle d — FC15 paste residuals).** The GNU `,##__VA_ARGS__` idiom is now CONFIG-GATED (`preprocess.variadicCommaElision`, c-subset opts in): in Phase A's `isVaArgsName` arm, when the `##` immediately precedes `__VA_ARGS__` AND the prior `items` token is the config-declared arg-separator, an EMPTY `__VA_ARGS__` drops both the separator and the `##` (`LOG("x")`→`f("x")`), a NON-empty one keeps the separator and emits the pre-expanded args with no paste (`LOG("x",1)`→`f("x",1)`). Pins `FC15GnuCommaElision{EmptyVaArgs,NonEmptyVaArgs,IsConfigDriven}` + corpus. Historical: FC15a named exclusion (2026-06-24): the GNU `,##__VA_ARGS__` comma-elision extension is NOT implemented. FC15a delivers the standard `#` (stringize, C 6.10.3.2) + `##` (token-paste, C 6.10.3.3) operators, but a `, ## __VA_ARGS__` paste where `__VA_ARGS__` is EMPTY does NOT drop the preceding comma (GNU/C++20 `__VA_OPT__`-adjacent behavior): the literal comma stays (`f(a,)`), and the `##` against an empty operand pastes the comma with nothing (a no-op paste → the lone comma survives, NOT a fail-loud — the comma `,` is a single valid token). NOT a silent miscompile (a stray trailing comma is a parse-visible artifact, not wrong code). Priority: **trigger-gated** (FC15b — a real corpus needing variadic logging `LOG(fmt, ...)` with zero trailing args, or `__VA_OPT__`). | Implement the GNU comma-elision special case: in `substitute`, when a `##` has a `__VA_ARGS__` right operand that expands to EMPTY and a `,` left operand, drop the comma (and the `##`) entirely. Consider also C23 `__VA_OPT__(...)`. Pin: `#define LOG(fmt, ...) f(fmt, ## __VA_ARGS__)` + `LOG("x")` → `f("x")` (no trailing comma); `LOG("x", 1)` → `f("x", 1)`. | plan 23 FC15b; `src/analysis/preprocess/preprocessor.cpp` `substitute`/`collapsePastes`; `tests/analysis/preprocess/test_preprocessor.cpp` |
| `D-PP-PRAGMA-OPERATOR-FORM` | FC15c named exclusion (2026-06-24, `#pragma` + `__has_include` + `__has_c_attribute`): the `_Pragma("...")` OPERATOR form (C 6.10.9) is NOT implemented. FC15c delivers the `#pragma` DIRECTIVE form (C 6.10.6 — consumed-and-dropped in `handleDirective`); `_Pragma` is a DISTINCT, EXPANSION-TIME operator (`_Pragma(string-literal)` destringizes its argument and processes it as if it were a `#pragma` line), so it can appear in a macro replacement and is resolved during macro expansion, not at directive scan. NOT a silent miscompile — a `_Pragma(...)` token sequence today expands as an ordinary identifier + call shape (or fails loud at the parser), never altering codegen. Priority: **normal / trigger-gated** (rare in hand-written C; common in library headers that wrap pragmas in macros). | Add a `_Pragma` operator (config `pragmaOperator` word, matched by TEXT like `defined`/`__has_include`): in the expander, recognize `_Pragma ( string-literal )`, destringize the literal (strip the `"`, un-escape `\"`/`\\`, C 6.10.9p1), and treat the result as a `#pragma` line — i.e. consume-and-drop it (DSS recognizes no pragma), so `_Pragma("once")` expands to nothing. Pin: `_Pragma("GCC optimize(\"O2\")")` in a replacement list expands to nothing (no error, no stray tokens). | plan 23 FC15c; `src/analysis/preprocess/preprocessor.cpp` (`expand`); `src/core/types/preprocess_config.hpp`; `tests/analysis/preprocess/test_preprocessor.cpp` |
| `D-PP-PRAGMA-RECOGNIZED-SEMANTICS` | FC15c named exclusion (2026-06-24, `#pragma`): specific `#pragma` EFFECTS beyond consume-ignore are NOT implemented. FC15c consumes-and-DROPS every `#pragma` line (C 6.10.6p2 explicitly licenses an implementation to ignore a pragma it does not recognize, so consume-drop is CONFORMING). The standard pragmas `#pragma STDC FP_CONTRACT`/`FENV_ACCESS`/`CX_LIMITED_RANGE` (C 6.10.6p2) and the ubiquitous `#pragma once` (header-guard idiom) currently have NO effect — `#pragma once` does not dedup a doubly-included header (the `#include` machinery's existing canonical-path cycle guard catches a CYCLE, but a non-cyclic double-include is re-spliced). NOT a silent miscompile — dropping a pragma is standard-permitted, and the FP/FENV pragmas only relax codegen latitude DSS does not currently take. Priority: **normal / trigger-gated** (closes when a real corpus needs `#pragma once` dedup or an `STDC` pragma's codegen effect). | Give the recognized pragmas effect: parse the pragma payload (after the consume scan), dispatch on a config-declared recognized-pragma set. `#pragma once` records the current file's canonical path in a once-set the `SynthBuilder` consults to SKIP a second splice; the `STDC` pragmas set a per-region float-eval/fenv flag the lowering honors. Pin: a header with `#pragma once` included twice is spliced ONCE; `#pragma STDC FP_CONTRACT OFF` disables FMA contraction in the following region. | plan 23 FC15c; `src/analysis/preprocess/preprocessor.cpp` (`SynthBuilder` splice + `handleDirective` pragma arm); `tests/analysis/preprocess/test_preprocessor.cpp` |
| `D-PP-LINE-DIRECTIVE` | FC15b named exclusion (2026-06-24, predefined macros): the `#line N` / `#line N "file"` directive (C 6.10.5) is NOT implemented. FC15b delivers the PREDEFINED macros (`__LINE__`/`__FILE__`/`__STDC__`/`__STDC_VERSION__`/`__STDC_HOSTED__`/`__DATE__`/`__TIME__`, C 6.10.8) — `__LINE__`/`__FILE__` resolve against the INVOCATION offset through the line-map to the PHYSICAL line / origin file name. A `#line` directive would OVERRIDE that presumed line number + file name for the tokens that follow, but until it lands `__LINE__`/`__FILE__` always report the PHYSICAL source line/name. NOT a silent miscompile — a `#line` directive currently falls through to the generic `P_PreprocessorUnsupported` fail-loud arm in `handleDirective` (an unsupported directive, never silently ignored); and `__LINE__`/`__FILE__` reporting the physical line/name (when no `#line` is in play, the universal case) is CORRECT, so this is a fail-SOFT gap that only bites a TU that actually uses `#line` (rare in hand-written C; common in generated code / `yacc`/`lex` output). Priority: **normal / trigger-gated** (closes when a real corpus needs `#line` — e.g. a generated lexer, or `__FILE__`/`__LINE__` accuracy under a `#line`-rewritten preamble). | Add a `#line` directive handler (config `lineDirective` word, mirroring `defineDirective` &c.): parse `#line <digit-sequence> [ "<filename>" ]`, then maintain a PRESUMED-position override (a per-region (line-delta, file-name) shift) that `materializePredefined`'s Line/File arms consult AHEAD of the raw line-map resolve. The line-map already gives the physical origin; `#line` layers a logical override on top. Pin: `#line 100 "gen.c"` then `__LINE__` on the next physical line → 100 (not the physical line), and `__FILE__` → `"gen.c"`. | plan 23 FC15b; `src/analysis/preprocess/preprocessor.cpp` (`handleDirective`, `materializePredefined`); `src/core/types/preprocess_config.hpp`; `tests/analysis/preprocess/test_preprocessor.cpp` |
| `D-CSUBSET-INCDEC-CONST-LVALUE` | **OPEN — pre-existing gap, fail-SOFT, normal (Cluster F item F1, 2026-06-24).** A `const`-qualified lvalue used as the operand of `++`/`--` (`const int x; x++;`) is NOT rejected — `classifyLvalue` / `simpleLvalue` do not model `const` today, so an `x++` on a `const` object lowers as an ordinary modifiable-lvalue read-modify-write. NOT introduced by F1: the SAME gap exists on plain assignment (`const int x; x = 5;`) and compound-assign (`x += 1;`), all of which route through the same `const`-unaware lvalue classification. F1's ++/-- lvalue guard DOES reject a manifest RVALUE operand (`5++`/`++5` → `S_IncDecNeedsModifiableLvalue`), but a `const` *lvalue* is addressable, so the shape guard admits it. Not a silent miscompile of VALUE (the increment is arithmetically correct); it is a missing CONSTRAINT diagnostic (C 6.5.2.4p1 / 6.5.16p2 require a MODIFIABLE lvalue). Priority: **normal**. | Add a modifiable-lvalue / `const`-qualifier check SHARED with assignment + compound-assign (the single lvalue-classification chokepoint), emitting `S_ConstViolation` (or `S_IncDecNeedsModifiableLvalue` for the ++/-- arm) when the lvalue's type carries the language's `const` qualifier. Requires the type lattice to carry a const-qualified marker the classifier can read. Pin: `const int x = 0; x++;` and `const int y = 0; y = 1;` both fail loud. | plan 23 Cluster F (F1); `src/hir/lowering/cst_to_hir.cpp` (`classifyLvalue`/`classifyIncDecLvalue`/`simpleLvalue` + the assignment path); `tests/hir/test_hir_lowering_c_subset.cpp` |
| `D-PP-VA-OPT` | FC15-paste-residuals deferral (2026-06-24, cycle d): the C23 `__VA_OPT__(content)` construct (C23 6.10.3.1) is NOT implemented. It is a DISTINCT, more general mechanism than the GNU `,##__VA_ARGS__` comma-elision THIS cycle delivered: `__VA_OPT__(content)` emits `content` (an arbitrary balanced-paren token sequence) iff `__VA_ARGS__` expands to a non-empty list, and elides the whole `__VA_OPT__(...)` otherwise — it requires recognizing `__VA_OPT__` + balanced-paren body extraction + conditional emission, none of which the placemarker/comma-elision machinery does. PRE-EXISTING gap (not introduced this cycle): a `__VA_OPT__` token in a replacement is left as an ORDINARY identifier (so a user writing it gets the literal `__VA_OPT__ ( … )` tokens through, a parse-visible wrong result, NOT a silent miscompile and NOT a fail-loud). Priority: **normal / trigger-gated** (closes when a real corpus / SQLite needs `__VA_OPT__`; the GNU `,##__VA_ARGS__` idiom — far more common in existing C — is already covered). | Add a config `vaOptOperator` word (matched by TEXT like `defined`/`__has_include`); in `substitute`, recognize `__VA_OPT__ ( <balanced> )`, and emit the `<balanced>` content (pre-expanded) iff `rawVaArgs` is non-empty, else nothing. Pin: `#define F(...) g(__VA_OPT__(0,) __VA_ARGS__)` + `F()` → `g()`, `F(1)` → `g(0, 1)`. | plan 23 FC15; `src/analysis/preprocess/preprocessor.cpp` (`substitute`); `src/core/types/preprocess_config.hpp`; `tests/analysis/preprocess/test_preprocessor.cpp` |
| `D-CSUBSET-FLOAT-NEG-ENCODING` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-07-01 (p19 Cluster G c78; §B USER folded into c78) — fneg realized capability-dispatched: arm64 native FNEG (0x1E614000/0x1E214000); x86 `xorpd/xorps xmm,[rip+16B-signmask]` (a minted 16-byte rodata sign-mask + the RipRelDisp32 slot). Objdump-confirmed 16-aligned masks on all 3 legs INCL. pe64 (4096 PE section + per-item 16-offset; the USER's PE-align concern refuted); signed-zero IEEE-correct (-（+0.0)=-0.0). Witness `examples/c-subset/float_negate`=42 (RED-ON-DISABLE → A_NoEncodingDeclared). Was a Cluster-F F3 deferral (2026-06-24, cycle 7): float unary minus `-x` AND a negative float LITERAL (`-42.0`) lower to the MIR `fneg` op, which has NO encoding declared — `A_NoEncodingDeclared` (x86) / `L_RequiredLirOpcodeMissing` (arm64). FAIL-LOUD (the function is dropped with a positioned diagnostic; NEVER a silent miscompile). NOT a simple mirror of fadd/fmul/fsub: x86 float negate is not a 2-reg ALU op — it is `XORPS xmm, signmask` (needs a `0x8000…0` sign-bit mask constant in rodata) OR `0.0 - x` (an FSUB from a materialized zero); arm64 FNEG IS a single 1-source FP instruction (`FNEG Dd, Dn` = 0x1E614000 / S-form 0x1E214000). Surfaced when the F3 `float_mul_sub` corpus used `-42.0` literals (the corpus was rewritten to avoid it via `(a-b)-(b-a)`). Priority: **normal / trigger-gated** (closes when a real corpus / SQLite needs float negation — common in real C). | x86: add an `fneg` encoding (an XORPS-with-rodata-signmask sequence, OR lower MIR FNeg → `0.0 - x` FSUB at MIR→LIR — the simpler, arguably-better long-term path since it reuses the now-encoded fsub). arm64: add an `fneg` opcode row (FNEG single-source, mirror the `fmov`/`fpcvt` 1-source fixed32 shape). Pin: `double f(double x){return -x;}` compiles + `-x` is runtime-correct on both targets; byte-pin the encoding. | plan 23 Cluster F; `src/dss-config/targets/{x86_64,arm64}.target.json`; possibly `src/lir/lowering/mir_to_lir.cpp` (FNeg→FSub lowering) |

---

## Allowlist (code-internal pins, NOT deferred work)

Anchor-shaped strings in `src/` that are **not** deferred-work markers and
should be **ignored** by the CI guard. Add a row when an in-code constant
or diagnostic-message identifier matches the `D-*` regex but isn't a
deferred-work anchor.

| Pattern | Reason |
|---|---|
| `D-MERGE-GLOBAL-INITFUNC` | Cycle 25 Stage B code-internal INVARIANT pin (`src/mir/merge/mir_merge.cpp`), NOT deferred work. Cited in the fail-loud abort that fires if a merged global's `initFunc` MirFuncId was not cloned into the merged module (`plan.funcMerged` miss). The invariant always holds for valid input — a global's module-init function is a defined function in the same CU, which the merge always clones (an init function is never a cross-CU weak loser). The abort is defense-in-depth: a breach means the planning pass dropped a function a global still references (a structural contradiction), so failing loud beats emitting a global whose initializer points at a stale/absent func. No closing work — it is a permanent guard, like the other `mergeFatal` invariant aborts. |
| `D-CSUBSET-COMPUTED-GOTO` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-23 (FC-deferral close-out c9, branch p14 — USER OPTED IN, overriding the named-exclusion).** GNU computed goto (`&&label` label-address + `goto *p` indirect branch) implemented END-TO-END, correct under the full release pipeline. §B-signed-off (full-mechanism-correct-under-opt + synthetic-per-block-symbol reloc); independently plan-locked (MF-1 CFG-correctness verified by construction; 8 opt passes cleared) + independently pr-reviewed. AS-BUILT: grammar (a dedicated `labelAddressExpr` operand rule `[AndAndOp, Identifier]` — NOT a prefix-group `&&`, because the parser rejects `&<undeclared-id>`; a 2-alt `gotoStmt`) + HIR `LabelAddressOf`/`IndirectGotoStmt` + MIR `IndirectBr` terminator (variadic successors = ALL address-taken blocks, like Switch) + `BlockAddress` value op (side-effecting → DCE-stable; `isBlockAddressTaken` DERIVED from BlockAddress ops, drift-proof) + the clone arms at mir_merge + mir_rebuild_helper + a SimplifyCfg guard (don't fold/merge an address-taken TARGET block) + Inlining refusal + LIR/asm (x86 NEW `jmp FF /4` / arm64 NEW `BR Xn` 0xD61F0000; BlockAddress→lea/adrp+add to a synthetic per-block symbol) + a NEW format-neutral linker interior-block-symbol VA (`interior_block_symbol_va.hpp`, ELF/PE/Mach-O, `SymbolKind::BlockLocal`). Witnessed: `examples/c-subset/computed_goto` (threaded interpreter exit 17) + `computed_goto_inline_host` (exit 11) on x86-PE + WSL arm64-qemu, under BOTH baseline AND release pipelines; red-on-disable pins (IndirectBr-successors-truncated, SimplifyCfg-address-taken-fold, inline-into-host-routing). 369→370 ctest. **The pr-review caught a reachable silent miscompile the plan-lock + build BOTH missed**: the `MultiBlockInliner`'s hand-rolled caller-host emit (a 3rd clone family) mis-copied a BlockAddress payload + aborted on IndirectBr when inlining INTO a computed-goto host — folded by routing computed-goto hosts to the single-block rebuilder (correct remap), red-on-disable demonstrated. **NAMED FOLLOW-UP (open):** `D-CG-INLINE-MULTIBLOCK-INTO-COMPUTED-GOTO-HOST`. | (closed — c9 branch p14) | grammar + HIR + MIR + opt + lir + asm + link (interior_block_symbol_va.hpp) / plan-23 full-C arc |
| `D-CG-INLINE-MULTIBLOCK-INTO-COMPUTED-GOTO-HOST` | **OPEN, OPT, trigger-gated (FC-deferral close-out c9, 2026-06-23).** A function that ITSELF contains a computed goto (`BlockAddress`/`IndirectBr`) is currently routed through the SINGLE-block `MirFunctionRebuilder` inliner (which remaps both correctly), NEVER the `MultiBlockInliner` — so a MULTI-block callee is NOT inlined into a computed-goto host (single-block callees still are). Correct + fail-safe (no miscompile); the only cost is a missed optimization. Closing work (only if a real perf consumer needs it): add `BlockAddress` (block-id payload remap via `blockMap_`) + `IndirectBr` (successor remap) arms to `MultiBlockInliner::emitCallerInst`/`emitTerminator` (mirroring the rebuild-helper arms), + a test inlining a multi-block helper INTO a computed-goto host under the release pipeline. Trigger: a benchmark showing the missed inline matters. | Add the 2 caller-host emit arms to MultiBlockInliner + a red-on-disable test. Priority: **opt (trigger-gated)**. | `src/opt/passes/inlining.cpp` MultiBlockInliner (the `functionHasComputedGoto` routing guard) + `D-CSUBSET-COMPUTED-GOTO` |
| `D-CSUBSET-LABEL-BEFORE-CASE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-23 (FC-deferral close-out c10, branch p14, 371 ctest + corpus `label_before_case` exit 25 PE/ELF/qemu baseline+release).** AS-BUILT = Option A (user-chosen — label NESTS over case, C-faithful): a new `caseStmt = [caseLabel, statement]` grammar form added to the `statement` alt + `switchBodyItem` made **speculative** (plan-lock CRITICAL catch: a non-speculative alt would trip the loader's `C_AmbiguousAlternatives` gate at CONFIG LOAD once {Case,Default} enters FIRST(statement) — c-subset would not load AT ALL) + a `caseStmtRule` config pointer (AGNOSTIC; toy/tsql don't declare it → `.valid()`==false → the new arms no-op, exactly like `caseLabelRule`). `lowerSwitch` peels a (multi-)label-wrapped `caseStmt` into arms via an iterative chain (handles `foo: case 1: case 2: stmt`), producing HIR **identical** to the long-supported `case 1: foo: stmt` — the label STAYS a real `LabelStmt` node, so the CST pre-scan + `goto`-INTO-switch resolution + duplicate/undefined-label checks all work UNCHANGED. A `caseStmt` reached as a non-direct-switch-item fails loud via NEW `S_CaseLabelNotInSwitch` (0xE023). Pins (all red-on-disable): HIR-equivalence (`foo: case 1: S` ≡ `case 1: foo: S`), bare-case-stays-flat (Finding 2), outside-switch guard; corpus `goto`s INTO the switch at the label → exit 25 baseline+release. Residual: [[D-CSUBSET-CASE-LABEL-IN-NESTED-BLOCK]]. ORIGINALLY: NAMED LIMITATION (FC5, 2026-06-15) — a goto-label immediately preceding a `case`/`default` label (`switch(x){ foo: case 1: … }`) is legal-but-rare ISO C that FC5 did NOT parse: `labelStmt`'s body is a `statement`, while `caseLabel` is reachable only via `switchBodyItem`, so `foo: case 1:` is a clean fail-loud parse error (P0001 "expected EndStatement", no binary — NEVER a silent mis-parse). All OTHER label positions (before any ordinary statement, forward/backward goto, goto into/out of loops, label on an empty statement, goto-over-initialization) are fully supported. Priority: **normal** (rare form; fails loud). | The clean fix is the case-labels-as-statements switch-grammar refactor — model `case N : stmt` / `default : stmt` as `statement` forms (so labels nest uniformly: `foo: case 1: stmt` = `label(foo, case(1, stmt))`) and re-point `lowerSwitch` at the nested shape. That is its own piece of work (touches the switch lowering's flat case-item consumption), disproportionate to bolt onto FC5 — hence the named blocker. Pin: `switch(x){ foo: case 1: return 1; }` parses + runs. | plan-23 full-C arc (FC5); c-subset `labelStmt`/`switchBodyItem`/`caseLabel`/`caseStmt`/`caseStmtRule`; `src/hir/lowering/cst_to_hir.cpp` lowerSwitch + the lowerStmt CaseStmt guard |
| `D-CSUBSET-CASE-LABEL-IN-NESTED-BLOCK` | **OPEN — NAMED LIMITATION, fail-loud, rare (FC-deferral close-out c10, 2026-06-23).** A `case`/`default` label nested inside an INNER block of a switch arm (`switch(x){ case 1: { foo: case 2: y(); } }`) is not associated with the switch by the dss flat-switch model — `lowerSwitch` groups only DIRECT switch-body items, so a case in a nested block reaches `lowerStmt` and fails loud with `S_CaseLabelNotInSwitch` (C 6.8.1). This is a PRE-EXISTING limit of the flat model (it was P0001 before c10 too — `case` was not a `statement`), surfaced (not introduced) by the [[D-CSUBSET-LABEL-BEFORE-CASE]] grammar work; correct + fail-loud, never a miscompile. Priority: **normal** (rare; fails loud). | Closing it = lowerSwitch recursing into nested blocks to harvest their case labels (Duff's-device territory) — a switch-lowering generalization, only if a real consumer needs it. Pin: `switch(x){case 1:{foo: case 2: return 2;}}` runs. | `src/hir/lowering/cst_to_hir.cpp` lowerSwitch (direct-switch-body-item grouping) + the `S_CaseLabelNotInSwitch` guard |
| `D-CSUBSET-VOLATILE-POINTEE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-27 (p19 Cluster G c27) — model A: `volatile` as a TYPE QUALIFIER.** ★ §B (user, 2026-06-27): **Design B** — a qualified `TypeId` (`TypeKind::VolatileQual`, the registry's anticipated "model A") — chosen OVER a Ptr-pointee bit. TRANSPARENT wrapper: `kind()`/`operands()`/`scalars()` route through `materialId_` so the ~128 kind-dispatch sites are correct BY CONSTRUCTION (the wrapper is observable only via `isVolatileQualified`/`get()`); idempotent; `const` gets NO wrapper (stays ignored for type identity). Accesses set `MirInstFlags::Volatile` via a new `volatileFlagForType` ORed with the c21 `volatileFlagFor` at EVERY access form. c21's per-symbol `SymbolRecord.isVolatile` RETIRED → migrated to the type (fixed a c21 double-count: `volatile int *p` wrongly marked the pointer OBJECT volatile). The two `S_VolatilePointeeNotSupported` (0xE025) reject sites DELETED + retired from kUnsuppressable (enum kept for ordinal stability). ★★ The independent post-build AUDIT CAUGHT a silent-miscompile the local Windows suite missed: member/index/by-value access of a volatile CONTAINER (`volatile struct S *p; p->a` — the sqlite Kahan-summation `volatile SumCtx*` + WAL `volatile WalCkptInfo*` shapes) dropped the flag — a REGRESSION from c21's loud reject to silently-wrong. FIXED by type-propagation: a member/index access of a volatile container yields a volatile-qualified RESULT type, covering nested chains + complex-lvalue compound-assign (`pSum->rErr += r`) by-construction, + explicit by-value-arg/struct-return/brace-init threading; 10 per-form red-on-disable container pins. A reintern silent-drop (transparent `kind()` would reintern `volatile T` as `T` cross-CU) also caught+fixed. WITNESS: 29 MIR volatile pins (red-on-disable, exact-count) + runtime `volatile_pointee_cse` (CSE folds iff the flag is missing: exit 3 vs 2, WSL-verified) + `volatile_pointee`/`volatile_pointee_member` (the c21 reject examples INVERTED to positives); 449→450. ★ LESSON: a multi-site volatile contract needs EVERY container-access form tested — the c21 lesson recurred (the local Windows suite was green-but-wrong; only the WSL runtime pin + the audit's per-form MIR probes caught the container hole). [orig:] **OPEN — NAMED LIMITATION, fail-loud, trigger-gated (c21, D-CSUBSET-VOLATILE-QUALIFIER, 2026-06-26).** c21 shipped `volatile` via **model B** (per-symbol/member `SymbolRecord.isVolatile` → `HirVolatileMap` on the access node → `MirInstFlags::Volatile` on every user Load/Store; the optimizer's DCE/CSE/Mem2Reg/LICM already honor the flag). Model B handles the OBJECT / struct-MEMBER / pointer-OBJECT (`int * volatile p`) forms — everything the SQLite frontier (`volatile int isInterrupted;`) needs. It CANNOT express a pointer-to-volatile **POINTEE** (`volatile int *p; *p`): there the volatility rides the DEREFERENCED access, which requires type-level cv-qualification (model A — a cv-qualified `TypeId` threaded through the interner + type-equality + every TypeId consumer + the optimizer's type inspection, a large core change). Building model A NOW, before a re-probe proves SQLite needs pointer-to-volatile, would be a speculative over-build, so the pointee form is REJECTED LOUD (`S_VolatilePointeeNotSupported`, 0xE025, unsuppressable) at BOTH type-name sites — the per-declarator typing arm (head `volatile` + a declarator star) AND the co-located pointer arm (head `volatile` before the first star) — making the fail-loud COMPLETE BY CONSTRUCTION (no pointer-to-volatile-pointee TYPE can be built ⇒ no `Deref` can silently drop the flag, the silent miscompile this gate forbids). | **Trigger:** a SQLite re-probe (or any real consumer) shows a genuine need for pointer-to-volatile-pointee. **Closing work (model A):** add cv-qualification to the type lattice (a const/volatile-qualified `TypeId`), thread it through type-equality + every TypeId consumer + the optimizer's type-inspection, and lower a volatile-pointee `Deref` to a flagged Load; then DELETE the two `S_VolatilePointeeNotSupported` reject sites (and the diagnostic + its kUnsuppressable membership). Pin: `volatile int *p; int a = *p; int b = *p;` keeps BOTH loads under the release pipeline (red-on-disable, exit-code witness mirroring `volatile_member`). | `D-CSUBSET-VOLATILE-QUALIFIER` (the c21 model-B parent); `src/core/types/parse_diagnostic.hpp` `S_VolatilePointeeNotSupported`; `src/analysis/semantic/semantic_analyzer.cpp` (the two reject arms); plan 23 full-C arc |
| `D-CSUBSET-STRUCT-MULTI-DECLARATOR` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-26 (p18 Cluster G c23).** A struct/union body admitted only ONE declarator per member (`int *a, *b;` → P0009 "got ';'"; sqlite3.c:15516 `struct HashElem { HashElem *next, *prev; ... };` the frontier). C 6.7.2.1 allows a comma-separated declarator LIST sharing one base type. FIX = REUSE the existing `declaratorList` mechanism (the engine's `collectDeclarators`/`declaratorNameNode` role dispatch that top-level/local decls already use): new grammar rules `structMemberDeclarator` = `{declarator?}{bitfieldDeclSuffix?}` (the suffix moved INSIDE each slot so `int a:3,b:5;` resolves per-slot) + `structMemberDeclaratorList`; `structField`/`unionField` head + `{structMemberDeclaratorList?}` + `EndStatement`; rows `declarator:1` → `declaratorList:1`; two OPTIONAL `DeclaratorConfig` roles `memberDeclaratorRule`/`memberListRule` (nullopt for toy/tsql → zero change). AGNOSTIC (config rows + the generic declarator engine; no lang identity branch). | ✅ THE CRUX (silent layout miscompile, handled by-construction): each declarator gets its OWN pointer/array/bitfield suffix; only the HEAD base type is shared — `int *a, b;` = Ptr<int> (a) + int (b). 3 mandatory plan-lock fixes folded: **FIX 1** (the feature is DEAD without it — breaks single-declarator too) — added the `memberDeclaratorRule` arm to `declaratorDeclaredType` (`semantic_analyzer.cpp`), mirroring the initDeclaratorRule arm, else every field type → InvalidType → struct never composes; the head base TypeId is taken BY VALUE into the append-only interner so no per-slot star leaks. **FIX 2** — added `memberDeclaratorRule`/`memberListRule` to the CLOSED `kDeclaratorKeys` array + OPTIONAL parse in `grammar_schema_json.cpp` (else c-subset config fails to load). **FIX 3** — the `int *a, b;` test asserts per-field TYPES distinctly (a=Ptr, b=I32) not just sizeof (==16 is ambiguous). THE ONE SEMANTIC CHANGE — the bitfield resolve search root moved `node`→`dNode` (per-slot) so widths resolve independently; the anonymous path stays from `node`. WITNESS: corpus `struct_multi_member` (`struct P{int *a,b;}; struct Q{int x,y[2],*z;}` write+read each field → exit 42; pe-native + elf/macho/arm64 release arm) + the per-slot/regression/sqlite-repro semantic tests + 445→446 ctest (the new corpus). MINOR pin: `D-CSUBSET-MIXED-NAMED-ANON-BITFIELD`. | `D-CSUBSET-MIXED-NAMED-ANON-BITFIELD` | **OPEN — NAMED LIMITATION, fail-aware (not silent), rare, off the SQLite frontier (p18 Cluster G c23, 2026-06-26).** A struct/union member list that MIXES a NAMED bit-field with a TRAILING ANONYMOUS bit-field in the SAME declaration (`struct S { int a : 3, : 0; };` — `a` named, `: 0` anonymous) drops the trailing anonymous slot: the named slot sets `resolvedNamed = true`, which SKIPS the post-loop anonymous-field path (`semantic_analyzer.cpp` ~2435, gated on `!resolvedNamed`). NOT a silent miscompile in practice: the anonymous zero-width bit-field is a layout PADDING/alignment-break hint; dropping it can only UNDER-pad (a layout difference), and the common single-anonymous and all-named forms are correct. Off the SQLite frontier (sqlite3.c does not use mixed named+trailing-anon bit-fields in one declaration). | `D-CSUBSET-FORWARD-STRUCT-DECLARATION` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-28 (p19 Cluster G c35) — OPAQUE / forward-declared (incomplete) struct types, via REUSE of the c24 incomplete-composite machinery (no new type state).** ON the SQLite path — opaque handles `sqlite3_stmt` / `sqlite3_blob` / … are exactly this pattern (`typedef struct sqlite3_stmt sqlite3_stmt;` at sqlite3.c:4649, used ONLY as `sqlite3_stmt *`); the prior "off the SQLite path" framing was wrong (sqlite3_stmt is a direct counterexample). | `D-CSUBSET-MUTABLE-POINTER-TO-CONST` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-28 (p19 Cluster G c36) — object-const computed from the OUTERMOST pointer layer, not a coarse whole-decl scan.** ROOT (sqlite3.c, ~50× e.g. `zFormat += 4` / `zDate++`): DSS wrongly rejected `const char *p; p += n` with `S_ConstViolation` — `const char *p` is a MUTABLE pointer to const (C 6.7.3: const qualifies the POINTEE; only `char * const p` qualifies the pointer OBJECT). `rec.isConst` was set by `subtreeContainsToken(const)` over the WHOLE declaration, which saw the head/pointee const and wrongly marked the pointer object const. SAME bug c27 fixed for `volatile` — the code comment even said "`isConst` keeps its scan", a deliberate c27 deferral now forced. FIX (single file, agnostic, NOT §B): a new `declaratorObjectIsConst` helper (semantic_analyzer.cpp) — descend the per-slot declarator to its inner declaratorRule, and if it has ≥1 pointer layer, the object is const iff the LAST (outermost, source-order) pointer layer carries the const marker; with NO pointer layer the legacy whole-decl scan applies (scalar / typedef'd-pointer head const). Mirrors the c27 per-layer volatile walk in `declaratorDeclaredType`. Const stays a SYMBOL flag (NOT a type qualifier like c27's `VolatileQual`) because — UNLIKE volatile — const has no per-access codegen effect; the architect's Option-2 (a `ConstQual` lattice type) was rejected as a ~100-site surface buying nothing the helper doesn't. ★ CODEGEN NUANCE (the architect's "no codegen effect" claim was INCOMPLETE — caught + verified): `isConst` DOES thread to `MirGlobal.isConst` → `.rodata`/`.data` global placement (asm.cpp). The fix only ever REMOVES false-const (a `const char *g` global moves .rodata→.data, the SAFE/writable direction — placing a mutable pointer in read-only memory was a latent fault), NEVER the reverse; the string-literal `.rodata` override is unaffected. Sites B (anonymous field — never an assignment LHS) + C (legacy positional — no c-subset constMarker row reaches it) left coarse by design (documented in-code). WITNESS: 12 semantic pins (pointer-to-const param/east/multi-level/multi-declarator/const+volatile CLEAN; const-pointer / const-ptr-to-const / outer-const VIOLATE; east-const scalar still violates) + runtime corpus `const_ptr_walk` (a `const int *p` walks an array via `p++` → 42; RED-ON-DISABLE: pre-c36 `p++` was a spurious S_ConstViolation → would not compile; int ops dodge the deferred sub-32-bit ALU gap, p++ dodges the flagged p+n stride). 457→458 ctest. | (closed — the helper + the Site-A swap IS the fix) | p19 Cluster G c36; builds on c27 `D-CSUBSET-VOLATILE-POINTEE` (the volatile twin + the per-layer walk) + c29 `D-CSUBSET-POST-STAR-CAST-QUALIFIER` (pointerLayer/ptrQualifier); `src/analysis/semantic/semantic_analyzer.cpp` (`declaratorObjectIsConst` + Site A); defers `D-CSUBSET-POINTEE-CONST-ENFORCEMENT` + `D-CSUBSET-GROUPED-DECLARATOR-CONST`; a sqlite3.c re-probe frontier; plan 23 full-C arc / SQLite-green |
| `D-CSUBSET-POINTEE-CONST-ENFORCEMENT` | ⏳ **DEFERRED (surfaced p19 Cluster G c36; the c36 audit broadened it).** The const-violation check (semantic_analyzer.cpp ~4404) only examines a PLAIN-IDENTIFIER LHS, so const enforcement is MISSING for every NON-plain-identifier const lvalue: (i) deref `const char *p; *p='x';` (pointee-const), (ii) member `struct S{const int v;}; s.v=2;`, (iii) array-subscript `const int a[2]; a[0]=5;`. | `D-CSUBSET-GROUPED-DECLARATOR-CONST` | ⏳ **DEFERRED (surfaced p19 Cluster G c36).** c36's `declaratorObjectIsConst` reads the outermost pointer layer that is a DIRECT child of the declarator; a GROUPED pointer declarator `char (* const p)` hides its layer inside the parenthesized group, so it falls through to the legacy whole-decl scan (STATUS QUO — no regression; the coarse scan was used for ALL forms before c36). | `D-CSUBSET-FUNCTION-DESIGNATOR-CAST` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-28 (p19 Cluster G c37) — a function DESIGNATOR cast to a fn-ptr type.** ROOT (sqlite3.c, 29× — `#define SQLITE_DYNAMIC ((sqlite3_destructor_type)sqlite3RowSetClear)`, `(sqlite3_syscall_ptr)posixOpen`): casting a bare function name to a function-pointer type failed error[S0010] S_InvalidCast. C 6.3.2.1p4 + 6.3.2.3p8: a function designator decays to a pointer-to-function, and a fn-ptr may be cast to ANY fn-ptr type (cross-signature included — calling THROUGH an incompatible type is UB, but the CAST is legal + value-preserving = the function's code address). | `D-CSUBSET-POINTER-SUBTRACTION` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-28 (p19 Cluster G c40) — `p - q` is ptrdiff_t (C 6.5.6p9); a COMPILE+RUN-green fix.** ROOT (the biggest remaining sqlite S0003/S_TypeMismatch class, ~50× — `sqlite3StrAppend64(pAccum, bufpt, fmt - bufpt)`, `length = &zOut[nOut-1] - bufpt`): `combineBinary` typed `Ptr<T> - Ptr<T>` as `Ptr<T>` (the "first valid type wins" fallback, since commonArithType returns invalid for non-arith operands) — WRONG. (2) **mismatched-pointee `char* - int*`** in a NON-arg context (`(int)(a-b)`, `long n=a-b`) compiles silently with a raw unscaled Ptr Sub — caught ONLY when the result coerces into a numeric param (an incidental `isAssignable`), never at the subtraction itself. **Trigger:** a consumer (or sqlite re-probe RUN) that hits `p - arrayName` or a mismatched/non-arg pointer difference. **Closing work:** (a) decay an Array operand to Ptr<element> in the subtraction (then c40's same-pointee path handles `p - arr` correctly); (b) when op==Sub and both operands are pointer/array but pointees DIFFER, emit a loud diagnostic at the binary node (not just incidentally in arg context). | `D-CSUBSET-POINTER-ARITH-ENUM-INDEX` | ⏳ **DEFERRED (surfaced by the c65 root-cause + audit, 2026-06-30; guarded fail-loud, NOT a crash).** An ENUM-typed index in pointer arithmetic (`enum E{B=2}; int *p; … *(p + e)` / `p - e`) reaches the MIR `combineBinaryOp` `p±n` index-widen site (`hir_to_mir.cpp:1208`) with TypeKind Enum; `mapCast(Enum, I64)` returns Invalid (its `isInt` excludes Enum) — the SAME unguarded site as the c65 `p - arrayName` crash. c65 added a fail-loud guard there, so this now emits a CLEAN diagnostic ("index TypeKind … has no widening cast … D-CSUBSET-POINTER-ARITH-ENUM-INDEX"), NOT the addInst std::abort. | `D-CSUBSET-INDEX-NEGATIVE-WIDEN` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-28 (p19 Cluster G c42) — a NEGATIVE array subscript `p[-n]` no longer segfaults; a RUN-green MISCOMPILE FIX** (user: include miscompile fixes in the cycles; surfaced by the c41 audit as a PRE-EXISTING crash one path over from c41's p±n). | `D-AS4-ARM64-NEGATIVE-DISP-LEA-NATIVE-SUB` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-07-03 (p19 Cluster G c94) — the arm64 negative-const-disp `lea` now encodes as a NATIVE single-instruction `SUB Xd,Xn,#|disp|` (config + shared matcher + encoder), the c93 base+index FOLD is REMOVED, and the residual DEAD const materialization is GONE (sign-agnostically, for the positive member-offset `ADD` too).** c93 unblocked `p[-1]`/`z[-1]` via a B-gated LIR fold that materialized the negative disp into a fresh GPR (MOVZ/MOVK ladder) + emitted a 4-op base+index `ADD Xd,Xn,Xm` — CORRECT but 5-7 arm64 instructions incl. a 2-insn DEAD const. c94 replaces it with the native SUB, mirroring the positive ADD-imm12 / shifted / MOVZ-MOVK `lea` ladder with the op-bit SET. **(1) The matcher (shared substrate, AGNOSTIC):** a NEW config-driven SIGN axis `negMemoffset` (bool, `guard.negMemoffset`) on `TargetEncodingVariant` — a THIRD routing axis beside width + imm-range. `walker_util.hpp` gains `variantNegMagnitude` (the |value| of a STRICTLY-NEGATIVE value-bearing operand, `-(int64)v` so INT32_MIN widens cleanly); `variantMatchesInst` reads the negative half when `negMemoffset` is set, the non-negative half (existing `variantImmMagnitude`) otherwise — the two axes PARTITION the signed value line. x86's disp32 lea slot has no immMin/immMax AND no negMemoffset ⇒ its match-any slot swallows BOTH signs in ONE `lea [base±disp32]` — COMPLETELY UNCHANGED (byte-pinned, see witnesses). `validate()` gains negMemoffset as a disambiguator (variants differing in negMemoffset route on disjoint sign domains, never a shadow) + a coherence reject (negMemoffset needs a `memoffset` operand). **(2) The config:** 3 arm64 `lea` negMemoffset variants — single-word `SUB Xd,Xn,#|disp|` (0xD1000000, |disp|≤4095), shifted word-pair `[0xD1000000, 0xD1400000]` (|disp| 4096..0xFFFFFF), and MOVZ/MOVK + EXTENDED-register `SUB Xd,Xn,Xd` 3-word `[0xD2800000, 0xF2A00000, 0xCB206000]` (|disp| >16MiB, Rn WIRED to the base not baked-sp). All SUB encodings re-derived from the ARM ARM (add/subtract-immediate + extended-register) + verified vs the existing `sub` opcode's fixedWords + aarch64-gcc objdump. **(3) The encoder (fixed32.cpp):** the MemOffset arm computes `effectiveDisp` = |disp| when `selected->negMemoffset` (fail-loud on a non-negative disp on a SUB variant — the sign matcher should have excluded it) and feeds the SAME Imm12 / Imm12HiLo24 / Imm32MovzMovk slots (no new EncodingSlotKind — the bit-windows are identical; the SUB base word makes it a subtract). **(4) The c93 fold REMOVED:** `lowerGep`'s const-disp arm emits the plain 3-op `lea [base + MemOffset(disp)]` for EVERY disp on EVERY target; `targetHasSignedDispLea()` DELETED (unused). x86 takes its signed disp32, arm64 the native SUB — target-blind. **(5) The DEAD const eliminated (sign-agnostic):** a NEW `foldedConstDisps_` set + `constDispFoldsIntoGep` predicate (mirroring the `foldedGlobalAddrs_` fold-skip precedent) — a single-use integer Const whose sole user is a 2-operand const-disp Gep (the disp operand, fits int32) is NOT materialized by `lowerConst` (`lowerGep` reads it via `constIntegerValue`, never `regForValue`; a stray `regForValue` fails loud on the undefined vreg). This removed the pre-existing dead-const on BOTH the negative `SUB` AND the positive member-offset `ADD` (objdump-confirmed: `mov #0xFFF..` count 0 in the arm64 release binary; `mov #0x4` gone before the positive `add x28,x28,#0x4`). | `D-CSUBSET-FAM-IN-UNION-MEMBER` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-07-03 (p19 Cluster G c99; NOT §B — C99 + gcc/clang give one answer) — a flexible-array-member-bearing struct is a legal DIRECT member of a UNION.** ROOT (the c99 re-probe's live blocker, the 3× `error[S001D]` = `S_FlexibleArrayInAggregate` in **sqlite3.c**, NOT shell.c): sqlite's `union { SrcList sSrc; u8 srcSpace[SZ_SRCLIST_1]; } uSrc;` (sqlite3.c:111815/158387/165978 — a stack-allocated slab that backs a "fake" one-entry SrcList; `SrcList` = `struct{int nSrc; u32 nAlloc; SrcItem a[FLEXARRAY];}`, a true C99 FAM struct). FIX (NOT §B; narrow, target-agnostic): the `typeContainsFlexibleArray` branch (semantic_analyzer.cpp:3600) gates the S001D emit on `permittedAsUnionMember = (ck==Union)` — a FAM-struct member of a UNION is permitted; a FAM-struct as a STRUCT member (ck Struct) STAYS fail-loud AT this branch. (The independent audit + review established that `ft` reaching this branch is ALWAYS a FAM-struct — `typeContainsFlexibleArray` doesn't recurse into unions, and an array-of-FAM member is InvalidType'd UPSTREAM at applyArraySuffix ~1630/1972 — so the once-proposed `&& in.kind(ft)==Struct` was a TAUTOLOGY that would additionally OVER-REJECT the p18-legal `union{union V v}` under any future recursion change; DROPPED. The gate is purely union-vs-struct.) An array-of-FAM-struct union member STAYS fail-loud upstream (still S001D — p18 "element of an array"); the nested `union{union V v}` form is ACCEPTED (gcc-parity, audit-verified). Matches gcc's pedantic-warn/reject posture + DSS's pre-existing FC6 stance. LAYOUT (no change needed — the real risk, verified clean): `computeLayout`'s Union arm already sizes to `max(member sizes)` and `computeLayout(FAM-struct)` already returns the non-flexible PREFIX size with `hasFlexibleArrayMember=true` (the FAM tail is 0-length for sizeof), so `sizeof(union{SrcList; u8[N]})==max(prefix,N)` — matches gcc (`sizeof(SrcList)==4`, `sizeof(union)==16`). ★ THE RE-PROBE (2-TU sqlite, current master `a20de6d683`): the 3× S001D CLEARED → **x86_64:elf64 + arm64:elf64 compile the `sqlite3` binary CLEAN (0 errors), and RUN SQL: `SELECT sum→42` + `--version→3.54.0` on x86_64-native + qemu-arm64** — the chase-master run-green legs are restored. | `D-MIR-VERIFIER-UNBOUNDED-OPERAND-SENTINEL` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-30 (p19 Cluster G c70) — the MIR verifier honors the variadic-operand sentinel (`maxOperands == kMirUnboundedOperands == 0xFF`) instead of reading it as a literal max of 255.** ROOT (the c69 re-probe's FIRST error, after sqlite3.c finally compiled end-to-end): `I_VerifierFailure` "opcode switch operand count 349 outside [1, 255]" — the c60 switch-flatten produces ONE MIR `Switch` opcode whose operands are `[discriminant, caseValue*N]`; sqlite's ~348-case VDBE dispatch (`sqlite3VdbeExec`) = 349 operands. `MirOpcode::Switch` (and `IndirectBr`) declare `maxOperands == kMirUnboundedOperands` (0xFF) — genuinely variadic — and the BUILDER (`mir.cpp` addInst) has always exempted that sentinel from the upper-bound check (`maxOperands != kMirUnboundedOperands && count > maxOperands`), so it accepted the 349-operand Switch. FIX (1 edit, `src/mir/mir_verifier.cpp`): mirror the builder's exemption — `bool const overMax = info.maxOperands != kMirUnboundedOperands && operands.size() > info.maxOperands;` — so a variadic-operand opcode is not upper-bounded. | `D-CSUBSET-CONTINUE-SKIPS-SWITCH` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-30 (p19 Cluster G c61) — `continue` inside a `switch` inside a loop targets the enclosing LOOP, not the switch (C 6.8.6.2).** ROOT (the c60 re-probe's FIRST error, H0002 H_InvalidBreak ×2): sqlite `sqlite3VXPrintf` (sqlite3.c:33119/33311) — a format-char loop whose body `switch`es on the conversion type, with `continue` inside the switch to advance the format string → "continue resolves to a switch; continue can only target a loop". `isBranchTargetKind` (hir_node.hpp:163) counts a SwitchStmt as a branch target, and a `continue`'s depth-0 resolution (makeContinue(0) — C has no labeled continue) landed on the innermost switch → the verifier (hir_verifier.cpp:193) rejected it. The verifier's loops-only view and the MIR's skip-invalid-continueBB walk drop the IDENTICAL frames (a SwitchStmt HIR node ⟺ a MIR frame with invalid continueBB), both depth 0 = innermost loop → consistent by construction. | `D-CSUBSET-ARRAY-DECAY-AT-CALL-ARG` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-30 (p19 Cluster G c63; NOT §B) — an ARRAY used as an rvalue / call argument decays to a pointer to its first element (C 6.3.2.1p3).** ROOT (surfaced by c63's first audit as a SILENT SysV SIGSEGV): a SysV `va_list` (`__va_list_tag[1]`, an Array) FORWARDED as a call arg (`vsum(n, ap)`) must decay to `&ap[0]`, but `lowerExpr(Ref(array))`'s addressableLocal arm emitted `Load(slot, Array)` = the tag's FIRST WORD (the gp_offset/fp_offset int) → the callee dereferenced garbage → SIGSEGV. Cannot mis-fire: every other array-rvalue context carries an explicit Cast (→ lowerLvalueAddress); only a bare same-type array call arg reaches this arm. | `D-MIR-ENTRY-BLOCK-ALLOCA-HOIST` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-30 (p19 Cluster G c69; NOT §B) — every body-local's storage `Alloca` is pre-emitted into the function ENTRY block (which dominates all uses), not at its decl site.** ROOT: a local DECLARED in an entry-unreachable block (the canonical case: a decl before the first `case` of a `switch`, which the c60 switch-flatten places in a predecessor-less pre-case block) had its `Alloca` emitted into that dead block; the mandatory unreachable-prune (`D-MIR-UNREACHABLE-PRUNE-NORMALIZE`) then dropped the block while a reachable case body still Load/Stored the slot → the `MirFunctionRebuilder` rewrite-map completeness abort (`D-OPT2-REWRITE-MAP-COMPLETENESS`), a SIGABRT compiler crash. FIX (`src/mir/lowering/hir_to_mir.cpp`): `lowerFunction` runs a `collectLocalDecls` pre-pass that emits each local's slot into the (still-open) entry block before lowering the body; the VarDecl site reuses the pre-emitted slot. | `D-AS4-ARM64-LARGE-DISP-LEA-BASE-CLOBBER` | ⏳ **DEFERRED (surfaced + confirmed PRE-EXISTING by the c69 audit, 2026-06-30; NOT introduced by c69).** An arm64 `lea result,[base+disp]` with a displacement > 16 MiB (> 0xFFFFFF) lowers to a `MOVZ Xd; MOVK Xd; ADD Xd, base, Xd` macro that CLOBBERS `base` when regalloc coalesces the base vreg into the result (base == Xd == result). c69's alloca-address rematerialization ([[D-CSUBSET-ALLOCA-ADDRESS-REMATERIALIZE]]) EXPOSED it on `large_frame_beyond_16mib` (a > 16 MiB frame slot) → SIGSEGV on arm64-qemu under the optimized pipeline; FIXED for the alloca-base case by folding a constant-offset alloca Gep into one `lea [sp + slotOff + disp]` (base = sp, the reserved frame register, never the clobberable result). RESIDUAL: a NON-frame `p + hugeConst` (> 16 MiB constant added to a DERIVED pointer whose vreg coalesces with the result) still hits the general Gep lea path, which c69 does NOT touch (audit-verified: no makeMemOffset/emitInst(Lea) added there; alloca bases are routed away first). PRE-EXISTING, c69-INDEPENDENT, astronomically rare, NO sqlite relevance. | `D-CSUBSET-ALLOCA-ADDRESS-REMATERIALIZE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-30 (p19 Cluster G c69; NOT §B) — a body-local alloca's ADDRESS is rematerialized at each use (a fresh `lea_frame_slot` per use) instead of held in one entry-spanning vreg.** ROOT (un-masked by the c69 entry-block alloca-hoist above): hoisting every alloca to entry makes its address-value live from entry; reusing ONE address vreg across that range tips a register-pressure cliff (`examples/c-subset/index_negative`'s `main` takes addresses of locals → `R_SpilledDueToPressure` + `L_VirtualRegInPostRegalloc` scratch-pool exhaustion at the rewrite stage). FIX (the conventional "rematerialize frame addresses" treatment; `src/lir/lowering/mir_to_lir.cpp` + `src/lir/lir_callconv.cpp` + both target JSONs): MIR→LIR emits the `alloca` op ONCE (it reserves the slot, in scan order) and, at each use of the address (`regForValue` chokepoint), a fresh `lea_frame_slot k` (k = the alloca's 0-based scan-order index, on the payload) whose result has a tiny def→use range; lir_callconv materializes each `lea_frame_slot k` into `lea [sp + offsetOf(k)]` — byte-identical to the original alloca's `lea` (offset from the alloca-index→offset map it builds in scan order, asserted congruent with the alloca arm's running offset). The new `lea_frame_slot` virtual op is DISTINCT from `alloca` so the frame-layout slot-count scan is unchanged (exactly ONE slot per original alloca). A CONSTANT-offset Gep whose base IS an alloca (`&local[constIdx]`/`&s.field`) FOLDS its displacement into ONE sp-based `lea [sp + slotOff + disp]` (via an optional ImmInt operand on `lea_frame_slot`) — cheaper (one lea) AND load-bearing on arm64: without the fold, a >16 MiB `disp` in the un-folded `lea_frame_slot` base + `lea [base+disp]` pair lowers to the arm64 MOVZ/MOVK macro `ADD Xd,base,Xd` which clobbers `base` when regalloc coalesces the tiny-range remat base into the Gep result (base==Xd → SIGSEGV, `examples/c-subset/large_frame_beyond_16mib` under the full-release-like pipeline); folding makes the base `sp` (never the result), so the macro is safe. Corpora `examples/c-subset/index_negative` (→42; RED-ON-DISABLE → the scratch-pool exhaustion compile error) + `large_frame_beyond_16mib` (→42 on arm64-qemu; the const-disp fold is what keeps it green under remat). Verified RUN-green on all 3 legs (Win pe compile + WSL x86_64-elf + arm64-qemu). |

| `D-CSUBSET-COMPOUND-ASSIGN-VALUE-PROMOTION` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-07-01 (p19 Cluster G c74; NOT §B) — a compound assignment on a SUB-INT lvalue used in VALUE/expression position integer-PROMOTES the base op to int (C99 `a OP= b` == `a = (T)((a) OP (b))`).** ROOT (the post-c73 re-probe STILL showed the SAME 2 U8 [ordinal 6] `<deferred>` ALU errors — c73 [[D-CSUBSET-BITFIELD-SUBINT-PROMOTION]] fixed u8 BIT-FIELDS, a REAL gap, but NOT sqlite's actual construct; ★ PROCESS MISS — inferred bit-fields from a probe instead of confirming sqlite's site, the re-probe is ground truth): I INSTRUMENTED the LIR ALU gate (mir_to_lir.cpp ~949, print `op#{int(op)} func# operand-ordinals`), compiled sqlite3.c once → **op#18 [=And] operands (U8,I32) → U8** = a compound bitwise-assign on a sub-int lvalue used in VALUE position (`if( (p->flags &= ~MASK) )`, `while((c|=b))`, `return (x&=y)`). c71/c72/c73 promoted the condition/++--/unary/bit-field sites, and the STATEMENT-position compound assign (`x &= y;`) already promoted via `lowerCompoundAssign` (my earlier probes used the statement form — which is why I missed the value form). But a VALUE-position compound assign lowers through TWO OTHER paths — the `lowerExpr` work-stack driver's `finishAssign` (cst_to_hir.cpp:1721, PRIMARY) + the `lowerBinary` Assign arm (~2600, recursive fallback) — both of which built `compoundLhsRead OP rhs` at the LVALUE type with UN-promoted operands → the sub-int ALU op → the gate. FIX (both paths, mirroring `lowerCompoundAssign`): `common = commonArithType(lhs,rhs)` (i32 for sub-int); coerce BOTH operands to `common` + build the BinaryOp at `common`; then `stored = (common != lv.type) ? coerce(opResult, lv.type) : opResult` (narrow back; the store+re-read yield the TRUNCATED value = C's compound-assign value). A NON-arithmetic common (Ptr compound `p += n`, common Invalid) keeps opType==lv.type → the c41 stride-Gep, BYTE-IDENTICAL. Promote-casts are pure conversions → the read-before-rhs value-position order holds. WITNESS: corpus `compound_assign_value_promotion` (`(x&=0x0F)`=15 + `(y<<=2)`=20 + `((z&=0x0F)==0)`+3 + `(w|=2)`=3 + `((s+=9)==1)`+1 [signed char] → 42; the yielded value is the STORED/TRUNCATED value so observables are low-byte [signedness-agnostic or explicit signed char], gcc-agreeing x86+aarch64; RED-ON-DISABLE → the ordinal-6/1 wall). 3-leg gate Win 504/504 + WSL/qemu 319/319 (ZERO regression — this value-position path change is GLOBAL but int/pointer/float/statement compound assigns all pass); gcc-cross-check 42 x86(signed char)+aarch64(unsigned char). ★★ INDEPENDENT AUDIT (worktree — truncated-yield property + no-regression on int/pointer/float compound + single-eval + red-on-disable): **SOUND** — 52 single-observable per-case programs (every op `&= |= ^= <<= >>= += -= *= /= %=` × u8/u16/s8/s16/char, operands chosen so the TRUNCATED stored value ≠ the promoted i32: `(u8 0x40)<<=2`→0 not 256, `(u8 0x10)*=0x11`→16 not 272, `(s8 100)+=100`→−56, `(u16 0x4000)<<=2`→0, plus mixed-sub-int + wider-rhs [common i64]) ALL match gcc on 8 legs (x86 signed-char + aarch64 UNSIGNED-char, O0/O2) — ZERO mismatch; STRUCTURAL: the yield is a fresh `lvRead` of the sub-int slot AFTER the store → by construction the truncated value, NEVER the promoted i32; the conditional narrow ≡ the untouched path's unconditional `coerce` (identity no-op to same type, cst_to_hir.cpp:331; `TypeId::==` on `.v`); the pointer path BYTE-IDENTICAL (`commonArithType` Invalid for Ptr → opType==lv.type → c41 stride-Gep, objdump-confirmed `int* p+=2` scales ×4 both arches); single-eval preserved (`a[i++]+=1`/`*p++&=m`/rhs-once = 204 everywhere). Red-on-disable = the exact ordinal-6 (`<deferred>` U8) + ordinal-1 (Add I8) wall. 319/319 WSL c-subset + HIR/MIR golden/lowering units (toy/tsql/generic/multi_lang byte-neutral). ★ PRE-EXISTING NON-c74 (deferred [[D-CSUBSET-BOOL-COMPOUND-ASSIGN]]): `_Bool b; b|=5`/`b+=3` fails S0003 in BOTH the untouched statement path (`lowerCompoundAssign`) AND value position → NOT a c74 regression (fails identically before/after); unlikely a sqlite blocker (sqlite uses u8/int not `_Bool`) → re-probe is ground truth. | (closed — the finishAssign + lowerBinary value-position compound-assign promotion, mirroring lowerCompoundAssign) | p19 Cluster G c74; the TRUE post-c73 blocker; the value-position member of the [[D-CSUBSET-32BIT-ALU-FORMS]] family (siblings c71/c72/c73); `src/hir/lowering/cst_to_hir.cpp` (finishAssign + lowerBinary Assign arm); a sqlite re-probe frontier; plan 23 full-C arc / SQLite-green |

| `D-FF3-SYSV-MIXED-CLASS-STACK-OVERFLOW-OFFSET` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-07-01 (p19 Cluster G c76; USER Option 2) — FIXED: the CALLEE-side incoming overflow-arg offset now follows a monotonic class-SHARED byte cursor (`incomingStackArgByteOffset` in lir_callconv materializeOneFunc) mirroring the caller's overflowIdx, so a GPR-overflow and an FP-overflow arg occupy DISTINCT source-order slots (repro=73 not 64); slot-aligned CCs (Win64) get a congruence assertion. The independent per-class overflow counters (GPR-overflow-index, FP-overflow-index) must EACH advance the SHARED incoming-stack cursor, not each restart at 0. WITNESS (CONFIRMED on build-rel): the repro → **DSS x86-elf SysV = 64; gcc -O0/-O2 = 73; arm64 AAPCS64 = 73; Win64 ms_x64 = 73** (only SysV wrong — AAPCS64 + ms_x64 slot-align, so no collision). | `D-RUNTIME-MAIN-ARGC-ARGV` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-07-02 (p19 Cluster G c88) — the ELF program entry materializes argc/argv for `int main(int argc, char** argv)` via a NEW config-driven `processArgs` format block; the pe64 leg split off as [[D-RUNTIME-PE-MAIN-ARGS]] (a genuinely different mechanism).** ROOT (registered by c76 corpus agent a62343ea, CONFIRMED all 3 targets: no-args argc read pe64=1801535488 / x86-elf=224 / arm64-qemu=80, all garbage; became THE sqlite RUN frontier at c87 — the 2-TU sqlite3 loaded clean [188/188 binds] then crashed INSIDE shell.c's `main(argc,argv)` on garbage argc=846361312: SIGSEGV(139) / glibc malloc.c:2599 sysmalloc assert+SIGABRT(134), no output, while gcc on the SAME bld-dss sources answered 42/3.54.0): the entry trampoline called main WITHOUT setting the argument registers — on SysV x86_64 / AAPCS64 Linux the kernel leaves argc + the in-place NULL-terminated argv vector ON THE INITIAL STACK ([sp]=argc, sp+8=argv[0]…) and the registers hold loader garbage. Registers come from `entryCallingConvention.argGprs[0..1]` (single source of truth); ZERO if(arch)/if(os) in the emitter — both ISAs ride the SAME 3-op LIR shapes through `assemble()`. SIGNATURE-INDEPENDENT: `main(void)` ignores the two registers (C-legal) — the whole corpus is unaffected (Win 545→546 green incl. every main(void) example). Mach-O declares NO block — LC_MAIN entry is CALLED by dyld with argc/argv ALREADY in the argument registers (pass-through is the correct mechanism; untestable locally, no darwin run leg); pe64 declares NO block — the Windows OS entry receives NO C argument vector at all (msvcrt `__getmainargs` out-parameter route = [[D-RUNTIME-PE-MAIN-ARGS]], the Windows-leg cycle; pe main(void) unchanged-green meanwhile). envp NOT materialized (c-subset main is `(int,char**)`; libc `environ` serves programs that need it). | `D-RUNTIME-PE-MAIN-ARGS` | ★ USER §B DECISION (2026-07-04, c111): chose the **synthesized pre-main INIT FUNCTION** hosting (option B — a compiler-generated function in ordinary MIR/LIR where stack locals + calls are FREE via the normal callconv pass, NOT hand-built trampoline RSP math) with the **msvcrt `__wgetmainargs`** CRT route (dumpbin-verified export ord 168; the WIDE form — shell.c's MSVC entry is `wmain(int,wchar_t**)`; already importing msvcrt, no new import library). | `D-LK-OBJECT-EXTERN-SYMBOL-NAMES` | 🔴 **OPEN (discovered 2026-07-07, SQLite codegen-validation session).** DSS relocatable-object emission (the non-`-exec` format `elf64-x86_64-linux`) writes externally-visible GLOBAL FUNC symbols into `.symtab` under DSS's INTERNAL numeric IDs (`sym_8`, `sym_10`, ...) instead of the source-level C identifier names (`foo`, `bar`). The object is otherwise structurally valid (`file` -> `ELF 64-bit LSB relocatable, x86-64`, Type `REL`; `readelf -s` -> binding/type correct `GLOBAL`/`FUNC`, `Ndx=.text`), so DSS's own linker resolves intra-DSS references and the `-exec` legs + the `sqlite3` executable build+run cleanly — the gap is INVISIBLE to intra-DSS linking. It only bites CROSS-TOOLCHAIN object interop: `gcc main.c dss.o` -> `ld: undefined reference to 'foo'/'bar'` (C names absent from `.symtab`). VERIFIED via `nm dss.o` (-> `T sym_8` / `T sym_10`) + `readelf -s` + the failing gcc link. Secondary ELF interop nit, same run: DSS objects omit `.note.GNU-stack` -> `ld` warns 'missing .note.GNU-stack implies executable stack'. Likely also latent in PE/macho object output (the internal-ID naming appears to live in the shared symbol layer — verify per-format on close). **Impact:** blocks linking a DSS-compiled object into a foreign-toolchain image — specifically the DEFINITIVE SQLite validation: building `testfixture` (gcc + `libtcl`) against a DSS-compiled `sqlite3.o` to run SQLite's own 1,190-file TCL suite against DSS codegen (all prereqs present on the WSL box: 1,190 `.test`, 44 `src/test*.c`, `tclsh` 8.6.14, `tcl.h`). Until closed, DSS codegen is validated by DIFFERENTIAL testing vs gcc on the SAME amalgamation (2026-07-07: 107 statements across 2 corpora byte-identical incl. FP->text 17-sig-fig + 100k-iter recursion; 0 miscompiles) — strong, but not the official suite. **Trigger:** fires when any real consumer needs a DSS object consumed by an external linker (the testfixture/TCL-suite route, or shipping a DSS `.o`/static lib for foreign linkage). | Carry the source-level C identifier name into `.symtab` `st_name` for every externally-visible (non-`static`) symbol in relocatable-object output — thread the real name through the shared symbol layer for the object emitter, not just the internal `sym_N` ID (static/local symbols may stay internal).
